The other way to make a cautery is that you heat the cautery with two nerves, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and remove the pus that is near the mouse, or the sore where the patient's bladder comes from on the left side, and lift the incisions according to the direction of the bladder, according to the length of the body, and the cautery should be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	 After putting the two inflamed nerves on fire until the boils are pierced from the other side, then draw out the cautery, and thus you will have four. If you see, cauterize the entire cautery at three places.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	 After purging for a long time, it is worth trying the other treatments mentioned earlier.
de ydropisie	of hydropisy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	 Cauterization does not work against dropsy, except in the manner known as "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	 If the cure according to the methods we have described in the divisions does not work and has no effect, then you should make four cauteries around the body, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the spleen, and two behind the back near the spine, at the worst place; and ensure that the cauteries are close to the affected area.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After letting the fire cautery heal for a long time, do not neglect the care of the patient after the cautery; healing would hasten and the two intentions will be combined with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery for the belly is the claw as we have shown before; and for the back it is olive-shaped, according to what was mentioned above.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	 When the feet are swollen in one who is edematous, and filled with citrine liquid, you should cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and ring finger; and lower your hand with the cautery without turning it.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	 And do not enter too deeply, so as not to burn the citrine liquid excessively; and make the cautery in this shape:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After making two cauteries in each leg at the tip of the index finger; and let the cauteries be long, one below the knee in front and another outside the leg; and leave the cauteries above for a while to heal, so that the water drains out; afterwards cure the other wounds as we have said.
de la menoison	of the swelling
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When the swelling of the belly comes from cold and moisture, while the digestive and retentive qualities that are in the stomach and intestine are inhibited, and it cannot be cured by means of treatment; and you see the patient suffering greatly and having strong symptoms, then do this: make one large cautery on the stomach as mentioned before (cautere of the stomach), or cauterize around the belly, in a circular manner; and four subtle cauteries around the navel, one subtle cautery at the clavicle, and two cauteries on the flanks.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see excessive moisture and the patient suffering, do a cautery on the elbow, one on each arm, and two small cauteries on the stomach, near the large one, for the treatment is beneficial when aid is available.
de la cure des emorroydes	Treatment of hemorrhoids:
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	 When the hemorrhoids are founded or multiple, and are old and are of thick, cold, and corrupted humors, and have been cured as we have said in divisions, and it does not help if you apply cauteries: III on the spine of the back, which is completely displaced from almecdate poc and poc in triangulating, and the cautery should be beneath the buttocks II times; and if you think that his stomach is cooled, and the meat does not cook, and you see the face swell, then the face gets a large cautery on the stomach as it has been said before, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen with all the cautery nails; and leave the cautery open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After curing the limb when it is healthy.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut an artery, take the fire-cautery that appears like a razor and then burn it all over the artery you are cutting; leave your hand there so the tip of the cautery comes to the vein opening, from which the blood flows; do this once or twice, and if there is much blood, cauterize each time as we have said; afterwards, treat with healing herbs until they heal completely; and if you cauterize a large area with a large fire-cautery, it will provide more help.
de plaie mal curee	of an unhealed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When a patient cannot endure such large incision or opening, as we shall explain in its place, comes the sickness that can only be healed by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	 For any boil that becomes pustular and is filled with impurities and corrupt matter, you must probe it entirely with a delicate test, and be sure to know the extent of the abscess fully.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	 After heating the cautery that appears like a razor, insert it into the abscess according to the size that the abscess is filled, and continue the cauterization until the body burns and decays, once or twice, depending on the amount of pus needed; be careful not to burn the nerves that are nearby, nor the large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	 If the abscess goes to the body of the bladder or intestine, beware of these organs and do not do anything outside of charnut (a medicinal preparation), and think that it is not perforated; after curing the limb when it is healthy, if the limbs are pierced and matter has been removed for a long time, know that the limbs are healed completely; and if the matter is not removed, know that the limbs are broken, and the bones are corrupted in this way, like one of those we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain in the flank comes with large swelling and does not take on female form, then it is necessary that you make a cautery over the kidneys from both sides using the cautery claw as we have said before; and if we cauterize it in the middle, there will be 4 cauteries in a line, and they will provide more help.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder becomes soft and weak from cold or moisture, causing the patient to retain urine, then make a fire cautery in the area outside the bladder, where the pubic hair begins, one on the right side and one on the left, each cautery should be as long as a thumb; and make one cautery behind the back, if necessary; and make the cauteries incisions like the shape previously described.
de la marris	of the anus
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the matrix is cold and moist, and does not permit conception, and the flowers are corrupted and their term ends late; and when they come, then it causes great pain: then you must make four cauteries around the womb, as we have said, or cautery of the bladder, and two cauteries behind the back; and let the cauterization be with a hot iron, as we have said.
de la hainche	The pustule
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When viscous moistures flow towards the abscess of the pustule and cause it to move from its place, the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the location of the source can be found by sight. If you need to cauterize the patient over the abscess of the pustule at one cautery resembling a circle, with the sign pointing before the place around the abscess as it turns, so that the abscess is within the circle; and let the cauterization be similar to that used for the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this fire cautery is not present for you, make 4 large olive-oil cauterizations instead, and let them be as deep as all the others; and heal it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain from the hernia
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain occurs in the hernia bag, it is due to coldness and moisture; the sick are healed with what we have said above in the division, but the cure does not work, and the disease is ancient: then it is necessary that you purge the sick person from the gross humors using fetid pills or other good-seeming pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	 Afterwards, make the cautery; and the method of the cautery is according to two ways: namely with burning substances, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	 Fire cautery is according to many ways, one of which is this: you should apply three triangular cauteries together on the boil of the hernia in such a way, with good depth and width, with space between each cauterization as thick as a thumb, and the cauteries should be olive-shaped; sometimes cauterization is done in the middle on top of the hernia's head, for which there are four as in this shape:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you wish, if you cauterize with the circular cautery that we have mentioned in the dislocation of the haunch, but do it in such a way that the circles encompass the entire haunch, and all the edges should be burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	 And this is the method used in sciatica, when pain persists in the loin and does not reach as far as the thigh nor the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	 If the pain reaches as far as the thigh and the leg, perform II cauteries at the location where the patient says that the pain is present, and the cautery should be placed 4 fingers above the ankle on the left side; and may it be a cautery knife, and may the coagulating substance of charcoal be applied; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the foot or near there, cauterize at the location where they feel the pain 3 or 4 fingers away from the pain point which is called "poins".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, do more; and if the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, perform a fire cautery using either a knife or circular device, and be careful in all your cauteries not to leave the cautery on too long so as not to burn the nerves and large arteries, and not to cause the patient greater harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	 And I myself have seen more who made a fire cautery on the heel of the foot, and they let it fester until the leg was completely swollen, and the toes also, and all the toes were pierced and corrupted.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	 After a stomach solution in which he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	 And if the pain is in two parts together, make a fire cautery in one and the other, according to this method.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	 And the wise shall say in the cautery of the ankle, as follows, make the iron thus and let it be as thick as a nail of the thumb, or a little less, and be interwoven or interwoven from one to the other at a distance equal to the size of a nut of the fist; and let the interwoven parts be above two fingers, and let them also be like nuts, and have the ankle iron well made; and this is its form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be scalded until it is all red and boils, and then put it on top of the sick man's haunch, and turn it over to the healthy side; and cauterize once with a fire cautery, and leave it for four days; then make a plaster of butter, and keep the wound open for a long time; afterwards, cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use this cautery sparingly due to fear of its appearance and not many who use it; but this is a good cautery for those who can bear it, and where it should be applied.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	 The instrument for burning medicine is that you make it in the form of a cross within which the edge of the opening should be beveled, and it should be made of iron or steel long enough, and at the top it should have two openings, and between each there should be the size of a thumb's thickness; and they should be overlaid and joined together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	 After placing the hot iron tool on the patient lying on one side, and then your hand slightly above the hot iron tool; after that pour the two circles of hot liquid into the opening in the tool which has been heated in the fire pot, and leave it for an hour, and let the patient suffer the heat and burning from it.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the bite or burn heals, take your hand with the instrument and gently lift the scab, then leave it for three days, and apply butter until the blackness from the burn is removed; and let it stay for three more days so that pus can drain out; and this will be the final help after the treatment of ointments until it heals.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	 If the pain extends to the thigh or leg, make the instrument that stains according to what you have done with the scab, and this is the method of hot water, and I have written it or treated it under the correction of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	 Take lime (alum) and hot charcoal, an equal amount of each, grind them together and put in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	 Have a small hole pierced so that the tip of a razor can enter; and pour from one pot into another well-sealed pot, and add lime (alum) and charcoal with a sweetener on top until there are two layers of powder over which you have firmly grasped your hand; leave it like this until it cools and solidifies or the pot seals, then take all that has settled, and pour it over charcoal and lime as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	 And when it is cooled and administered in the work of various medical procedures and cauteries for other members, as it does a similar job as fire, it is mixed with other medicines that are used to cauterize an ulcer in this manner, such as wax, honey, cardamom, charcoal, and soap, all mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	 And Galen tells us of a cure from which one nobleman was healed of the pain of the hernia and sciatica, and praised it greatly, and said that no other treatment was applied to it, and that it became healthy at once when this treatment was carried out, and he was bathed as instructed below.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	 And it is said that you should take fresh green litharge and grind it well with a small amount of fat, and apply it to the hernia, to the thigh and to the leg where the pain occurs, and hold it; leave it for three hours until the patient no longer feels the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	 And then make him enter or bathe until the body is slightly warmed up, and put him to bed, and the pain will leave completely and it will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	 And know that no one should use such fire cautery, unless after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	 And Dyascorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's fat, it helps greatly; and the cautery should be done in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	 Take the linen and beat it with old oil, then place it on the furrow between the little toe of the foot and the one called foscile.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	 After that, take dry goat's fat and heat it until it becomes charcoal, then put it on the linen and leave it until it turns black; repeat this process again and again until you believe, by your senses, that it has reached the hilt, and that the pain has stopped; and this method of cautery is called "cautere de chievre".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain in the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from falling or from striking or from excessive evacuation, or from similar causes of cold matter, none of these similar causes are worth cauterization, unless it is caused by the influx of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after this that the patient be bled of fetid pills or similar, and make it on the back where the pain is located, three inches marked with incisions, and in each line five or more cauterizations according to the power and quantity that the patient can bear; and the cauterization should be made according to the cautery called "poins"; and if you see, do four cauterizations or four on the cautery called "clavile moien" in this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes to small children, and the signs of its onset are that they have a narrowed anus when they defecate, and fear; you can find it in the lower spine of the back and in the appearance that appears above the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this [object] and wish to cure it, if necessary, use the fire cautery in this manner.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	 The cautery increases every part of the spine.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	 If you wish, cauterize around the spine with the cautery pointing two or three lines and the tips close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	 After curing the limb until it is healed according to what we have said, be careful not to apply cautery in a gilbositeit (a swelling or inflammation) that may be in a nerve of the spine.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain in the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain in the joints is from swelling affecting every member of the body, and when pain comes in the feet, which are called "podagre" properly, and it is caused by coldness and medicine cannot cure it, it is cured by cauteries in this manner: make the patient prepare a cautery around the joint of the foot, and the cautery should be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	 And if it is necessary to prick on the face of the foot, make the cautery with a point all over.
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	 And if the pain comes to the knees and other joints, which happens often, make the cautery over each knee three or four times on every side with an olive-shaped cautery; and if you need more, do more, but do not hold your hand away from the heat of the coal for too long.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	 And if the pains descend to the knees and the back, administer the cautery as we have said in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	 And if the pains are in the hands, do point-pricking twice on the fingers; and if there remains no pain at the wrist, do point-pricking above each joint and above the hair of the hand; and if the pains come down to the elbows or up to the shoulders, cauterize each part, give good care to the patient, consider medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	 For if you give good care and purge him with bile, he will be healed by God's aid.
de la routure dou syfac	of the breaking of the vein
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the hernia comes in anguish, and the bulge descends into the groin and this happens suddenly, if you want to treat it, you must not let him eat anything that day; you should use things that relax the abdomen so the stool passes from his stomach. Afterwards have him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to cling to his loins as tightly as possible until the bulge has receded, then press it to your sides, and apply pressure on top of the hernia above the joint of the little finger, and at every sign that is similar to half a circle on the chest. Then heat the cautery in the shape that is shown here:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	 until it is white and exudes pus.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	 Then pull the muscles to their place; and the assistants hold the patient's limb so it does not return; and work well on the thigh of the patient, put the cushion and the sergeant under him on the thighs, and the other one holds the hands; then place the cautery on the affected area with your entire hand, hold it straight and keep it there until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, try again until you reach the bone; be careful that the boil does not burst when you perform the cauterization; that you do not burn it; and so that the patient does not die or suffer any other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	 And know that if you do not reach the bone with the cauterization, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	 And the cauterizations for children should be subtle according to their size, and for big people also big according to their measurement; after three days heal the wound from the cautery with butter until the burn is healed; afterwards heal it with other medicaments until it becomes healthy, and make the patient lie down on his back for forty days while the wound heals well; and it is necessary that his urine is allowed to flow freely, so that the scabs do not appear when he is about to go into rooms.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	 After forty days, when he wants to get up, bring him a well-made bedsheet and leave it for forty other days; let him rest well, so that he does not exert himself too much, nor drink too much, eat too much or cough too much; and if he follows these instructions, he will be completely healthy.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	 And I shall say afterwards the treatment of amputation in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the cutting into the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	 When roundworms come in other bellies and are recognized, and you see that they do not grow anymore, then you should perform the fire cautery according to its quantity, and let it burn one third of the skin; afterwards, cure it as we have said; and none of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with a three-pronged cautery in this shape:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	 but first, mark the place where the worm is and make a line above it, and another below, and move your hand all over the three-pronged cautery.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	 But the first cauteries are more delicate and mobile.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	 When pain comes in any limb, either from falling or being injured, and that pain lasts a long time, and the medicine cures do not help; then it must be cauterized by the cautery called "poins", and the cauteries should be according to the length of the member and its smallness and weakness and its nature and location of twisting and of its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	 If the first cauterization is healed, that's good; but if not, start another cauterization on top of it, because it is customary for the cauteries to turn to the member closest to them, so you must make the cauteries as many times as the patient is healed.
de meselerie	When a wound occurs due to cutting or an injury, and pus comes out of it, and the limb surrounding the wound becomes inflamed, then it should be dressed with the medicine called "meselerie," and the dressing should cover the wound entirely, and the dressing should be applied daily until the wound heals.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	 The disease is sometimes helped by cauterization with great help, and equally the sickness that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	 Can you see if the patient can be cauterized, take care if the disease is at its onset, and if it has been treated according to what we have said in the division, and it does not deteriorate or remain, and you doubt that the corruption will affect the entire patient, then perform V cauteries on the head: Place the head on your lap, the other towards the front to the end of the hair; and [the cautery] above the two horns, and behind on the occipital bone; leave your hand such that the cautery reaches the bone, and such that the scales come out forcefully so that the vapors of the thick humors can escape; and cauterize above the nape according to what is in front.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the swelling is spread out everywhere; it clearly indicates that you must burn with these cauteries which we have said: one on the neck, and two on the spine of the neck, and six on the spine of the back, and one large one on the hip and one small one, and two on each shoulder; two on the ribs, and two on the tendons of the feet, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and beware of nerves that are above the ankles, do not burn them; sometimes a cautery is made on the bone of the fist, and one other on the bone of the stomach, and one other on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	 And know that the more you do with fire cautery, the more help it provides, and it benefits them; and know that patients feel no pain during cauterization as the body is already completely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	 And it is necessary that the cautery be large and small according to the members and joints, as you will find in the ways of ironwork.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	 After treating the wound with wheat flour mixed with honey and other treatments until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When swelling arises in any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters but is not healed, then you perform cauterization on the member according to its size and smallness; and let the cautery be a little deep into the flesh; then treat it with oil until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	 And sometimes they make a cautery at the hand and foot and back, at the nerve opening that immobilizes the limb, and thus if it is opened the inflammation follows; yet no one should interfere unless he is knowledgeable about the members and the openings of moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	When a boil or abscess breaks open and is left to heal on its own without treatment, and it remains swollen, then apply leeches to the affected area according to its size; and let the leeches suck until the swelling goes down. And sometimes leeches are applied to the hand, foot, back, at the opening of the nerve that makes the limb numb, and in this way the boil or abscess is drained; but no one should interfere unless they are knowledgeable about the limbs and the nerves moving the body.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" appears and the medicine devices do not work, then cauterize it with a deep cautery according to the size of the affected area until the blister is removed and its color changes; then apply a poultice made from barley flour and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, along with goose blood and woodpecker blood, of each one part; mix everything together, tie it in a cloth, and place it at the affected site until it becomes healthy.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of scrofula by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	 When a boil begins and you wish to stop it, cauterize with the circular cautery around the entire circumference of the boil.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	 Yet the wise say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the boil; however, this does not seem good to me, because I fear it will ulcerate and corrupt, and I have seen this happen once; rather, it is more proper that it be cauterized around, with the circular cautery as we have said earlier regarding cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	the swelling that cannot grow larger
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	 When someone has a disease called "adubelati", which is slow to heal due to its excessiveness or the age of the patient when they are weak (meaning very old) and have little blood, or due to the time it takes; and you see it speed up in healing: then cauterize around it with many small cauteries by pricking. Afterwards leave it as is.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	 When it speeds up in healing.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierced completely with the cautery, then heat the cautery in this manner:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	 And place your hand in the middle of that disease called "adubelati" as long as the cauteries have pierced through, and make sure those cauteries are such that the patient feels them so that the course of the pus is unobstructed.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 After the patient has been completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure for fire is with iron.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	 Another kind of disease is called "corrodens," which is nothing but an erosion of a limb, for it consumes the limbs as fire dries up wet wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	 If you see this disease in a place that can be treated with fire-cautery, then heat the cauteries little and large, as required for the location or the affected area; after cauterizing all parts until you eradicate all the corruption and nothing remains of it, all that is corrupt should be removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	 And then leave it for three days, and apply soft butter made with oil on the cauterized areas until the burns from the fire are removed and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	 After the cumin seed remedy for generating heat.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	 If after three days you see that healthy pus does not appear, it is good; if not, you should repeat the fire cautery on the corruptive lesions.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	 This poultice has sometimes been cured with an ague medicine instead of fire cautery; but in any case, fire cautery is of greater aid, and I have already said the cure for ague in the division: take it when needed.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	drops that come to the feet.
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	 It often happens that in the foot there arises a disease called "claw" according to our understanding, and it is a large thing swollen which pierces the flesh.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	 And the cauteries for this disease are according to two methods.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	 This means: Cauterization by fire and cauterization by hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	 Cauterization by fire is when you heat the cautery like a quill of a pen, and it should be made of good iron to the extent that it can pierce through the nail on all sides, and there should be fine margins around it; afterwards put the whole thing hot on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it comes out of the hole in the nail; and leave it like this for three days until it starts to emit pus; then make a plaster of wild herbs boiled with oil, and leave the plaster on it all night, and the nails will shrink and be uprooted from their roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then treat the joint with a soothing ointment until it heals.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	 And if it has been turned out of its place by the body's fluid, and this happens often in hands and feet, then you must apply hot cautery. This is done in this way: take a catheter made of lead or iron, or a rod from a potter's oven, and put it on the nail and the blister, that is to say for removing warts; place the catheter so it surrounds completely, then apply a drop of hot oil, and hold your hand tightly, and press your hand while turning so the edge of the catheter reaches the root of the nail, and can find the hot oil passage deeply rooted to the root; and allow the patient to bear the bite of the hot oil for an hour; then leave it as it is, and it will uproot itself with all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	 Follow after another, while you are heating all those who are within the body, then cure them with ointments that soothe pain.
li cure dou trembler	the cures for shaking
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some tremble from cold or quartan fever, or other illnesses, it is necessary that you make four or five cauterizations on the spine of the back, one between each vertebra; and one cauterization at the heel, and one on the stomach using the olive cautery; this will stop the trembling and hasten the recovery from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of putrid boils
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	 Occasionally, through the body, baths or pustules appear, which come from large corrupted substances.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	 In the first instance, when they appear, it is necessary to make a fire cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery made from mirte wood, where the tip should be dipped in fire, or from the long root of aristolochia, or a cauterizing iron.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	 And sometimes the cauterization is done at the beginning when they appear, in this way, and they cannot grow further, but the excesses from which they come are broken, and they become healthy; but it should be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often there are great flowings of blood from the cut artery at the wound or in the incision of the abscess or the cauterization of the member and similar things; it is a very bad thing to let it out.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And although this happens in some cases, hasten to put your finger on the wound of the vein and hold it very tight until the blood is stopped from flowing out; then take the olive oil cauteries, both small and large, until they are all red; then dip .i., whether large or small depending on the size and location of the wound where the artery is cut, in the oil and place the cautery on that vein while holding your finger, and keep the cautery there until the blood is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if the wound suddenly jumps when you hold your finger on the vein and the cautery is extinguished, take quickly another one of the cauteries that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease doing one after the other until the wound is healed; and beware that you do not burn the nerve that is exposed, and that no further harm comes to the patient; and know that when a vein bursts from an artery, it cannot be well stopped at all, except by one of the four methods we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction if it has not been treated, or by tightly binding with thread, or by medicines placed on it which can stop blood; and bind and hold it accordingly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever provides tight binding with strips of cloth or places hot things on it, or similar things, will not achieve anything beneficial if the bleeding does not stop.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this does not help and there is no remedy or medicine available, he must place his index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch it wide until the bleeding stops above the wound and above the vein; and do not move it, but let it be dampened with cold water often so that it becomes very cold, until the bleeding stops and thickens and stops; and make inquiries in advance about the necessary cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of treatments for wounds.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about all diseases in which it is necessary to use fire cautery or burning medicine, and we explain the kinds of cauteries, their causes, instruments, forms, and types; I placed that chapter from head to foot, and I will proceed in this chapter by the same way because those things are easier to understand that way.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, as I begin this, it is necessary, dear friend, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and for that reason, greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	 And I advise you to avoid foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	 For many ways of people come in treatments.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	 There come those who, with their illness, become weak and die quickly because of the craziness caused by their disease or the greatness of their evil, and these should be feared.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	 And from these comes one who gives you advice and says "wait, I am cured"; but the illness is deceitful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	 You should not be too quick to listen to those who come to you with this behavior, but put more trust in your honor than in your desire, and do not believe blindly but wisely from those about whom you are certain, and from which you can draw conclusions; and use prediction and indication in the treatment of your patients so that salvation may be achieved, and this will help you acquire good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear dear son, Our Lord gives you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to breathe from the holy inspiration of his hand, so be it.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	I have divided this chapter into sections, in speaking of each section, just as I have written about the cauteries from head to feet, because you will find it easier to understand what you need from that which is before you.
dou chief plein d’aigue	a head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness often comes upon children at birth, and when the head of the child is forcefully constrained; and sometimes it happens for reasons unknown.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	I have never seen this illness in adults, and all those I have seen hastened to death; therefore, it seems worthwhile for me to describe the treatment in some cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw an infant whose head was filled with water, and it swelled daily to the point that it could not support it; and so much moisture accumulated that it seemed he would die, and this moisture is collected below the bone at the siphac, between the skull and the bone. Therefore, when the moisture is between the skull and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you must make a large incision over the head; let the size be as long as two fingers, so that the moisture flows out. Here is the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the swelling is larger and the abscess is greater, make two cuts in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the swelling is below the bone, and the signs that you see are the incisions at each end of the abscess opening wide when pressed from within and it does not respond: then you must make four cuts in the middle of the abscess according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	 And after incising, remove all moisture entirely.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	 And after the incision, strain the linen and powders, then put vinegar and oil on it, and leave it like that for five days; afterwards, loosen it, and treat the wound with bandages and ointments, and allow the swelling to subside, and give the patient dry meat of a moist animal until the limb is comfortable and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is that you look for the size of the abscess and gather the pus; because sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Then take care that you do not cover the artery and make sure there flows blood, so that the patient dies a proper death by bleeding and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	diarrhea
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to anyone with a disease called "cataract" in the eyes or worse, and the disease is old, and the medicine's cure does not help at all, then the last cure is the cautery, with which two arteries will be cut.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	 Therefore, when you cover them, the patient should lean backward; after that, rub the area with a rough linen until the arteries appear, then strangle the patient's neck with the entire length of the linen; look to see if the veins are visible, and the one on each side will be found behind the ears; mark the places where they intersect, then cut one and the other with a sharp spatula of two fingers deep, until the incision reaches the bone, and this should be done along the wide part of the neck.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, push the spatula under the artery and cut above it, making a cut similar to two fingers wide across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when a vein is cut, it jumps continually outwards without ceasing.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 If the artery does not open on its own, you must measure the space of three fingers, then make an incision to the bone; and the amount of blood that needs to be let out is approximately 6 cubic centimeters, and possibly a little more or less depending on what the patient can endure and the filling of the artery; then observe the wound: if it remains above the bone without spreading, the pus from the abscess does not come, then hold the wound closed and bind, and treat with ointment until it heals.
de emigrainne	of migration
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When an old migraine comes and the acute catarrh arrives, due to moisture in the eyes, heat in the temples, old foolishness and similar things; it is treated with methods of medicine but none of it helps; if arteries from the temples are cut and cauterized as we have said.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extracting them is that the patient should lie down with his/her hair on the temples and pay attention to the artery that opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is not easily found except in some cold people; and if it is found, the patient should tighten his/her neck with some cloths, then rub the area with a rough cloth, and moisten the area with warm water until the artery appears clearly; then take the spatula as shown in the following form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	 Then gently scrape the skin to reach the artery, then pull it up to the pulleys, and carefully separate the tissues that are underneath on both sides; if the artery is thin, turn it at the point of the scissors, then hold the part according to the size of the two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	 If it is not cut open, it cannot move at all by itself in every way.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out the blood from the 5th vein, up to the 3rd one; and if the artery is large, then you must tie it with a strong double thread of silk, so that pus does not come before the wound closes and there is flowing of blood; then remove the surplus between the 2 ligatures in the same hour itself, and then, if you see fit, cauterize the wound with the cautery cutlass up to the bone, but this is the hard work, if the patient does not have a fever and he has a hot constitution.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cauteries are help for treating moisture: therefore it is of great help to those with moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For the extraction of arteries, one must fill the area with old cotton and place a well-made tourniquet on it; and when you loosen them, they should be cured with dry medicines that produce char, and bandages, until it is healed; and if without cutting the artery as you perform, hasten to cover it with cautery, or use vitriol and squeeze it with your hand so that the area becomes discolored; and if this is not available, place your finger on the area for a long time until it freezes, and rub the area with cold water until it stops, and then squeeze it as necessary; and the hard and more difficult part in the extraction of an artery is that you cauterize the vein of this sharp cautery of 2 parts, but they should be well thickened to keep their heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the straw is too thin, it retains less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be between the two blades, one of a thick gap, and then when you have signed [the wound] for two leagues, and you place the heated iron on it until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two leagues; and they should be spaced apart because it is not glued with this cautery throughout; and this is the shape of the cautery:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the eyes' tears are flowing from the veins that are above the testicle of fire, and medicine does not help in treating them; you see the patient writhing in pain, and his forehead sweating as if with fever; and if they are soft and moist, so that the hairs on the scrotum have fallen out, and the scrotum is burned, scalded by the heat of tears, it requires this treatment.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	 And it was called the "crushed cure" by the ancients; you must do this to the patient who has this disease, shave his hair from the forehead, then make three cuts evenly across the forehead according to the length of the forehead; one cut should be as deep as necessary, following the slope of the forehead down to the nose, and the other two cuts should be along the eyebrows above the eyelids, and be careful not to incise the arteries that are located above the eyelids; keep your hand away from the continuation of the jaws, and each wound should be the size of three fingers joined together; prepare a piece of sponge and a lot of linen to wick away the blood, then insert the sharp spatula in two parts as shown:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.
