From the incision which is above the temple to the second incision; and scrape the entire core that is between the two cuts all the way up to the bone, then continue from the mid-incision to the other second one, and then remove this spatulumile (spatula).
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Insert the tool called "cultellaire" into the first incision. It is very sharp on one side and soft, not sharp, on the other side, and its shape is:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	 And strike the bone cutting towards the flesh as needed, and the bone becomes soft towards the bone, and push it until it comes to the midway split.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And cut all the veins that descend from the head down to the base of the incision, and then in the midway split do the same on the other side; and then equally press the blood, press firmly for the blood taken; then place a tent made of old cotton in each split, and place damp linen soaked in vinegar, oil and rosewater on top, and make sure no pus comes out; on the third day untie the bandage, and apply a large plantain poultice with cold tea tree oil, and other treatments to heal wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	The root of the hairs
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When a sharp catarrh comes commonly, and you see the thin and small hairs falling out, and the vision becomes cloudy, and burned paper-like spots; and the hair follicles itch, and when the head hurts with intense pain, and the patient coughs; then know through these symptoms that those materials and that catarrh do not come from anything but many veins, and the remedy for the cure that is there, if it exists, is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	 And you command the patient to bend their head back, then make a deep cut along the forehead and another wide one in the upper lip.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	 From the temple on the left side to the temple on the right, make an incision up to the bone; and move your hand away from the nerves that move when eating; once the bone is exposed, remove all blood with a sponge; then insert cotton between the two sides of the cut and use linen thread; then cover it with dampened cloths soaked in wine and oil and avoid heating the abscess; when it is removed, you must rub the bone until char starts to grow, then treat it with things that promote char growth.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take 2 parts of wheat flour and 4 parts of turmeric, and make a poultice with them; administer it in these wounds to promote healing throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	ear stoppage (or ear drops)
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that falls into the ears is one of the four things: grains or animals, or stones or similar objects like iron; seeds, such as peas, beans, lentils; or something flowing like water and sand and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	 When it falls in the ear stone (or something else that does not fit into the ear) and does not settle or grow in the ear, put the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	 If you see a stone (or something similar) in the ear, pour some drops of violet oil or camphor oil on it, then apply extraction; and make him sneeze with mustard powder, and stop his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and place pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and stretch the ear above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	 Often fever comes from this treatment; and if it does not come with the fever, extract it with fine tweezers, as follows:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it does not fart through the tweezers, extract it with thin wire of small length; and if it does not through this method, make a cane of wax and push its tip into the ear forcefully or through the ear canal, and stop up that which is around the cane with molten wax so that the wind cannot enter with the cane; then pull it out in the form of farting, for often it farts as we have said; and if it does not fart in this way, take glue of any kind and put it on anything that you find, and place any instrument sharp at the end over it; then put a little cotton around it; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not fart through any of the things we have said, hasten to open the ear before the abscess comes and spasms; and the method of opening is that you first make the patient sneeze the cephalic head, and draw blood according to the measure of its power, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small opening in the root of the ear where the fat or flesh depends; and let the opening be as a moon, so that you come to the stone, then extract it with your strength, and suck it quickly into your mouth; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is an abscess that swells, administer drainage; and if it cannot be drained, administer a thin, fine spatula according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	 make an incision in that grain (of earwax or stone).
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	 But do not do that when you think the grains are moist due to moisture in the ear, until you have made many pieces; then take them with subtle tweezers and put them in a sucking solution, as we have said, so that the extraction is done correctly.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	 Then in the ear where liquid falls, the patient should use a warm gargle with first-boiled conditions and wipe the ear thoroughly with cotton wool.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	 And let it lie on that same ear where the liquid is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	 If it jumps out due to this, that's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	 If it doesn't jump out due to this, take many pebbles according to the size of your finger and make them warm slightly in fire; then make the patient hold a pebble or cotton wool in their ear, pressing down with another pebble from the other side and striking another pebble on the one in the ear; do not stop striking one pebble against another until the liquid jumps out entirely and it jumps out completely; if you see, take a thread, tie one end of the finger in the ear and heat the other end with fire until the closer end is burned; then repeat this process with other threads until the liquid jumps out entirely, as we have said in the previous section.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of small animals, such as fleas and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is large and can be felt, bring about extraction with tweezers; and this is the lightest thing that can be removed from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the division and the cure does not improve, if you see any worms, remove them with fine tweezers; but if there are none, take this substance's cord:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	 And it must be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	 Place the thinnest head (of the instrument) into the ear according to the amount of pain the patient feels, then follow immediately with the whole canal; do this repeatedly until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	 If they do not come out (the worms), then stop the canal with cotton as I said in the previous section; and if they do not emerge as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven effective for the expulsion of worms, and you will find or treat the distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with this device, here is its form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And silver or tin is to be placed under a small hole, and above a receiver for distillation; and for pressing within the distillation there should be an instrument of tin well made for this purpose. If you wish, take a scraper and wind it around the tip with cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicine you wish in the canal, which should be in the ear. Then push the scraper into the cotton, and press gently until the oil is distilled or has risen to the ear. The patient will feel the heat within. The distillation should be heated with fire in the same way as it is distilled in the ear; and guard that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be as effective if it were cold.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	ear stoppage (or ear drops)
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without ear problems; and this same thing happens in men due to ear wounds or pus inside the ear, and this stoppage sometimes comes suddenly into the ear, if it cannot be seen; and sometimes there is a small amount of discharge from the ear, which can be seen well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, when it comes in full (meaning the disease), if one cannot see it, is grave in many conditions and when one can see it, you must place the patient's ear to the sun; and look inside: if you see the opilation (pustule) apparent, then open it entirely with this spatula of which the form is as follows:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be sharp and pointed in front and behind, so that it does not prick the ear; if the opilation is of pus or cartilage from the ear, hold it with subtle tweezers and gently press it until all the pus is expelled.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	 And if the opilation is in the ear, take the subtle rasher lightly and heat it a little over fire, then place it in the ear canal.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	 If you feel the opilation that gives the patient pain in the ear, make a small opening carefully without injuring the nerves of the ear; then insert a tube according to the width of the hole made, and moist it with the Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Make this every day until the wound heals, take a linen cloth and soak it in rose oil and powdered vitriol; if you see swelling on the ear, then you must pull out the linen cloth and apply another linen cloth soaked in oil of roses and wax, until the swelling disappears; then heal it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	If bleeding comes, dip a sponge and cloth in cold water and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the flow of blood which are either to treat with distillation.
de la char des papieres	of paper pulp
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is the remedy that comes in papers for the eyes when they are moist and dry; you should stretch them with tweezers and forceps, then strike their roots with a spatula; afterwards place vitriol powder on it.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if it does not work without peeling, then cauterize with the subtle cautery of the lentil, and cauterize afterwards after the incision has healed; and many times they heal, yet nothing remains from their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the hailstone
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	 Often come in the earwax small things that resemble hail in shape and hardness, and because of this is the disease called "grandine", which is a thick mass of moisture in the upper and lower parts of the paper; the treatment is as follows: watch carefully if the grandine moves from one side to another, and it is an easy thing to know; then make an opening of suitable size, then gently scrape each part, take with tweezers and crush.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	 If you cannot cover it with a piece of paper and just prick it a little, it causes no harm to the patient; and if the wound is large, gather it together in a stitch, and treat it until it heals; and if it is small, do not apply force because the ointment restores it soon and annoys the flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	"If the hail is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, turn over the paper and grasp the hail with tweezers and press from both sides; if the paper is pushed away by the incision, do not worry; when the hail is covered, apply salty oil, and care for the affected area until the patient is healed."
de la graisse des eulz	"of the fat of the eyes"
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	 Exinach is a grease that is anointed on paper towels above, and this happens more often in children than in adults, and it greatly irritates their eyes, and they come down with catarrh in the mornings, and cannot bear to look at the light of the sun because their tears flow quickly towards their eyes; therefore they lie down immediately, and sleep on top, and their paper towels are damp beneath their eyelids that the exinach has opened in oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	 And when you press the joint with your fingers and feel something coming out between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	The method of treatment is that the patient should place his head on your clean surface; then take one small linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity of exinach contained in each part, then put it over him; press with your hands from both sides so that the exinach is gathered within the circle; then make an incision in the middle of the moisture using a pointed spatula, but not too large, no larger than the wound made when opening a vein; and cut through the skin to where you see the exinach; and in several positions, the exinach comes out from the incision, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then take hold of the entire piece of coarse cloth between your hands and turn your hand to both sides until it is spread; and make sure not to tear in the incision, that you do not go all the way with the spatula up to the oil, that you do not pierce it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the wound does not open at the beginning of the incision, lift a little the incision gently until it opens; then pull out as we have said, then moisten gauze in water and oil, and place it on the wound, and hold bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	 To such men who crush oilcloth and put it over to corrupt the moisture that is present.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then, heal him until he is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the joint becomes abscessed and hot, heal it with plasters softening it until it is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs from the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper lice are born with hair other than nature's, and they grow, they harm the eyes, and cause illnesses such as customary tears and softening of the paper lice and albugo, which leads to the destruction of the eyes; and there are four ways of treatment: either by cautery along with fire, or by cold medicine according to what is stated in the chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and stitching or by squeezing, as I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the paper lice from the oil to your left hand; if it is converted, that is good; if not, push an awl through one filament of it; and cut off the margin of the paper or the hairs growing from these hairs, and pull one filament along the entire length of the paper, and shave it with a razor; then make an incision in the part underneath the paper, under the hairs, covering the whole spatumile, from the large tear to the small; then draw out one filament, and place a small tent made of cotton and linen beneath the paper, then mark upon the paper a figure similar to the mirte leaf, and it is essential that the figure be according to the quantity by which you want to lift the paper as described to all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	 And to those who have need of large quantities of paper according to how the paper is softened; then they place it entirely over the affected area up to two lines that you have marked, and begin from the largest blister until the smallest; and one of the incisions should be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert an onion in one of the two angles of the key, then peel all of it; then bring the two edges together with a stitch of a fine sewing needle, and squeeze out the blood, and fold over the excess thread on the two corners with anything sticky, if you want to do this; and if not, leave the stitch and the thread for three or four days; then heal the wound without a stitch with drying and binding agents, because the paper revives at the edge of the wound and holds it together, but the stitch is rotten (as they say in ancient times), and this is work without fear; and another method is that you sign the paper with a figure like a thistle leaf, as we have described, with three onions cut according to the form shown here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then join those who are above the small spaces equally according to the form below:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	 And if you cannot hold the pliers, and the thing is not even, take a needle with thread, and insert it into the figure; insert the other thread through the large hole, and the second thread through the small one, and assemble the threads equally between your fingers; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin as you have explained, then close the two edges of the wound with stitching, and cure it until it heals; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar ointments; and sometimes the hair of the paper may be converted: in such a case, you must use what we have said for the incision; but stitching in one place or another is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of dogs is as follows: you convert the skin and turn it inside out as I have said, and then make two stitches by art, and two thin threads as long as the skin and the width of the incision; and tie together the two ends with threads; then assemble one on top of the other subtly over what is above the skin of oil, and bind the two stitches from the two parts tightly; leave it like this for some days, and the skin that is tightened will rot and necrotize and fall off, leaving a hole through which it can heal.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	 If it takes a long time, if the wound is deep and strong, then cure it until it heals; and when the wound has been stitched, and the paper is raised, and the hairs cannot be felt; and these are the shapes of the two canines that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	1. The work (li ovraiges) is such that you take a fine needle, and put on it one thread of silk and fine; then assemble the heads (les chiés) and join them subtly, and let the lengths of threads be a palm long; then prepare another fine silk thread briefly, and join its ends; then place the patient's head in your hand; let the work be done in sunlight so that it is visible, for this work is subtle and minute; then push the needle to the base of the hair adjacent to the natural hair, and make it pierce through the paper quickly until you pull it over the natural hair; then remove the hair up to the base, and put the removed hair back into the hole in the paper, if there is any; then remove your hand until the hairs come out entirely from the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the case (la chasse) is treated and the hairs do not come out, you will draw the case to below, along with the thread that you have prepared, until the case comes out through the opening made and you see it through oil vision; then you will draw the case and the thread, close the oil, and leave it for 2 or 3 days, until the hair adheres in its place and the flesh grows over; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long natural hair, and let them grow together, until they are elongated and then shave them.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the purulence of oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	 When this disease that is called "alecraty" or the purulence comes in the eye, there are two kinds of it: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	 And occurs suddenly due to a wound or incision, or similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	 The method of work in it is that you cut the suture, disconnect the eyelashes, insert linen threads into it, and tie it until it heals; and you should not use drying or constricting substances in its treatment.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	 If you do this, the illness returns worse than the first; but for things that soften, such as fenugreek; and the juice of water or wheat, and linseed boiled, and when it has been reduced to any oil, wrap it in a tent and cure with it.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the key to your cure is that you do not allow it to heal in its original form; and this treatment that we have described is not without caution against this disease returning in its original form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	Of the fat that comes in oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	 This illness which is truly called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	 The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cauterization and similar things; and the procedure for this work is to take a needle with double thread, and stick it in the flesh, and make it pierce from the left tear duct to the right, so that the threads come out in two places of the flesh; then place the flesh above the whole needle, and press with a large spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the shape of the paper returns as it should, that's good; if not, take a rasp and place it in the crack, then turn the paper and make two cracks where there is bone inside the paper; and let the heads of the bones be from the ends of the cracks, and make an angle so that when they are assembled, the figure will be like the figure of a letter with the name "Greek"; then remove that cartilage, according to its thickness from the surrounding paper, then join the two separated parts with a thread of linen; then treat it with the medicine we have said for softening and heating, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	If the illness comes from a crack or incision or cauterization, then you must make a smooth cut beneath the hairs of the paper, as described before; then you should split apart between the two edges of a tent, as I have said; and the work must be done according to the shape of the illness, for it is very diverse in shape, and the wise masters prepare engines with all their power as they know how to bring the figure back to its natural form; and the patients themselves, according to what is required for the work and various instruments.
dou soudement de la papiere	quickly from the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this bond occurs in the hand of men in such a way that the paper is stuck together with white oil and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then it is necessary to insert the point of a razor beneath the paper, lift it up; and hold it between pliers until you cut the adhesion which is near the spatumile, not too sharp or too deep so as not to cause pain to the patient from the sharp spatumile; and make your incision, by which you scrape the assembly, lightly, so that the paper returns to its natural form; and heal the entire assembly, and salt the oil at times, lift fresh sweet oil, and colyrium; then place a linen tent between the paper and oil, and put above the oil wool moistened abundantly with egg yolk; and after the third day use the colyrium and the healing substances until it heals.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail has two types: one is nervous and resembles a hard horn-like growth, and another which is not nervous but resembles white moist matter that when touched with iron and cooked with pliers, it cannot be removed; and both start from the large root, and grow little by little until they cover the whole eye and all the light and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of incision is that the patient places their head on your hand, then you pull out the hairs; take paper in your hand, then bend the nail over with small tweezers, and hold it up; then take a needle, put a horse hair or ox or cattle hair and a strong thread on it; bend the tip of the needle slightly and pierce the nail, poke through the entire needle, tie the nail with a thread and hold it up, then scrape off all the skin surrounding the nail root including silk and wool to the head; then chop the remaining in the root of the nail at the spatula-like tip and the small forces, leaving the natural flesh or nail, so that the incision does not bring forth tears as is usual; sometimes the nail is only set on the onyx, and at the thread, as we have said; then scrape off all the soft spatulum around it as described in this shape.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And ensure that the spatulum does not touch the flesh layer and break it, and that the pulp is not pierced; and after the incision pour some broken oil and ointment made from litargire on it, and leave it until the next day; then treat it with whatever is necessary until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerveous, and you cannot insert the needle, and the tweezers cannot enter it, this condition of the nail is often treated with medicines; and it grows as I have described in the division, and if you see it covered, open the oil of the patient, and take a spatula-like tip slightly sharp according to this shape:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And gently scrape the nail above, and if you see that it does not lessen at all and the reason is pursued, distill from your mouth into the collyrium oil made of litharge and red collyrium powder and boiled, and stop up the oil until the next day; then continue the other work according to this same method, until it is completely healed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing goes against you in the oil as in an abscess, then let it heal on its own, and first treat the abscess with warm remedies until it is healed, then continue the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh from the tear harms the oil greatly, suspend it at the onion, and crush a part of it but not too much, so that tears do not come; then distill into the red collyrium oil made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows over the eyelid
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	 When some men's nails grow red and cover the nail bed and stick to the paper and turn towards the back, appearing like a rose bud; and in such cases, the patient places their head on your hand, then you open the nails, and apply all the red flesh that surrounds them to the appropriate uncures with force; then cut the first layer of red flesh, and continue cutting until smooth, ensuring not to prick the oil at the operation; the incision should be made with a spatula as described in the extraction of the nail and small forces used for excising the bone, according to the form shown afterwards in this chapter; when the incision is completed and all the red flesh is removed, apply oil of ointment or you distill red collyrium resembling corrosive medicines, and place cotton with egg white on top, ensuring it is securely covered by a plaster; if anything remains, let the oil rest and cure the abscess with calming agents for the abscess; then return to your operation when it is healed, and do so for every nail that grows red in this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But in every case, it is necessary that you be cautious of the treatment for each weak part of the natural way; and of the accidental way, in work with iron; and do not strike your hand in any of these works until you see that this member can bear that work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	 The red veins covered with oil become visible and their work is apparent to the eye, weakening the oil for all days.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	 First, inspect the oil that is affected by the sebel and ensure it has no other disease than the sebel. Then, as instructed: ask the patient to place their head in your hand, then press those veins all along the length according to your wisdom, and make sure the pressure is subtle, double as shown below:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be two times in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then let these veins be handled delicately, and suck out the blood an hour after another, until you see the veins move away from the oil; and be careful not to prick the oil with the tips of the spatulas, and do this work at noon before the sun, and be very warm in your work so that no heat remains but the veins themselves; and when you have done this, if it distills green and red collyrium to cure those who are congealed.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to suck out all of it in that hour, apply a plaster on the oil with soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is relieved and assured of healing, then continue according to this manner as before until it is healed; and this is the form of the treatment:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula from oil
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The term for "arissati" fistula: when you cure it with cautery and burning medicine as I have said earlier, and it is not healed, there is a trap in it that you cut open above the abscess where it should die, and drain all the moisture that is there until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you see the corruption and blackness, take all the tools mentioned earlier to reform it; and it is called "sharp head", and it should be made in the form of a pointed chief, and sharpened like a chisel as shown in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place the rotten bone part on top, then turn it between your hands, and press your hand slightly until you feel that the corruption is restored; do this once, then restore the bone with medicinal pressure.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	 If the joint is welded and pus appears, and the body of the bone is also welded, and it remains in this state for 40 days without renewing or becoming abscessed, and no bad accident occurs (for it is healthy); but if not, there is no other remedy than to return the fistula to its original state as shown here: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron, and by hot medicines, and when it is uncovered, take the fork according to this form, and let the head of the iron be at three angles, and let the shaft be tapered to the tip as you see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	 Then place the iron on the edge of the bone, and move your hand away from the oil hole, then turn the fork completely until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through the veins if they hold their hand on the nose (if the blood flows out); and then restore the joint with dry medicines as I have taught you, and when the pus forms and hardens the joint, the matter goes to the nose; it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	From the flow of oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	If all the eyes (meaning openings in a body part, such as wounds or abscesses) are fully opened and there is no need to dislodge anything or lessen it, then you must tie up the patient; next, heal him, apply hot poultices or plasters with iron to help, then apply oil (made of ingredients like acacia, aloe, incense, and sarcocolla); then hold the oil, and apply the poultice on bandages and cloths. The manner of the cloths should be that you take soft cloths, fold each one in four, and place one on top of another according to the size required by the eyes; then bind them with a tough bandage and repeat the hot poultices and plasters and the oil and the cloths and the bandages until the eyes are healed. If the bandage weakens, you must tighten it more; if the bandage wears off after a day or night, you must remove it and see if the eyes heal over again. If they do, that is good; if not, repeat the poultice, the cloths, the bandages and the oil until they are healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	From the breaking of woven fabric
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions occur in the ruptured eyeball, it opens up and fumes like grains of resin, and is frightening to see; then if you cover it, the treatment is such that you push an awl into the root of the affected part all the way to the top, then push another awl where there is a double thread from the limbus; pierce it, leaving the first awl in place according to its position; then hold the eye tightly with the double thread and wrap a portion of the eyeball around it, tightening it well, then pull out the awl and put oil-soaked woolen yarn on it abundantly; and leave it until the threads adhere with the eyeball, then treat the oil with comforting substances until the wound heals; and sometimes the wound is held closed by the eyeball itself in a circular bandage of fabric until it heals.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the eyes appear swollen, pierce them with a thin spatula that comes from oil, remove the moisture and clean the eyes, then enter immediately; then pull it out when it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the oil bowl
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	 This disease called "alcunnati" is not far from an abscess that assembles in the oil, appearing like an ulcer draining pus, but it is not an ulcer; and the manner of its appearance in the work is such that you make the patient sit on a prepared seat and upright, then take the head between your hands from both sides, and move it until you see the abscess come up to your eyes; then it should be lanced, and the pus should not drain and the light should be let in, and let the patient see things as he is used to; and if it does not drain under, know that it is an ulcer, and if the draining of the abscess is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 Make the patient sit between your hands, then take the thin spatulum and press it against the corneal membrane I pouch through the continuation of the conjunctive with the corneal membrane and the corona, until the bubble appears; and when it is issued, distill in the hot sharp oil mixed with honey or hot water and fenugreek, boiled with honey, then cure it with another treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	oil abscesses
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	 We have the resemblance of eyes in the division and what is needed to pierce it; if it works according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	 It is necessary that you make the patient sit crossed between your hands, away from light because of the sun, and hold the oil tightly; then put the paper of the oil in your left hand if the eyes are on the left side, or in your right hand if they are on the right side; then take the instrument called "almagda" in your right hand if the eyes are on the left side, or in your left hand if they are on the right side; then put the point of the instrument under the cornea by the thickness of a reed in the white part of the oil at the lower part of the eyelid, then push the instrument called "almagda" forcefully, and keep your hand pressed until it penetrates the white part of the eye, and feel that "almagda" comes to the empty place; and it is necessary that the measure of the passage of "almagda" be at the full width of the space from the eyelid to the end of the eyebrow; this is the cornea of the oil; you will see the bone through the paper due to the clarity of the corneal membrane, and then put the instrument up to where the water is, then press it down a path after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	 If it (the dislocation) aggravates now, the patient sees it (the dislocation) before him and the instrument in its oil.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	 After a little rest and if the dislocation recedes back to its second position, place the force with the instrument, and when it is in deep and does not go further, you shall gently press around your hand, palm to palm; then reapply the oil again from within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	 Then put in oil cloth or wool dampened with rose oil and egg, and bind with the oil of the wound.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	 We, and those of our time, place on it a mixture of fine powder with much egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	If the gemstone oil cannot enter due to its hardness, since there are some men who have very hard hairs, then you must take the tool called "alberit," which is shaped as follows:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	 And therefore pierce the conjunction only, and do not go too deep, but make it subtle, then put in a little, as we have said; and at the completion of the work, prepare the patient who sleeps on his back in the dark place; and be careful of all movements, and take light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and tie him according to his position until the third day; then untie him in the same dark place, and test his sight, and make him see some things, and then return the bandage for seven days; and it should not be done during the time of the cure or after the incision now, but you should reduce it, because the dislocation rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	 If an abscess is about to open, you should lance the oil before the seventh day, and direct it towards the one who soothes an abscess; and when it is soothed, you should close the wound and put gold on it to cover for any number of days, and remain in that dark room ever after.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	 And then, slowly leave the house, one step at a time, and turn to your own affairs; and know that no disciple should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in his country people make almagda perciet, so that the juice comes out, but I never saw any such thing on our land, nor have I heard of it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And here are the likenesses of the forms of almagda, because those who do not know them will see them; and they are properly from arsenic:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And the head of these [should be] of the same subtlety, and the backbone in four angles bent.
de la char sor le neis	On the flesh upon the neck
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	 Sometimes, charred abscesses of various types are born, some of which resemble scorpions in appearance; and if there is one such that the char is thickened with pus color, or if it has a soft char of bone color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	 In that case, for the soft and unhardened char, it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands towards the sun; open his nostrils, and pour the onion juice into those chars, and pull them out; then take what you can hold with the sharp, thin spatula, until you know that the char is entirely ossified.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any substance that cannot be covered, open it with all sorts of subtle and light instruments so that nothing remains; and if without your notice, or the abscess swells, aid it as necessary; and if it is malignant abscesses, hasten and cauterize it until the pus dries up and all the charred matter is removed, then pour in oil, vinegar or cool water.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	 If it does not open and moisture comes up to the palace, know that it is sane; if moisture does not perforate as required, know that there is new char in the bone above, to which the instrument does not come for cutting: then take a thread about half an inch thick, made of our hands, and spaced between each knot by no more than that amount; put the child's head through the thread at its widest part, and pull through while smelling it until it comes out of the nose into the mouth; and many times children do this in school, and it is easy for him who wants to do it; then hold one head coming from the nose with one hand, and the other head coming from the mouth with the other hand, and know one after the other as we who are holding the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	 Make sure that you know the procedure for the instrument to purge the head, then draw out the thread, squeeze the blood, moisten the thread with Egyptian ointment, and put it back in its place as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes everything that remains of the flesh; then put a plaster made of linen on it for several days until it is healed, and if there is a need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the shape of the instrument to purge the head, as one distills oils and medicines from the head:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be made of silver or lead, resembling a lamp with an open top, like a funnel, and guide it accordingly; and if you see, make the funnel closed, and let the instrument be filled for purging the head; and have one handle on the head to hold when heating oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	On the flesh upon the neck
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often on the head of the neck arises a disease called "telul", which grows and becomes large until it is visible to look at; and because of this, you must cut it open at the beginning, and completely remove it, then put in place the fire cautery or burning medicine; and if you delay too long when it becomes large, take care if it is hard, dark colored, insensitive: do not touch it with iron as it is an aggravated abscess, for when it is cut open once, much harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch and not dark colored, you can cover it all, fear the patient and treat the area with drying and constricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the neck is cut and sewn up
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	 Know that when swelling comes in one of these jointed cavities, it is of little use for some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore, when such a thing happens to someone, check if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then place the two lips together in a stitch, heal it until it heals; and if the lips are already separated from both sides, you must cauterize all the parts of their flesh until they heal, then bring the two lips together in a stitch, tighten it, and sprinkle powder of dragon's blood, and pulverized incense; place some plaster on top of the powders, either strong or other plaster adhering, and let it stay until it dries up, then heal with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of stitching is that you assemble the solution: either with needles, as we have said in abdominal stitching; or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	To the human hands, it often happens inside the lips there is an abscess hard like grains of wheat, smaller and larger; then you should turn the lips and cut above each tooth, take with forceps and strike in every part; afterwards use leeches after incision of vitriol powder, until the blood stops flowing; then apply the ointment of asafoetida and cure the wound with dry substances until it heals.
de la char des gencives	Of the skin around the gums
