Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times, there arises on the gums a type of skin that the ancients called "albulus"; you should hold it with forceps and strike its root, letting the blood flow; then apply vitriol powder or other drying powders to the area; if the skin returns after the incision and this happens often, cut it again and cauterize; it will not return after being cauterized; these are the shapes of the instruments for covering.
des sordens	The sores (or ulcers)
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes sores are collected at the top of teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, rough and harsh scabs which are ugly; and sometimes they are black and yellow and swollen as corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink; you must have the patient sit between your hands, with their head in your lap, and remove the sores or scabs that appear, as long as there is nothing remaining; and do the same for the blackness and greenness, and the yellow and other spots, until they are cleaned; and if one removes what is at the first root, it is good; if not, start again on the second day and the third, as long as you have completely removed everything; and know that teeth require various forms of instruments to be smoothed, according to the work that shows, because the razor used to remove the teeth from between them has other shapes than the one used to remove them; and these shapes and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When treating the tooth for pain, you should delay drawing it out as much as possible, because it must not be done at all; since this is a very high substance and there should be no excuse for razing (or removing) it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 Therefore, when the patient is to be treated for drawing (teeth), you must be certain of the tooth to pull.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	 "Many times the patient feels pain and thinks it is a toothache, and makes the good tooth bleed; however, the pain does not go away even when the bad one has been removed, as we have experienced with some saints; and when you are certain about the dying tooth, then you must make an incision around the tooth all around. Use a strong spatula to protect the gum from all sides; then twist it with your fingers or fine pliers at the very tip of the tooth, until it is completely loosened, then tighten the pliers; and hold the patient's head in your lap so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 "After extracting the tooth properly so that it breaks off, and if it does not come out freely, take any of these instruments and gently push it in from each side, then shake it back and forth as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	 And if the tooth is pierced and eaten, you must fill it with bandages where the holes are; and gently tighten it with tweezers so as not to break it when pulling; it is very important to work around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 And be careful not to break it and leave a part behind, for returning the tooth will bring more pain to the patient from the root.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 And be careful not to act like the ignorant lords who in haste and recklessness break the chariot, and never bring about what we have stated; but they sometimes cause great illness through the roots which remain or because of the broken chariot as we have often seen; and when the tooth is removed, wash the area with wine or oil and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, fill the area with powdered vitriol; and if that does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of instruments, which mute the teeth at first, should have long points and large handles, so that they do not double when you extract the tooth; and these are their shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And have large handles so they do not bend when used, and be of good iron, and toothed for holding them firmly.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	 When the root remains exposed, you must put soft wool dampened in butter on it for a day or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 until the limbs are softened, then put the instruments called "algefri", which resemble a forceps; and inside they should be made like a wedge and this is its shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these instruments, then you must uncover the flesh all around the root and place the tool called "althali," meaning pliers, here is its form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	It should be thick and large so as not to break it, and if the root pops out with these tools, that is good; but if it does not, then help with all the instruments, here are their forms following:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you help with this instrument that has two prongs, here is its form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other tools that are placed before the teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large pliers, whose shape is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this tool must not break, and know that many tools of teeth are; and also other tools, which are not counted; and the wise masters find their own instrument according to what their work and illness require, because there are various diseases where the ancients did not teach any instruments due to diversity among them; and if it breaks a chariot or another bone, which is possible, then he seeks the tools that are required, as I have told you, and helps with gestures, as follows:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and sturdy to hold the bone tightly, so that it does not slip away, but can be held and removed; and then restore the bone with appropriate medicine; and if there is pus in the bone, and it is small, then remove everything with this tool:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to natural shape and the form is ugly, even in young women, you should know if the tooth has not erupted after the milk tooth, and it is not properly aligned, and cannot be filed or trimmed; then extract it. And if it is accompanied with the tooth, take this instrument that is described as being similar to a small beak, made of sharp iron at its tip:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And press hard and hard for many days due to the tooth's hardness, and because you do not move the others; if it appears that it can be filed, file it with a small file as shown below:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and is like the file used to make needles; and file the tooth gently but firmly for many days until it loosens slightly; then smooth it at the end with any smoother, and if the tooth is excessively sharp and bites the tongue, you must file off the sharpness so that it does not bite the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth fall out
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	 When the teeth are about to loosen, either by percussion or falling out, and the patient cannot hold down what they eat without it falling out, and you have treated them with medicines that contract; but this does not help; then they should be restrained with a gold thread, because silver threads become green and rot, but gold never changes; and the thread should be medium sized, neither too thick nor too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to tighten the teeth, take the thread and double it between the two healthy teeth, then put the forceps between the loose ones, if there is one or more, as far as you can see up to the healthy tooth on the other side; then resume the covering until the part where you started, and hold your hand gently but skillfully, so that it does not move; and tie the knot at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 Then put the joint with a wire using pliers, and assemble them, and place it between healthy teeth so that it does not puncture the tongue; and then leave it as tight as it can stay, and if it dislocates, or the wires break, hold it with another wire; if it stays in place and serves for its entire duration, it is the shape of the teeth and the alignment of the two healthy teeth and the two molars, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the teeth fall out and are put back in place repeatedly as we have said; let no one who is not wise and patient interfere; and sometimes the shape of a tooth made from bone from a cow or other animal is placed where the missing tooth was, and it is held in place as described earlier, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cover the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	 Sometimes this ligament comes under the tongue naturally, or due to an accident from a healed wound; and the work is such that you open the mouth of the patient, hold their head still, lift the tongue; then take the nervous ligament and cut it wide enough so that the tongue is dislocated from its holding, and if there is hardness or pain, and it is due to a wound, push an unguent and cut it wide; and make sure the incision is not too deep, because of the artery that is underneath; and when you have done this, lift the affected joint with warm water and vinegar, then put a tent of linen under the tongue; and tighten the patient's jaw each night so the joint cannot heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	 And if bleeding occurs, put it on the level with vitriol powder; and if it refuses to stop, cauterize it with the slow-burning cautery (lentiginout), which is good for this; then treat it with another cure until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see it of short color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is cancer; and if it is declining towards blenchor (gangrene), and there is moisture, press the uncine, and cut it with a thin spatula from both sides; and if the wound persists at your treatment, apply vitriol powder until it is drained; then raise cool water or oil, and treat with other medicine until he is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	 Sometimes boils called "godath" appear inside the throat, which are properly called the two almonds; and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take care: if it is a hard abscess of small size and pale color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also because of the bleeding; but leave it until it turns black, and then you will cut it open or it will burst by itself; and if it has white color on top and the root is thin, prepare the instrument to cover it, but first check that the abscess pus rests in place and is soothed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	 Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his shoulders be in alignment, and he opens his mouth wide, and the sergeant takes hold of it between his hands, and presses the tongue down against all the instrument, as follows; and it is made of silver or subtle iron like a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And press the tongue down on top of the instrument, and if you see the abscess, take the awl and insert it into the mandible, pulling it up more than you can; and pull anything from the cloths with it, then cover it with the instrument, which has this shape, resembling a fork; even though the neck is curved and one end is close to the other, and they are very sharp, they are made of iron or bone.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, hold the iron tongs like this shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And if you do not have this instrument present, hold the iron tongs in such a way: one part is named, and when you have grabbed one of the nuts (or bulbs), grasp the other in the same manner, then heat the wound with hot, sharp, and smooth objects, and if bleeding occurs, continue heating it until the bleeding stops; or scabs from pomegranate peels are cooked, or bay leaves, and similar things to stop the bleeding; then cure it until it heals; and sometimes more abscesses than two nuts grow in the throat, grasp them then equally as well.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 And I treat a woman of an abscess that was inside the throat, to wit, an abscess of small size; and I had closed the throat tightly, so the woman could not exhale through the blocked passage, nor eat or drink, and she would have died if she lasted for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 And the abscess was so high that it had been pushed in through both openings of the throat.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	 I immediately then, and thrust into one of the openings, then pulled it forcefully, and took out a large piece of bone; then I set another in its place where the wound was located, and opened his mouth and pressed on his tongue; afterwards, I thrust the opening into these abscesses, and cut off a portion of it, and nothing but a little blood came out; and thus the woman's throat was freed, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not stop cutting this abscess for long time; and the abscess repeatedly closed up, and filled the place that I had opened, until it became quite large; then I tricked him and cauterized inside the throat; thus it remained without growing; and I left those parts, and God only knows what happened to them after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	 When the arm extends towards the eye and is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is large and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	 When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the swollen abscesses are calmed down, and it is subtle, you must cut it; and if it is round and not long, and it is blood-colored or of a thin color or black, you should make the incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	 For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	 Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said about its size and length, you should make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument as we have mentioned before; then pierce the anus into the eye, and pull it out, and cut it at the second place that I have mentioned in the incision of the two anuses.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And it is necessary that you not cover more than the natural limit of superfluidity, for if you do, it causes harm to the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what has been said in the incision of the II amandres, and treat it until it heals.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	 And if the patient fears to cover (it), then you must use an instrument for the cauterization of the senses to make them fearless.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	 The manner of the cautery is sharp heat.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	 And the patient places his head in your hand, and then you press the tongue against the instrument that has been said or in the chapter of cautery, and fix it with sharp hot iron, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and use the handle of this instrument, which has this shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient has hair in the eye, or oil is applied to it, as with the scoop of a spoon, and the instrument is placed on top of all the medicine over the eye; and the patient lies on his side so that saliva and mucus flows from his mouth into the medicine without reaching the throat and nose; then hold your hand on all the medicine and press it onto the eye for half an hour, until you see it swelling and the bite of the medicine is eased; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, wet the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument into the socket to the cotton, so that the cotton sticks to the eye; and do this repeatedly until the cauterization is perfect, then let it dry for 4 or 5 days. And if you have to start over with the cauterization of the medicine, begin again, and after the cauterization drain the pus around the eye, using a cotton swab dipped in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and be rinsed with cold water, and treated with gargling until it heals.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more effective by fumigation rather than cautery; if it is treated by this method, take camphor and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and wormwood and similar herbs, gather all or some of these in one pot, put them inside, boil them; the pot should be tightly closed with strong clay, and in the pot place one instrument made of hair according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	 And it should be silver or tin, and one of the shoulders pushed into the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the eye through the cane, until the eye is poisoned; afterwards it frequently starts again, until the eye dries up, and make sure you do not do this at the beginning of the abscess heat, for many things happen there; and do not do this except when the abscess heat declines.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	 And if this is not present, then take a cane and put an eggshell inside the head of the patient so that his mouth does not become too hot; for the eggshell does not let the vapor harm the mouth, and it is good treatment along with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a bone or fish spine is stuck in the throat, or some other thing; you must therefore pull out what you can see and press the tongue against the instrument so that you see it move; if it does not open and remains stuck in the throat, the patient must vomit before the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps it will expel the thing then. Or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of cotton, or a radish root, or one morsel of dry bread; tie a thread to the sponge and then swallow it; and when it reaches the place, it will stick, and you can pull it out. And if it does not come out as we have said, take one instrument made of reed according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And bend the instruments slightly at the head so that they can enter the throat more easily, and lift the head high; and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, for it may swell up or push the bone in; it is better for the patient to push the instrument, because they will move or adjust what needs to be adjusted; if they push downwards, pull it back evenly along the entire instrument until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	from the throat's cavity
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	 Sometimes the medicine for sores, as I have said in the division, is done through the treatment of medicines; and when it does not work at all, then look at the throat of the patient towards the sun, since you press the tongue with the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	 And if you see the sore, pull it out very carefully, or use fine scissors that are suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	 And if that doesn't work, take a heated iron, put it in the throat of the patient, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	 And anoint the patient with water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	 Then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth, and pour it in without swallowing, move it around with your hand often; and as soon as the sore feels the water, it will be healed.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	 And if it does not fall as we have said, then subdue the patient with asafetida, at the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will certainly fall apart.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	 And the method of fumigation is that you take the pot or it has charcoal in it, and cover it with a cloth perforated in the middle, and put the head of the instrument inside; then pour your fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the snake in his mouth, and closes the mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but comes up to the anus; and the anus will now certainly come out, and if it does not, repeat the fumigation many times; and the patient should suffer thirst, and eat salty and hot things and drink nothing; and then it will be necessary for it to come out through this management.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument used to treat the nasal cavity, when it can be seen, resembles curved pincers for insertion into the throat; and has the appearance of a syringe tip, and is coated with lime, so that what it takes, it cannot release; and here is its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 Many things resembling abscesses are described here following the memories that come afterwards from one and another in this book, and they are diverse in perforation and incision; and it is in two ways that the one is similar to its appearance, and of that which holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second way is for those that are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 For abscesses of the head are different from those on the bottom, and abscesses in fatty tissue are different from those that come at joints; each should have its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 If there are abscesses, one should not pierce them until the swelling has subsided according to its completion; and if there are such as need to be pierced when they are ripe, and do not die according to their completion, like abscesses that come from joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 For when abscesses come near to joints, and it is left until it bursts around, perhaps the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, which causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 If the abscess is near the main member and you delay the puncture until it has become ripe, it will harm the main member; if it is near the base, pierce it as soon as possible if it is ripe; do not pierce an abscess without digestion being completed, except for one that is near the base, which cannot be fully brought out and should be drained internally, and a fistula may form and not heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you should know the time of piercing the abscess that has ripened according to its completion, and it is when the pain is relieved, and the disappearance of the fever, and the decrease in pain and redness, and the swelling and opening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and you should make sure the piercing is as far from the abscess as possible, and where it has opened; and let the piercing be along the length of the body, and if the abscesses are in the hands or feet, or near joints, nerves, and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no hair.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 In those that drop (down), according to the same limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 And when an abscess is in the hard flesh, it is good to let the perforation remain until confirmation of complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 For if you pierce it beforehand, the body will be filled with much pus, and the abscess may harden and deepen further.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And if any abscess that has been pierced in a large part of the body is needed for the limb to be, it should be.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	 It is necessary to make small abscesses, small punctures; and large abscesses, large punctures, and many fissures according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where the key should be applied, and covered; when it has become as a cloth, and is softened, it is necessary to do the same as with babies: and if there are those that are cut into three angles, and if there are those where the key is used like myrtle leaves, such as angular abscesses; and if there are those where a round incision is made, and other incisions similar to covering.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 He who has no head, like a superficial abscess, it must be pierced completely; and when the abscess is large and has collected much pus, you pierce it but do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but draw out a part; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out nothing crooked; do this repeatedly with great care, many times, until the pus is gone; likewise if the patient is weak or a woman carrying, or small children, or elderly people weakened.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 The pus sometimes spurts out at times with the drawing out of the abscess, and it may happen that the patient dies unexpectedly, but do not worry about it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore, be extremely careful with this chapter, and when you have pierced the abscess, drain the wound, and check if the opening of the abscess is small; and if it is a large abscess, bring threads of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess and there is much damage, it is necessary that you place a thread in each place so that they come against each other; and if you have cut into the abscess part of the skin and shaved around it, fill it with old cotton or linen rags without moisture, and tie it until the third day; then open it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 And if bleeding occurs during your work, bring cold water and apply it, wet the cloth, and place it on the spot, pressing repeatedly with it.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the bleeding persists, apply care and treatment, and the powders I mentioned in this book, and if it is winter, and the affected area or abscess is very sensitive, you must place hot and wet cloths on top of it; but if it is summer, and the affected area is fleshy, you must place cloths moistened with cold water and oil, or cold water and oil, for three days, as we have said before; then open the abscess and drain it, curing it until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	This is what you should know universally about the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how to proceed before the treatment of abscesses, and now here is the chapter.
des soros	on the sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	 For small abscesses on the head, there are methods that we know of which are in linen, just as the jester of a pear, and there are many similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	 There are some that are fat and swollen like boils; and there are others that are hard and rock-like at the base, and no doubt that the arteries do not oppose them.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	 And the procedure of the tail is that you try everything called "incisor", by which the following form comes afterwards, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	 For if it contains moisture, then they make an incision along its length.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	 And when the moisture is drained, they scrape without leaving any hair that contains it, because it will return if left; then immerse cotton in Egyptian ointment if present; if not, in water and lime, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and corrosive sublimate will help those who remain until morning.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then continue the lint, as before, on the second day and the third, until you know well that it does not remain in place; then treat the wound with appropriate ointment until it heals.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	 If the abscess is hard and swollen, cut it open in this shape, longwise; pour out its contents, strip off all the skin from all sides, and apply all your care to draw pus from the cavity where it lies; if the arteries oppose you, do as I have told you before.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	 And likewise for an abscess that is hard and full of pus, cut it open and treat as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	 Cut open the hard, pus-filled abscess and wet it, for it is easier, because there is little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	 And if in any of these abscesses or head there is no moisture, and among these was the abscess that I cut out from an old woman's head; and I found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and it could not be broken; and if one had pierced it with anything, one would have made a wound like that of a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	 In other abscesses or heads coming from children's heads and the roots of ears, they should be opened always at most according to the situation, in order for the pus to drain out; and treat them as necessary.
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	 Often this abscess appears at the neck, under the shoulders, in groin areas, and sometimes it occurs elsewhere on the body, and they are large and connected to each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	 And each scrofula is properly within its side, as the neck and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and the resemblances of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	 Some contain moisture, and there are malicious ones which do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	 In the one that you see with good position, and resembles the color of the body, and is silent in all parts and not at the neck nor the artery or duct, and is not deep; then it must be cut through, and peel off each part, and open the two lips of the scar, if necessary, as we have said for abscesses of the head; and pull slowly, and be sure not to cover the nerve or vein, and do not use a lancet or sharp instrument that may slip, and look carefully, so you do not cover what should not be covered.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	 And if you open the vein or artery and it does not yield, place vitriol powder in the wound, or any powders that stop blood; hold the wound closed; let it remain until the abscess is appeased and the wound softens and begins to suppurate.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	 When the pus has stopped flowing, return to your work until you finish it; then look for your indication if there remain small scrofulas; if so, cut and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	 If there is a vein running from the root of the scrofulas, do not cut that scrofulas at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread and let it hang down, without causing harm; then dress the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then heal.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	 And if you excise the entire scrofula, you must close the two lips of the wound and sew it now because there will be no delay due to excessiveness for the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 Then you must understand to cover the root of it, drain pus, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Those scrofulas with excessive material, pierce there where it is most open; and pierce as the one before said, descending, then introduce probes with ointment and similar things, so that it destroys what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, cure it with ointment made of char, until it is healed.
de squinance	In this case, "de squinance" appears to be a misspelling or variant of the term "d'escroquance," which means "from squeezing." Here is the corrected line:
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke about the size of the throat, but I never saw it done in our land and it is written according to their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who have squinancy, it is necessary that the throat slit called "epiglote" should be cut open; and no aid should be given by these, because all the veins and the spur of the disease are at those who have an abscess in the mouth, or in the throat or in two tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the spur, it is necessary to cover the epiglote to avoid the death that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	 It is necessary, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it under three circles or four small cuts across, between two circles or by the amount of the cut depending on the thickness of the epiglottis; not in the cartilage; and such lesions are suitable for sectioning the epiglottis as there should be no cartilage. And the vessels are long enough for this.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	 If the master is afraid, then it is necessary that he extends the skin of the throat all along, then cuts open the cervical vertebra until reaching the chin; and cuts off the vessels of blood if you see anything, and then breaks the cartilage as we have said; and this is demonstrated by the section of the windpipe which bursts through the broken neck and the lack of voice; leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed where doubt of strangulation exists, bring together the two lips of the wound and sew it closed with care, then apply medications that cause pus to form until it heals.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Al-Zahrawi says not to do this until the throat is completely stopped up, and the patient is judged dead, and the wings are cut off.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 Then press on the throat because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and it prevents death in this way; and for this reason, the old ones commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease passes, and it passes within three or four days. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and treat it until it is cured; and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 A young girl took the knife and stuck it in her throat, piercing part of the windpipe; and I was summoned to treat her, and found her just as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I found the wound and saw the blood coming out of it, and I knew that it had not opened or led to any vein other than the throat, and the veins were flowing through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	 I hastened, and sewed up the wound, and treated her until it was healed; and nothing more happened to the girl except that she regained her voice, and returned to her position; therefore I say, in such a situation of the windpipe do not be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat   (The word 'gorge' can also mean 'throat' or 'neck', but here it refers to 'large throat' as a translation of 'la tailleure de l’epiglotte'. In modern French, 'tailleure' would not be used this way.)
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	 This abscess is called "hernia of the throat," and is a large abscess in color like a grape, and it is more common in women; and it occurs in two ways: natural, and accidental; where natural has no instrument.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 And the accidental type has two ways, where one is similar to a fatty tumor, and the other is similar to an abscess that comes from an artery; there should be caution, and it is not advisable to perform strong measures except in small ones, and prove and search through the whole opening: if you find it similar to fat, and it does not open at all, strike it as one strikes a tumor, and pull it completely out if there is any; and seal it tightly, and cure it as necessary until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	 Many ways of ours are, which I shall explain all their similarities; and now it is necessary that I say the entire difference between a notch and an issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	Issue is heat and sustained fever while the inflammation has passed, and the swelling is complete; then the fever subsides and the heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	 With a notch there is no heat, fever, or pain, and it contains the pus which is its own sac and corresponds to the color of the body, and begins like an abscess, and becomes large; and they are similar in two ways, whether fatty or moist, and very much colored as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to the treatment of the nose, you must first test and examine all the instruments called "introscope", according to their shape that appears in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	 The method of inquising the abscesses in us is that you take a more moist place than you find in the abscess and turn your fingers bit by bit until you know that the straw has pierced the core; then, according to the size of the abscess; extract the pus-holder, and pay attention that it does not burst.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	 If moisture runs from the abscess, let it drain as I have said for other abscesses; and if after the opening no more moisture comes out, know that it is filled with pus, then make a cross incision, take hold of it with forceps, and gently scrape it lightly on each side and pull out the rotten part where you can pull it out safely without damage; and if you cannot pull it out safely, then remove it in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	 If nothing remains, it returns several times; and if a small amount remains, which does not trouble you, apply some corrosive powders to the wound, hold the wound closed, and place warm soothing substances on the abscess, and cure it with other treatments until it heals; and if it is large, cut the two lips of the wound, and heal what causes pain.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein beats against you or something else, and you are forced to act quickly, use vitriol powder, and let it lie for 2 or 3 days, until the wound heals, and let the swelling of the blood subside; then cover again what has remained unhealed.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	 Look at the shapes of the probing instruments, and they come in three types: large, medium, and small; there are also three cross-shaped ones called "albarets", and one called "breb", and they come in three sizes as well: large, medium, and small, to surround abscesses with fistulae; and they are like needles used for sewing witches, and are made of citron wood, iron, or silver, and the yellow ones are more valuable, and are more experienced at penetrating black corbures of fistulae; and they come in three types: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the wounds.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	 The forms of the ankles are very similar, as you can see here: large, medium, and small; and some ankles have two bends in three ways; and some ankles have three bends, also in three ways; and some ankles have two bends, and ankles with only one bend, all of which are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	 The heads of these [anatomical parts] from which one makes an incision are sharp, and there are those who do not cut at all except from one side, so that the vein or nerve is not severed; and these intromissions [tubes] are responded with plugs, so that the patient does not perceive it at the opening of abscesses; and they are in three ways: large, small, and medium, as you can see; and one does not use it except in charnut [cartilage], such as legs, arms, breasts, groins, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another tool smaller, resembling fistulae stitches, according to this form, to stop the blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed sometimes at the place that bleeds from the veins and arteries, and sometimes it is reapplied in this large form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	 Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, until they resemble women's breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wishes to cure them should do so according to this form of this line b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	 Then, cut away the fat, apply medicine-soaked linen to the wound, then sew together the two lips of the wound with stitching, and cure it until it is healed; if the breast tilts downward and becomes enlarged like women's breasts as it happens, tie them up in two crossbars above, by two similar cuts; so that one is held by the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from line b to line g; then cut away the skin between the two lips, remove the fat, and bring what we have said about stitching and powders, and whatever else is necessary for the cure, until it is healed; if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely made, because the patient does not wish to rest, or due to bleeding, then you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; leave it until it digests the remaining fat, and then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of the abscesses in the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the buttocks are handled as hard scrofulas containing moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	 Therefore, those who contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from the line .b. up to the line .g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the whole boil that is in the abscess is emptied, apply the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day; then remove all the cotton and dress it with ointment as needed until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	If the abscess resembles scrofula, make incisions as we have said in the treatment of scrofula; and if the wound becomes boil-like again, bring fire as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	The rupture of the artery.
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	 When the artery is injured and the skin above it becomes stuck, there are often abscesses, and this also happens with an inflamed vein and abscess; and when one recognizes this by the artery, the abscess grows long; and when you feel it with your fingers, it feels tight; and when it is due to the vein, it swells outwards; and it is foolish to cut such an abscess, especially when it is below the joints and angles, near the neck and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore, it is necessary to remove the iron cure and also the one who is at the head should be removed, and in the one swollen with an artery, make an incision through the skin on top; then open the abdomen evenly, and carefully separate the artery from the tissues until it is exposed; then place a needle beneath it, and pierce it up to the opposite side, and tie the artery with double thread in two places, as I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then press the area between the two ligaments with an intromissoire until the pulsation stops and the abscess is drained; then apply the curing bow to it, until the ligament cries out; then treat it with dressing as appropriate, until it heals; and if the abscess is due to a vein wound, you should stain your hand with it from the abscess to all the skin, then place the needle beneath the area that you hold in your hand, pierce it and have a double thread, so that you draw it from the opposite side; then tie the abscess, as I have told you, or the ligament of one of the two parts with two threads; and if you doubt that the threads will not pass, push another needle through all the thread beneath the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and bind the threads in four places; then press the abscess so that the excess is expelled, then press the excess of the wound and leave what is tied; then apply a damp cloth in wine and oil, then treat it with tent and ointment until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	from the black abscesses
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses come in the artery and vein, abscesses appear in black areas when they are wounded, or due to excessive labor, and similar things.
