Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	 And this often happens in the shoulder and the thigh and in all places where there are joints, and it is called an abscess, and its color resembles that of the body, and it is found in various positions with pain; and when it is pressed firmly, the patient feels pain, but it is not entirely in the body, but beneath the skin; and it can be felt all over, and it does not go forward or backward, neither up nor down, and one who is in joints should not be covered by iron: perhaps contraction would occur; and one who is on the head or forehead, apply the cup to it.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the abscess is small, hold it with tweezers and press its base; if it is large, hold it at the edge, peel it off, then cut open the wound and sew up the incision until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	Large swellings hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	 Sometimes it happens in bellies and nowhere else, and it is a disease called "funge", resembling mushrooms, with subtle roots and large heads; some are small and others very large; I have seen men who had two or more bellies that resembled mushrooms rather than anything else, without any difference, and were white, had thin roots, were cut open, and immediately became wet.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	 I weighed them and found one at eighteen ounces, the other six pounds, and in the incision it is such that if you look, the patient is wet and the color of the intestine is white and moist with a thin root; if you cut it open with a broad spatula, then have the fire cautery ready.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	 For in the thigh there often comes excessive bleeding, and if it overwhelms you, then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient afraid and fearful of the iron incision, take a well-made thread, tie it around the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then tighten it, and do not stop tightening the thread until it stops the bleeding, and press through it; if the roots are large, be careful when pressing because of the stomach, but you can well press half of it, then cauterize to prevent it from returning; then heal the wound, and be sure not to cauterize the thread which is of foul color and poor sensation and milk-colored gaze.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an abscess enlarged, and I will come to the treatment of scabies later on.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the thigh is pierced
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	 If the appearance of an abscess comes from cautery of a wound or a fissure in the stomach, and it is above the belly and one of the boils, as happens in other routes, or from blood that leaks from veins or arteries, according to what is before, or from ventosity; and if it is through the route of the stomach and from the exit of the stool, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a light thing with little pain, and open with diverse discharge.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the intestine rupturing, then it is more varied; and when pressure is applied to it with hands, it rebounds, and then returns, and possibly swells, and greatly increases at the entrance of the wound and by heavy labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	 And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing and open when pressed with your hand, do not constrain it; and if it is due to blood, the abscesses are large and hard, and filled according to a certain quantity; and if it is due to ventosity, it is soft to touch, and the operations are that you look to see whether the appearance is due to the blood of the artery or vein, or ventosity.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	 You must let the treatment be.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	 For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, about the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	 And if the appearance is of the intestine or the belly, you must instruct the patient to bend his knee, and be extended straight, then stretch the intestines all around the belly; then command him to strain gently between your hands, then go around the area that you have stretched with a spatula, then cut half of the abscess with a large spoon; then tie it with a strong thread or cord firmly, and make the two ends meet; then open the stretched half of the abscess over the thread, and stick your finger inside, and search for the intestines; if you find it caught by the thread, release it, and push the intestines to the opposite side of the stomach; and if you find a belly, take the spoon, and cut off the excess; and if the artery or vein opposes you, go cautiously, then return to your work and take two needles with thick threads, and stick them next to what you have made an incision; then hold the abscess in four leagues above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the area as it is, and let the dead flesh rot by itself; or cut when it becomes soft and can be pushed, then cure the area as necessary, and cover the abscess as we have said; and drain the blood or moisture that you find, then heal the area.
dou chancre	The translation is "on a boil" or "a boil".
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the resemblances of chancre, and how one should treat it with medicines, and how to avoid the cure of iron; and we say that chancre originates in the marriage, and great caution is required in its cure, and the ancients stated that when chancres are in a place where it can be shaved like chancre that is on the genitals, and in the thigh, and in similar places, it should all be removed when it first appears; and when it is large and old, it is not advisable to approach it, for I never knew anyone to heal it; no one ever healed it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in a place where it can be removed as we have said, is that you purge the patient once with black bile; then make him sweat if there is manifest repletion, then shave the patient.i. one good place to perform the operation; then pour boiling oil or vinegar over the place where the operation will be performed; then press your thumbs or an instrument onto the chancre, and remove all of it without leaving anything behind; let the blood flow freely, and be careful not to prevent the bleeding by cutting into an artery or a vein, if that happens, cauterize until the bleeding stops; then treat with another remedy until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of hydropisy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	 We have said in the division the resemblances of edema, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each resemblance, and the cure that is done with medicines, and that which is cured by iron: it is only revealed; and one should not touch iron in these two resemblances: namely, tympanites and ypsarche, for it is a fatal thing; therefore, when you treat this resemblance of edema called "edematous effusion", if the cure with medicines does not help, look to see if the patient is weak or if he has another disease other than edema, such as dropsy and similar things; in that case, do not touch iron, for there is doubt; but if you see the patient of strong constitution and he has only edema and he is not too young nor too old, you should proceed thus: lay the patient straight on your hands, and the minister presses the abdomen pushing the water to the lowest part of the bladder; then take the curved spoon according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	 And let it be cut through by two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	 And let it be pierced by no more than two fingers' depth, and it should not be bled; then check if the urine is directed towards the intestines: if it is directed due to disease of the liver, then your incision should be on the left side of the third rib; and if it is due to obstruction, then on the right, but do not let the patient lie on the incision lest the excess fluids flow to that weak place; then cut through all the skin with the tool, pull it back, and press your hand all around the bladder as when scouring at the amount of a nail or thereabouts; then pierce the bladder until the hand comes up to the depth of eight fingers, and this is the bladder's neck, then draw it out, and place the instrument in the form shown:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	 And it is similar to a silver needle, thin and made of thread or light wire, and has a hollow part at its small end; and where it touches one side, there are three holes; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and the head of the needle is cut like a feather quill, and this is the shape of the incision that scribes carve into a pen:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	 Above the anus is the urethra, so when the instrument approaches water, you should now move it upward on the instrument; empty then either half or one-third of it, because if you empty more than necessary in that hour, perhaps the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit due to the weapon, or he will fall faint, or approach death; but empty according to its potency and according to what the conditions of the patient's health and his pulse indicate; then draw the instrument out and retain the water, and it is now held back by the cauterization that stops the flow from the bladder, as I mentioned, that you pierce in this manner; then restart the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering, and draw a small amount of water out; do this every day and take care not to let it last too long but only a little water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	 And if you doubt about the patient, and leave him in water, cure him with burial or hot sand, and much sweat or bath, and anoint with wine; and cure him with drying medicines until he is healthy, and cauterize on the stomach and the liver and the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Stopping (or treating) the member (or penis).
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	 Sometimes children are born who do not have an opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	 If it is necessary to make a very fine incision everywhere on the spittle like this shape:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	 then place the small, fine incision in the spittle with wood, and hold it and keep it for 3 or 4 days until he wants to urinate, if it is removed, let him urinate, and then replace it; and possibly there should be no need because the urine that comes out does not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	 The patient with a small ulcer, is to be treated with the cupping glass filled with water, as we have said, it will open up.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	 Those without an ulcer in its place are bled, for no one is born who has the ulcer at the tip of the penis, hence they cannot urinate before lifting their penis upward; and they cannot perform intercourse due to this because the matter cannot reach the opening, and it is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	The method of work is that the patient lies on their back with the head of the penis and the buttocks aligned as the tail of a feather, so that the sore opens in the middle, as necessary; and you should beware of the flow of blood which comes often, and if it happens, you should stop the bleeding by applying pressure to the bleeding area and cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	genital ulcers
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times this albathe comes in the penis, and it is an appearance of a bad genital condition; and there are both harmful and harmless ones; you must take them one time with very subtle hands, crush and clean all, then put cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment on top, and cure it with diafinicon ointment until it heals.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	 And if the ulcer is malignant, of pus-colored and swollen, then you must bring fire cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	 When you have cauterized it, and if the ulcer is along the penis, and has both parts inside the skin and outside, then you must first remove the ulcer that is within; and when it is sealed, heal the outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When you are treating it (the patient), do not be certain that the testicles will not be pierced; blackness and corruption come into its sheath and scrotum; therefore, all that is black and corrupted must be cut off, then apply a plaster made of honey and flour which should be made from the peel of pomegranates and walnuts, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	 If bleeding occurs, bring the moon-shaped cautery in this manner:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	 The cautery is prepared in this way: namely, for the removal of blood and corruption; and if the testicles of the penis are corrupted and retracted, you must bring or lead out a sheath made from yew wood, and make the patient urinate through it; and when the hair is spread at the head of the penis which occurs in those who have not been circumcised, or it occurs due to an injury or abscess, therefore, you must shave the area with a sharp instrument, until the ligaments are loosened, and the testicles are released from the penis on all sides; and if this is difficult to say, then you must shave it with a sharp tool a little below the head of the penis and pubic hair; then press gently between them, and put a thin linen cloth moistened in cold water underneath, which should not be removed immediately.
de la circoncision	When performing circumcision, first cleanse the member completely with warm water; then take a sharp knife and cut off the foreskin, leaving a little skin at the bottom.
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not without its complications, like other wounds; however, when we perform this work of our own free will and for infants, it is necessary that we do the best job possible and make it as easy as possible for healing.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of the circumcision of their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	I wanted the greater part of the masters and sages who performed circumcision to have at least one dagger, and with force, and in all one novacula; but the cowardly ones fled because there are two layers, and by chance if he strikes the upper one and delays the lower one.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Then it is covered and the pain is doubled, and at the mundification which is done with a dagger, the tip of the member is not secure; and in the mundification of the nail, by chance the iron escapes and spoils the work, and many times are born like that which do not need mundification and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Regarding the amputation that is made to all the links of the chain, I have found the advantage in the experiment, because the forces cut equally well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When you press your hand, make an equal cut all the way through; but let the thread be well straightened around the skin; and the procedure is the same as before, so that you make the child understand, if he can, not to tie the thread anywhere else except around the rod alone, and then release it in all possible ways; then make him place it upright between your hands, and bring back the forces between your hands or beneath your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any tool; then push your hand against the rod and blow or suck, and draw it up until the head of the rod is in; then clean it very well of the filth that has accumulated there; then tie a double thread around the fracture site; then tie another thread around the other end of the first one; and hold them both by the second knot at the wrist and the finger, and break between the two threads; then quickly untie the knot above and pull the head of the rod out; then let the pus flow out and out, for this is the purge; and put powder on it and powder that glues well with a little cooked egg yolk tempered with rose water, mixed with fresh rose oil, and leave it like that until the next day, and treat it with other treatments until it heals.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The forms of the forces for the healing are as follows: the two cheeks should be tender and thin, and the cheeks should also be as wide as the hand equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in the healing is when the kernels are at incision; therefore, you must extend it to your nail, so that the lesion becomes an abscess; and cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your nail, then hold it with pliers, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they exceed three days and what is beneath the scrotum is swollen, leave it until the abscesses have subsided and gently scrape it; if it bursts as you can move it, be careful of the part of the scrotum, this will not harm it.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the affected area with powder on a shallow wound as we have said about treating powders, and if it bursts excessively and goes above, this will not harm anything; heal it then, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	The retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	 The retention of urine is due to a stone, or blood congealed, or pus, or frozen water, or similar things, as we have said in the division; and if the urine is not expelled, and you see it is retained by the stone which is lodged or neck of the bladder, then the patient should be bent on their knees; and they should put their feet on the back, and extend their abdomen from the upper part above the lower back, and restrain the patient as much as possible; and then it is forced the neck of the bladder to express the stone above, so that the urine is expelled; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction using an instrument called "siringue", of which this is its form: it should be made of fine, light silver pipe, like a bird's feather; and the tube should be one and a half palm long, and thin at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 And the manner of the issue of urine is that you take a double thread, tie one end to the top of a cotton or wool plug, and insert the plug with the thread inside the syringe; then tie off the excess thread and insert it to the top of the syringe, then oil or butter the syringe and put egg white on the urethra and bladder; then gently place the patient on the seat, and anoint the urethra and bladder with oil moistened with warm water; then carefully insert the syringe into the urethra until it reaches the root of the bladder, then bend the urethra upwards towards the belly; then push the syringe forward to the bladder, and make the patient feel the urine filling the empty space, and this is not done according to this order unless the conduit through which it goes is twisted; then tie the thread to the entire plug and the urine follows the thread, then remove the thread, and straighten the urine; and repeat the syringe until the bladder is empty, and the patient relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	The diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scorching or blood comes into the bladder, or pus is assembled there, and you see it distill acids and medicines, do everything with the instrument called "clepsydra", and its shape is:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	 It is closed, and has three openings: two of them and one in the middle, as you see; and the medicines are inserted into the middle opening so that the medicine reaches the verge without addition, if it can draw out the moisture, and push as needed; and when you want to throw your medicines into the bladder, place the head of the catheter in the moisture, and draw out while withdrawing; if you draw out the moisture with the catheter, then forcefully push back the catheter within; the moisture will enter, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the form of a subtle enema used to administer an enema to the bladder. This is it:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	 And it is made of silver or iron, and the head is higher; beneath it lies the ribs or the liver; then take a sheep's bladder and fill it with the moisture which you wish to use for clysterizing the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts using a strong thread; heat the moist substance on fire; then insert the head of the clisterer into the penis, then hold your hand above the bladder over all the moist substance until the patient feels that the moist substance has reached the bladder; and if you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, make a circle, puncture it roundly; then insert the strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle like a pouch and put in what you wish of oil and moisture and water, seal it in the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, to press with your hand until the moist substance reaches the bladder.
de la piere	from the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the ways of stone and its extraction with medicines; and I have said the difference between the embedded stone in the intestine, and all the signs, and when you should work on a stone of size; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is engendered in the bladder happens more often with children, and this is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder like water in its subtlety; it opens the urinary orifice, it inflames the patient's penis, it pricks it many times, then binds it; and the jumping of these stones often causes foundation problems; and the healing of children is light until they are 4 years old, and it is severe in adults, and it is most moderate for those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is lighter for those who have large stones, than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 And when we come to treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the patient with an enema, to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 For it sometimes blocks the opening of a wound.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 Then grasp the patient by the feet, bend them back and move them under, so that the stone descends into the bladder and does not go too high; then make him sit between your hands arranged, and his hands should be under his thighs, so that the bladder is completely declining downwards; then press and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in the cavity, hasten now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 And if it does not fall when touched all over, you should moisten your right hand with oil, if the patient is a child, or use soap, if the patient is an adult; and push on its base, press the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, bring it to the neck of the bladder; then press downwards with your finger, and push it out towards the place where you intend to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Instruct the assistant to press on the bladder with his hand, and instruct him to stretch out his right hand above, and remove the skin that is under the bladder in the part where you make the incision; then push the spatula covering it, so it takes its shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 And they make an incision between the coccyx and the base, not in the middle but along the left side of the lower back; and it should be straight across the bone, and your fingers should be either at the base or the coccyx, and the opening should be large enough to pass through easily, yet narrow within, according to the size of the stone, not too large; in case the fingers which are at the base press on the stone, causing it to jump out without effort; and be aware that there is this kind of stone or stones with angles and corners: it is necessary to extract them. And if it is soft, resembling a plum pit with a round opening through which the stone passes easily.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	 Then, if there are corners and edges, make the opening larger; and if it does not come out, you must pull up on pliers that resemble a file at the top to extract the stone so it does not escape; or push down on the instrument with a subtle curve at the top; and if you cannot trick it out like this, widen the wound slightly and remove the stones with vinegar; and if there are more than one stone, take out the largest first from the bladder's neck, then strike downwards, pull it out, and remove the smaller ones afterwards.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 And if it is very large, then it must be made larger, and a bigger incision should be made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	 For the patient, there are two things: either he dies or urine comes out due to a leak that the wound cannot heal; however, you must try to drain it or break it with pliers, until you remove it piece by piece; and when you have completed your work, apply incense, aloe, and dragon's blood to the wound and hold it closed, and put on a damp cloth soaked in oil and vinegar, or in oil and cold rosewater, to cool down the abscess heat; then make the patient lie on his neck, and do not undo the bindings until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you loosen it, rinse well the area with oil and water, then apply healing ointments such as diaphanicon and basilicon until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	 And if an abscess swells up in the wound and corruption, and congealing of blood in the bladder occurs, which keeps urine from passing freely: then press your finger into the wound, and drain that blood; for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder, and cause pain. Then clean the wound thoroughly with water, soap, and linen, and aid it in all ways you know until it heals; and it is necessary that all the herbs you use on it, you bind the patient's thighs together, and apply the medicine to the affected area.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	 If the wound is small and closed from the penis, pierced and filled with urine that cannot pass, cure it in this way: you will make many incisions and excuse yourself for the cutting due to this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have already experienced this.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take a metal probe of this shape and sharp at four angles pierced into one thread:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	 Then take the thread and tie it around the stone's shaft so that it cannot return to the bladder; then push the awl gently into the shaft; then turn the awl towards your hand in the stone bit by bit, as much as you can pierce the stone from the other side; soon the urine will come, then press your hand on what remains of the stone inside the shaft.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it is broken and jumps out with the urine, the patient is healed; but if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, tie one thread around the stone and another above, then push the shaft towards the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, untie the string, and clean the congealed blood in the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	from a woman's stone (ovary)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens rarely that a stone is in the womb of women, and if it ever happens, it is a great grief for the cure, and it is forbidden for four reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is because one cannot find a woman skilled enough who reveals herself to mirrors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	 And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a skilled woman in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone of a woman is deeper than that of a man, which requires a more profound incision, and great fear is present. If it is necessary, then you must take a midwife who knows well, and if she cannot be found, then cast your subtle eye [to find one]; and present a wise woman in the affairs of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to make the incision of the stone; and observe very well if the woman is a virgin: Then you must press her shoulder or lower abdomen and seek the stone; and if she finds it, then constrain it under her shoulder, and command her to press her shoulder or press on the sick woman's abdomen, and press with her left hand on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	 If it is dislocated, it must be moved gently from the entrance of the bladder until below, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then strike on the bone in the root of the thigh near the middle of the hip, where the bone is movable and can be felt; do not move your finger over the bone or under, and cut it slightly at first; then push the buttocks into the thigh, if you feel the bone protruding so that the bone can be brought out, and know that there are many types of bones: for example, small and large, sharp and smooth, long and round, and those with rings.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	 know the characteristics to know the solution.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	 And if the bone breaks out, place vitriol powder broken into it and hold for an hour until the bone stops bleeding; then return to your work, as long as the pain persists, and have instruments that I told you in the extraction of the stone for men to help you in your work; and if the bone breaks out again, and it is from the artery that is cut, place powder on the area and press with bandages and do not resume the work anymore, and leave the pain and do not pull it, lest the patient dies; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is alleviated and the wounds are healed, return to your work until the pain subsides.
de hernie carnouse	of carnous hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	A hernia aquosa is nothing but an accumulation of moisture or white matter, which is beneath the bladder, containing the egg; and it is called a "white matter," and sometimes it is specifically in the egg's lining, if one thinks that it is another egg; and this is the skin of the bladder between the white matter we have mentioned; and this does not occur without pain.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this hernia is due to weakness that comes from the bladder, and it spreads out that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	 And sometimes it comes from percussion on the skull, and this moisture may have several colors: either it is declining to yellow, or without red, black, or watery white, and this happens more often; and these are the signs to recognize this assembly, for if it is white as we have said, it is an abscess, round like an egg, and do not open the skull, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	 And if there is moisture in the very fabric (of the abscess), the abscesses are recognized as being of one type with a part of the egg, and because of this it is thought to be another kind; but if the moisture is between the skin and the yellow pus, it can easily be felt; therefore, when you want to know the color of the moisture, probe all around with the instrument, from which its form can be seen.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what follows the intruder, judge of what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when we treat (it) with iron, it is necessary that the patient be bled according to our ability and the fullness of his body; then lie him on his back, on something slightly elevated, and place a lot of cloths underneath him; then sit on his left side, and command the assistant to stand on the right, and extend the arm towards one of the two shoulders nearest the neck; then take the spatula (or lancet), and pierce the skin between them along its length until you reach the point where the pus is yellow, and strip off the skin gently according to your ability; then open the pus pouch completely with a deep incision, and remove all the pus, and then put on the onions (or dressings), and cover it up; but do not touch the neck, only the pus; pierce the whole length of the arm carefully so that if you do not do it properly, the pus will return; and if the egg bursts in your work, collect it back into its place when you have completed the operation on the abscess; then bring together the two shoulders near the neck to a stitch, then treat the wound as other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted with another disease, then it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are suspended, doubting the discharge of blood; afterwards strike the coccyx to the whole suspension, and extract the egg, and heal it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	 And if an abscess has assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches; when the other part is pressed like you have done the first equally, then draw out the blood, and put moist linen in oil of roses into the wound; and put another moist linen in wine and oil on it, and put the two pieces on, and put over it double fabrics, and tie it all with a string according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	 Then take two fabrics and employ them with moist linen according to this appearance and sew them together into the girdle of the armpits, and one of the branches take above the foundation up to the back, and the other at the part of the handle; and the other two branches on the two angles, and let it all be held in the loop of the bandage; and sometimes this branch of cautery is used instead of a knife blade, and you should take the pointed cautery, touch the skin of the coins, and let it become hot as we have said, so that the white pus that contains the abscess is uncovered; then take the cautery according to this form, pierce the white pus with onions, and scrape it off with this hot cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	 And the cup in all ways that you can, while you are heating it; and ensure that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more salubrious; and be mindful of the decorum of blood, and be careful about the operations of cutting; and if anything opposes you, either an abscess or decorum of blood or something else, then cure whatever opposes you, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	 If the patient is afraid and does not wish to undergo this operation due to its frightfulness, you should perform perforation as I have told you, and know that when you are certain by the signs we have mentioned that a discharge of pus has occurred at the location, then have the patient sit on an elevated seat; then perforate the abscess in the area beneath the thumb-sized space, and place the perforation along the length of the body; make the wounds wide so that all the pus can flow out; then put cotton on the site, tie it up, and allow the remaining pus to drain out until the wound is healed; and if the white linen cloth does not let the pus exit from the opening of the wound, you must insert a feather or the instrument for draining pus from dropsy, as its form has been described before; stretch open the wound, know that the pus will return, and in about six months or thereabouts it will be assembled, and when it is assembled as before, the patient will pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of an abscess of the eyes
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	 Know that in the incision of this vein, fear arises in many positions, so it seems to me that one should leave it alone; and I will tell you the work and similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Therefore, many abscesses come from the body, including the eyes; and it is often the case.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	 It is by excessive sour and acute liquid spreading in the joints, or by percussion; and the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; there is no pain found, but it is a severe abscess; and sometimes an abscess swells fearfully and pus-filled, with such color, and occasionally comes from an artery, or from an inflammation of the vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	 When it is from an artery, it can be known by the hot disposition of the abscess when you press it with your hands; and it should not be touched.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	 One who is made swollen by the vein is known by his disposition to the expression of touch upon the thumbs, and can well perform the surgery on this likeness, and on other members; and it is that you strike the core of the bones, then the egg is above, and the thread goes straight through white substance, and releases the suspensory from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	 If the egg is already softened with these swellings born, then it is necessary that you pull out the egg and strike it; and if it is toward the white substance, or within the vessels, it is necessary that you release all of that tender part and strike it again.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the membrane is to one side, you must break it all and draw out the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, apply linen soaked in rose oil and wine to the wound, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of an abscess of the eyes
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	 This is an abscess enveloped by an envelope resembling a boil, with the softening of the bones, and the patient groans greatly as he goes; and the cure for this disease is cautious as fearful as that described above, and nevertheless we will tell you the work on it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	 It is necessary that you make the patient sit on the elevated chair, then push the suspension belt of the loins downwards towards your hands, to all the straps close to the penis, and tie them tightly; then cut with a sharp spatula wide enough to expose the veins, and then skin each side as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in temples; then insert a double-threaded needle where blood comes out, and tie it at the first place where the blood vessel is visible, and tie it straight to the other end; then pierce them evenly along the length of the body, and remove all corrupt humors; then treat the wound as you would a swollen bowel, so that no vein bursts that nourishes one of the loins; because there will be no harm, and if all the veins burst, it is necessary to extract the loins at all the veins; so that the eyes do not lose their nourishment due to the incision of the veins, and dry up and cannot help.
de la routure dou syfac	of the breaking of the vein
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	 The occurrences of this condition are due to the opening or extension in the abdomen, specifically in the area of the intestines, for which the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the openings; and this rupture is either the syphac or the extension of it, and these two types of occurrence have multiple causes: either due to impact, jump, strain, lifting of heavy loads, and similar things; and the signs when it's about the syphac extension are that it occurs little by little, over a long time, and does not happen suddenly; and the abscesses are equal up until near the full extent, because the syphac pursues the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is of a section through the stomach, which brings sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscesses appear variously beneath the skin close to it, and this is due to the outflow of the intestine and the body cavity through the stomach.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	Sometimes the intestines are expelled through the anus and remain blocked, causing great pain to suffer for the patient, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments, due to fear, it is necessary to escape.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	1. The manner of the work is that you command the patient to push their intestine back into place within the wound if it can be reached; then hold the neck in your hands, bring the thighs together, raise the bones above, and crush all the skin of the joints with long forceps; then insert thumb-sized instruments according to what is needed to open the wound, making sure that the eyes can emerge; then excise the diseased tissue beneath the skin of the joints until the white diseased tissue is exposed on all sides; then place your index finger in the position behind the joint, in the area between the white diseased tissue beneath the skin of the egg and the second layer of diseased tissue, and separate that which is behind the egg and the second layer of diseased tissue; then move the joint manually with your right hand, while keeping the white diseased tissue on top to the left side, and push the egg towards the abdomen; command the assistant to stretch the egg upward and dislocate what is attached at the back; check if there are any intestines involved or hardened white tissue, and if so, place it in the abdomen; take a large needle with thick thread made of 10 threads, and insert it into the rear part of the diseased tissue, which is after the skin of the joints; after the abdomen, crush the bones that appear to be of filament size, until there are 4 filaments; then arrange them one above the other in a cross shape, and tie the diseased tissue, as we have said, beneath the skin of the joints, with a strong ligature of 2 parts; then wrap the filaments in thread, and tie them together to form 2 parts, so that no vassals who nurse it can enter; attach the ligature according to the first ligature length, 2 fingers beyond the diseased tissue beneath the skin of the joints, and after these 2 ligatures leave the remaining diseased tissue beneath the joint capsule in a large piece, about the size of a thumb; then crush in the area that is under the joint capsule, until it becomes soft and rounded, as we have said earlier; then apply moistened linen cloths to the wounds, and attach the ligature that we have mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white sores that I have mentioned are cauterized after incision due to fear of blood loss.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 This often happens: leave the ligament until it chooses to slip off; and if it delays in slipping, it should be stimulated with warm water, and place what has been said above on it until it slips; then cure the wound with another remedy until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of carnous hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case, I never saw anyone who dared to perform the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the ancients said that it is made like a splint joining the bone, in this manner you tie the ligaments lightly above them on the underside; then break it, and treat the abscess of those who work on it until the ligaments slip; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
