Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	 Sometimes it comes to rupture in the anus, as we have said, and open the ligaments; and do not remove any intestines from the anus, and if some are removed, it is a mistake, and repair it every hour; and although it stays too long in this place, the wound or suppuration may occur until the intestines are removed; and this happens by the spreading of suppuration which is in the anus, as we have said, because it is spread out, then it is softened and swollen ligaments and opened; and the cure is done by cautery, as we have previously said; and sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner: and the patient lies on his back between your hands, then break the swollen ligament of the rupture at a width corresponding to three fingers; and then pull out the suppuration which is under the skin that surrounds it, then take the right hand and place it over the visible suppuration; and press deeply into the abdomen, then bring the two visible parts of the suppuration near the head of the right hand, and close one and the other; then pull out the head of the right hand, but do not cover the suppuration or extend the egg nor anything else, as I have told you in the cure of the intestinal splint; then treat it with the wound treatment.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And when you cut the threads (sutures), if they break and heal the wound, let it be healed (or until it is healed).
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The leech is confined and has no appearance in the wound, and the cautery is heated up in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the heels
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the heels becomes soft in some men, because the fat inside is softened and can be seen; when it is observed that it needs to be cured, one should make the patient lie on their back, and cut the softened skin above the natural skin; then assemble two lips together for a stitch, and if you see, sew the excess skin of the softened area with 2 or 4 firm stitches; then cut between the stitches, and heal as other wounds do, until it is healed, and cut the threads.
dou chastrement	The torture
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	 It is known that castrations are done according to our law, and for this reason I will not talk about it in this book; and it is only necessary for two reasons: the first is that a person who is castrated responds when asked, and its cure is known; and the second, because we often have need of castrating certain animals to help us, such as bulls, sheep, pigs, and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	 Therefore, I say that castrations are done in two ways: either by attraction or by incision (cutting).
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	 In that which we do by attraction, make the beast sit in hot water until the joints are softened and boiled; then take hold of it with your hand, until it is set and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 From the method of cutting: it is necessary that you dye the beast, and press the hide of the joints with your left hand, then tie the suspension, and strike on each side as much as needed to well skin them; and let no little or subtle fat remain on the veins; and this method of chastisement is better than the one made by attraction because the attraction may happen to leave something from the joints, which makes the beast want pleasure; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	 Hermaphroditism is of two kinds among humans: one kind is when there is an opening between the two genitals as in the figure of the female nature, who has hair, and sometimes urinates in court.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	 And the other kind is in women, with a projection like a phallus and two genitals.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	 The treatment of men and women is that you shave all the hairs around them (the genitals), and treat them as other wounds; in the second kind (of hermaphroditism), from males whose urine squirts through the skin of the genitals, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	The disease or illness:
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	 A hairy growth on the natural part (of the body) is called tentigene, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have as much of it as a hand, and this is treated.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	 It is necessary that you stain the excess of the tendon at your hand or fingers with onions and lightly scrape it; and do not go too deep, so that blood does not come out; then treat it with another remedy until it heals; and to another sore that arises from the mouth of the ulcer, and the boil, and by chance bursts, and is like a cow's teat, and for this reason it will be called by the ancients "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 It is necessary that you treat the tendon as we have said, and heal it until it heals.
de erratique	From erratic [situations]
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	 If the nature of a woman is not perceived or small, it is natural by birth, or an accident caused by disease that comes about; or it is due to the joining of the cervix, or from the soft or thick sifak, and it happens in the womb, or the sides, or beneath, or wherever it may be; and they are unable to conceive, give birth, and possibly have flowers; and their knowledge of this is by observation of the belly.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	 If the stoppage is about to appear, it can be at your throat or nose.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	 If the poison is subtle and about to be at the liver, hasten and do this: place your index fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back, spreading her legs; then form the two livers, while the subtle poison remains round, and close the stoppage; then take wool, wet it in oil, and put it on the spot, and let the woman rest at home for each day, so that she cannot defecate.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	 And if the poison is hard and large, you must cut it with a spatula resembling a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the stoppage is from milk, suspend it at the onion and cut; have medicines made of coagulated blood, such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, together with egg; then bring a large bandage, so that the wound cannot close; and thus let it remain long, and bring a tent of dry linen; then cure it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	 And when a childbirth brings forth frost, it should be covered in this manner, unless the abscess is aggravated.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	 For in an aggravated abscess during childbirth, one should not do anything.
des emorroides	From hemorrhoids [a condition characterized by inflammation of the veins around the anus or lower rectum]
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	 Hemorrhoids are openings of veins which without cure are usually not treated, and when hemorrhoids become old they turn into ulcers; and we have already said in the division their similarities, signs, and here I will say those that respond to treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	 I say that hemorrhoids and ulcers, when they are completely in childbirth, and are not felt by touch, should be cured with iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	 Those at the mouth of the womb, which can be felt, are those that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	 Therefore, you should put the woman in a cold house, then put the tool near the nails, and hit at the roots, then sprinkle medicinal powders that stop blood, such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then press her feet to the floor for an hour, then immerse her in cold water; and if there is bleeding, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and ivy leaves and similar things, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and oil, and make a plaster on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	 If there is bleeding, that's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	 If not, make it sweat with mustard plasters on the back and without injuring the breasts; then take linen, wet it in juice of plantain or elder with old wine, and apply it to the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when the abscess rests, if you treat the place with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, resembling a rough crust, so it must be covered as I have said in the ointment recipe; and then let it heal.
des apostemes de la marris	"from the rectum" - del recto
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	 Many types of abscess come in marriage (a euphemism for the female genital area), such as boils, painful abscesses, herpes, syphilis, fistulas, hemorrhoids, hot abscesses and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the classification.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	 Therefore, I must describe the hot abscess that comes in marriage (the female genital area), which is not like those abscesses that heal on their own; and if you want to know the work of iron (surgery), observe whether the abscess is acute at the beginning of its appearance, full of heat and fever, and becomes red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	 Then do not hurry to puncture [the abscess], but let it heal as long as the pain is eased; and then make the patient sit on a chair, or two small chairs where he can lean, and support him on his back and align his legs at the parts away from the leg; and let his thighs be spread out, and place his arms beneath his knees, and tie them well with a strong rope; then bring the pus towards the right side, and introduce the instrument used to open the abscess, from which the form follows; and it is necessary that when you see you have introduced this instrument, that you pierce the point first to know the depth of the abscess, so that whatever enters within from the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is large, it is necessary to cover the depth of the abscess with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt [the abscess]; and it is necessary that you place the tip of the instrument above, and hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	 And when the abscess opens and it is touched with the thumb, it should be covered with oil of roses or freshly boiled linseed oil; and when the cavity is empty, you should put moistened linen cloths soaked in oil of roses or freshly boiled linseed oil into the wound; place the linen cloth from the wound to the end of the arrow, and on top of the arrow and on the netted linen a clean, moistened linen cloth soaked in vinegar or malves that have been cooked; then treat it for two days with ointment until it heals; sometimes lift the arrow and the wound using an enema of vinegar and honey, and then of vinegar or long-cooked roots of lilies and aristolochia; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	 And if the wound is closed in a marriage (hernias), you must avoid iron cure, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	The birth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	 It is first necessary for the midwife to know the figure of natural childbirth and its signs when you see a woman after labor, desiring to push out the fetus; then hasten the birth of the child; thus know that this childbirth conforms to the natural figure, and it comes forth with its head and the second one follows; and when you see these signs, press gently on her abdomen so that the child is born quickly; for as soon as it descends toward its head, the afterbirth accompanies it, and the marriage is discharged of its excesses by good cleansing; and he who comes out in any other way does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	 For there often comes upon the feet, or upon the body or shoulders, or the hands, or upon the belly, or the back, and it changes by chance upon the neck, or through other malicious shapes; therefore it is necessary that the bailiff be wise and skilled in such matters, and avoid errors and deception, and I will show you all the figures as to how one should assist them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out first through natural delivery and the woman delivers with great effort, and her strength is weak, let her sit on a saddle or have women hold her; then anoint her nature with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then insert the midwife's little spatula between her fingers in the shape shown here:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	 Then cut the afterbirth, and strike its nail so that the moisture within it escapes; and hold the woman's belly until the infant descends, and if it does not descend, you must cleanse the woman with fennel juice and camomile oil; then make her take and vomit emetics, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: this will help the infant now.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	 And if the two hands come out [of place], you must gently reset them bit by bit; and if they cannot be put back, put a woman on the chair, lift her feet up; then turn the chair onto the ground, and bind the woman so she does not move during the process; and if the hands still cannot be put back and the child dies, cut open the dead child with the knife that is placed before you, take out the child, and reset [the hands] equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	 of the birth of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	 When the child comes out on its feet, you must push it upwards; and then turn it bit by bit, until it is even; then grab one of its feet and stretch it bit by bit.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	 If it can jump up to such height, when commanded to jump, and causes it to vomit convulsively; if it jumps away, may God will it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not leap as we have said, you must turn it gently and slowly, according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is easier.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	 And if it does not come as we have observed, say that you give her muscillaige of height, oil of sesame, and beeswax melted, and grind everything in a mortar; put this ointment into the woman's nature and apply it externally; then let her sit in hot water up to the chest; and when she is softened below, let him apply myrrh oil, and place it below, and leave for an hour; then let her sit on a chair, then make her vomit and hold her mouth and nose, and press lightly on the stomach, because the infant jumps now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the exit of the child upon its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	 When the infant comes in this form, place his hands little by little on the belly; then lay him gently on his back, and hang his feet downward, and let him lie on the bed; fold his hands little by little, then take hold of his hands above the stomach, and push the knees out of the way as far as possible; and if the infant does not come, take hold of his feet and pull them firmly, then pull the belly upward, then place your hands; and stroke the infant little by little; and command the woman to grasp herself until the infant is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the infant's delivery which comes out with a hand's breadth wide.
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	 It is necessary to attempt to return the hand: if it cannot be returned, then make the woman stand up and walk; if she cannot walk, then make her sit on the bed, and spread out her legs widely; then bring the mustard plaster that I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on a chair, then study how to return the hand; and stroke the infant according to its natural figure, and make it vomit, and command it to grasp itself until the infant is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	Of the birth of the child on its neck, and it has spread its hands, and its face turned towards the back of its mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	 It is necessary that the midwife touch her hand, then gently twist and twist it bit by bit, and ease it slightly; and when it is leveled, place the natural musk on top of it, as we have said, then command it to move bit by bit; and when you have done this, make her sit on the chair, and command her to take hold of it; then make her vomit.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same way, you should proceed with everything
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	 When the afterbirth comes in this manner entirely, you should pinch the afterbirth with your fingernail until the membranes are emptied; and if the child presses against her face and neck, you should strike it from below so that it is not retained, and the child dies; then push the child inside as necessary, and command the woman to seize it gently.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the birth of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born often, and sometimes three or four; and this is not strange and seldom happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	 These are strange things that do not live unless they are named; I know what they are, they multiply, and are sought by the one who designs them, which is related to filth; and sometimes they issue naturally like mice, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	 If they issue loudly, the cure is as we have said, and let the balm be subtle, and do quickly and lightly what it does; and do in such a way as it is worth moving for salvation.
de plusors enfans	of many children (lit. from many children)
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	 Sometimes they are formed in the womb for one or two or three or four or five or six, or up to fifteen, and they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the wise glorious one, and it is necessary that the balm knows this because sometimes similar things happen; do accordingly.
de l’enfant mort	Of a dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	 When you cure the woman of the dead or miscarried child, and it doesn't come out by itself and you are forced to operate by hand, then you should know if the woman is in good health and has no accident or fear of death. The woman should lie on her back, with her hips inclined downwards and her legs raised. The attendant should apply a mixture of oil and musk-scented alum and fenugreek seed to the mother's mouth, then anoint his hands with these oils and mixtures. Then he gently inserts his fingers into the mother, seeking the position where the fetus is located. If the fetus is near the head, he should fish it out from its neck or mouth or palate or under the beard or in the navel or near the ribs, and if the expulsion is from the feet, he should grasp or pinch it and at the mid-ribs. The attendant should hold the instrument in his right hand, with the curved part between his left fingers, and gently insert the instrument into any of the positions mentioned above until he reaches an empty spot. This is the shape of the instrument:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	 Then insert the arrow against another bone, or if you need to extract it, so that the extraction is even; and then make it even by moving it from one side to the other to come out, and the bones should be dented for holding it in place while moving, as shown here:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	 And if there remains a part of it, press the thumb of one hand with oil against that part and push in that part while pulling the other part; and if there remains no part, insert this bone or higher up in its place, and do so until it completely comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	 And if one hand comes before the other and cannot be returned due to strain, you must wrap it with a cloth until it completely comes out; then break it at the joint of the sole or at the toe, and do so in the other foot as well.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	 And if the child's shoulder is large and it is narrow in the opening, or if it has a tight neck assembly, you must insert the pointed spatula between your fingers, and press the neck and extract the tightness; or you may use the instrument called "almidach", from which the form comes with the tools or chapter that follows this one; and in the same way do the same for large natural births; then pull out the bones with the pliers, and if the shoulder jumps out and it is pulled with force, it may be cut, as necessary for the moisture that is in a worse position; and if it cannot come out, you should break it into pieces where you can. And if it is swollen in the abdomen or under the ribs, you must pierce it until the moisture comes out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	If the swelling is above the feet, the treatment is light, and the direction towards the mouth of the bladder is easy.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	 And if it is dislocated in the abdomen or hip, you must straighten it with the hand wrapped in a cloth; and make the abdomen or hip, until the moisture that is there is corrected; and if other members are broken and the joint remains, you push the ball of your hand deep inside the cavity, and pull out; then you push the bone out further and continue pulling; and if the cavity of the bone is constricted due to an abscess that has come in, you should not work on it, instead you should administer moist and fat substances; and you should introduce plasters, and apply cool soothing and softening liquids.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	 And if the infant is on its side, and you can put it straight, bring forth what we have said in the living child; and if there is no power to do so, draw it out piece by piece, and leave nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	 And when you have done that, bring forth what we have said in abscesses arising during marriage, and if bleeding occurs, it should be tightly constricted, and other treatments should be applied.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	I have seen a woman whose fetus had died, then a second one was placed on top of the dead one and it revived.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came to the armpit, and swelled so much that it opened, and began great purulence.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called for the treatment, and thought long about it, but could not stop the bleeding from the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied strong-drawing plaster, and an object came out, and after several days another one did.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I wondered much, because the stomach has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I suspect that it is the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	 I cut the bone in the wound, as long as the woman was in the best position; and the woman lived for a long time in this condition, and afterwards a little pus came out from the side; I do not recall this chapter being used except when masters find something strange that they know how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	Return the arm to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here comes the form of the pressor, with which you weigh books; and at two turns to the two shoulders of the two hinges.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	 The first horn should be more subtle for binding, and it should be made of ebony or boxwood; and the hole in the stick should be large, and the edges of the sticks should be, and one and a half palms long; and between the two limbs there should be two joins of the same stick, which should be fastened on one side and the other, half a palm long or slightly more; and these two joins are inserted into the hole of the stick to open when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	 Another form, similar and more delicate and lighter in appearance, should be made of the stick of ebony or boxwood, like the pliers; and have two joins, as you see, one palm long, and two fingers wide; and when you are about to open the sheath with the whole instrument, make the woman sit on the bed, her feet hanging and legs spread apart, then place the two joins side by side in the sheath, and hold the head of the instrument under her thighs; then work your hand with the entire instrument as you have done with the pliers, according to the quantity that you see to open the mouth of the sheath, until the woman gives birth.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	All these tools are covered and multiplied in their likenesses; and when the master has prepared them, then he works more quickly, and higher for humans according to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Never disdain the tool that you have not prepared, for their necessity is not excusable.

des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you the treatments for hands and medicine, according to the accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and how they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	 The things by which wounds are made are by impact of a stone, cutting with a sword and knife, or spear or arrow, or similar things; or those that are made according to the body's laws, such as the wound on the neck, head, stomach, liver, and similar limbs; I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds of the head, for the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	 I say that when a simple wound or abscess comes about or a head injury occurs, and the bones are not broken, be careful if it is due to an arrow or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large; doubt the presence of an abscess: immediately make it drain from the head itself, even if blood comes from the wound; and empty the patient's swelling with wine and thick foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it does not want to drain, reduce its food and do not drink wine or eat meat; and place on the wound, if an abscess appears, cotton soaked in rose oil only, or in stiptic wine; and if there is no abscess, place on the fresh wound, with all its blood, and not moving by air, the powder that I will say a little later; and if fire has moved it, place some ointments on it until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like the size of a sword and its lips cannot be brought together by tension, bring them together by suturing, as I will explain for abdominal wounds by suturing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	 If the wound exposes the bone, is gaping and does not hold together, press it; then treat the wound with medicine, fill the gap with hard flesh instead of skin, and instruct the patient to eat solid foods such as cooked heads (of animals) or bread, pulses (beans), and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	 And if the skin or flesh rots away and there is no bone exposed, press everything and pour sulfur (fumes), then treat it; if there is an artery in the wound or vein that cannot be stopped without cutting, try to stop the artery; if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread; and if that does not help, cauterize (it).
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if the wounds are small and simple, the cure is easy; put this powder on it so that the arse moves it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 And the way of the powder is: take a part of incense; dragon's blood II parts; live coal III parts, and grind them finely, and apply it to the wound, making sure it forms well and blends with all its blood; then bind it well, and leave it to heal if it doesn't swell; for medicine is not removed until it has healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes they do this with only chalk when there is no incense nor dragon's blood, but the ulcer has not moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the fire has burned the wound, especially in that case, do not put this powder on it; instead, apply some digestive ointments or wheat flour poultice made with water and honey until it heals over; then cure it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	 And if a bone fracture comes with the wound and it is small, extract it with fine forceps; I will tell you later about the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	Of the wound of the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes or is in the neck and it is simple without any difference from that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are severed.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	 If it is the nerves, there should be no other instrument than to let it heal, and nothing binding should be put on it because it harms the nerves and causes them to shrink; and nothing cold should be placed on the wound because the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be warm, as warm water washed in sweet oil, and boiled water washed likewise in sweet oil, and other stones of this kind according to this manner, and immediately moistened.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is large, then cut it and bind it with strips, until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	 And if the wounds are deep and closed and full of pus, pierce it or deeper; if the artery is cut, and blood flow comes out, stop it, lance it, and cauterize if necessary; if the spine of the throat is cut or the veins, keep them guarded so that the flesh goes upward, and do not touch the throat but replace it according to its natural shape; then tighten it gradually, and leave it for some days, then treat with decayed onions until it heals; and if the wound has pressed into the bone, open it; and if there are pieces of bone, pull them out completely if you can, and those that you cannot have, leave until the wound becomes purified and aligned; and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle powder on it as I said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	If there is bone in the wound and it has a fistula, treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	 If it is a sword or dagger wound, and the wound is deep, observe whether the wound gives off vapors when the patient breathes: know then that the wound is mortal; if it is not deep, and the wound is fresh with all its blood, do not put powder on it immediately nor tie it for the blood that stops up, let it return to the heart, and leave the patient; but apply attracting ointment, and bind it twice a day; and if you do not have ointment, put old cotton in the wound to absorb moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound 3 or 4 days, or more; the spasm, bad tremor of heart nor strange symptoms of pain will not come; and when you see good signs, know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	 Treat the wound and other treatments while it is healthy; and if it cannot heal, then make an incision, knowing that there is a fistula; treat it as needed.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	 If the wound is from a sword or knife, and it is simple, deep, or on the back, treat the front part of it; if it is large, stitch it; and if it is small, use powder, and if it is close to the bone and has broken into pieces, deal with the wound and pull out any foreign bodies if they are loose; if they are not loose, let the wound drain and allow for the extraction of pus from other wounds as described previously.
dou derrompement dou ventre	Breaking of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	 The first dismemberment of the belly is large, medium, and small; from a large wound, sometimes intestines or parts of the intestines come out, because of the insertion of them; and the suturing is more difficult, and often a small wound is worse than a large one, since it requires more effort to put the intestines back in place if they are not put in carefully; for this reason, the medium-sized wound is more beneficial, since the intestines can be moved back into place where they belong rather than at other places. And know that the incision of the belly is according to four types: the two common sutures occur in the suture of the belly, and the sutures of other wounds of the body and the sutures proper for other wounds are common for other wounds; however, they are more appropriate with the suture of the belly, and I will explain each one.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	 I say that when the wound is small and nothing from the intestines protrudes out of it, it is easy to set (the injury), this is one of the two ways: either because of the small size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	 And when it is cold, thaw it in one of these ways: either by soaking a sponge or a piece of wool in hot water only, or you cook in hot squine and cipre and spike, and clean the intestines until the swelling is removed; and sometimes make this wine restraining, and it is boiled to reduce (the swelling).
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	 And when you see the swelling spreading (or growing), if the intestines are bad or sour and cooked, for this reason the entrance is blocked almost completely; and if it cannot enter, then make a small opening in the wound with the instrument used to treat hemorrhoids; and the first cure is boiled until it is cut, but one should not cut too much; and this is the instrument to split (the intestines): if you slice through from within into the cavity and do not push out, and look at the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	 And when the wound is enlarged and the intestines jump out, if it can be reinserted according to its natural form in its proper place, do so, for it is necessary.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	 When the wound is in the lower part of the abdomen, you should make the patient lie on their back and raise their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the lower part of the belly, raise the head and feet higher than the other parts, and similarly if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, direct your attention so that the damaged part is higher than the other, and do the same for both large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	 For small wounds, use the appropriate tools, then place a compassionate person who will cover the entire rupture with their hand and close the lips; and this is the common method of suturing, and it involves taking an awl or several, according to the size of the wound, then leaving space at the edge of the wound and inserting an awl with a strong thread; puncture the two skin layers with the two layers of fascia beneath the skin, as far as you can pierce that part, and bring together the four edges of the fascia; then bind the awl with double thread around it, then bring together the two edges of the wound in order, and leave space again, and insert another awl; tie the thread as you did for the first awl, and continue doing this according to how many awls you need, until the entire wound is bound; and the awls should be medium-sized, neither too fine nor too thick, because fine awls pierce all the flesh, and overly large ones cannot enter well. And it is not good to insert the awls at an angle from the flesh and skin, lest they damage the wound before it heals; and afterwards bind the heads of the awls, so that they do not prick the patient while sleeping, and place tents or cloths over the heads of the awls to hold them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed. This method of suturing with awls is more suitable for small wounds, because it requires only one awl or two if a secondary suture is needed, and involves bringing together the skin layers and fascia edges at one awl with a strong medium thread; and when you have pierced all four edges together, remove the awl to the part where you began, in the manner of sewing cloths; and place space between each stitch the size of a small egg; this suturing is called "home suturing," and I sewed a wound on a man who had a belly wound caused by a knife, and it was larger than one palm, and his intestines were about two palms long, and the wound was inside the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	 I returned the intestine as it had been twenty-four hours before, and the wound healed up to fifteen days, and it was cured, and became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	 And they had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in a place where none was found, nor any medicine; and I placed old cotton twice a day on the wound, and washed it with water of honey until it became healthy.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	 I will now tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle, and thrust it from the outer side to the inner; when it has pierced the flesh straight through, place the tip of the point or where you have stuck the needle, and make it pierce from the other side from the inner to the outer; and the meaning of this stitching is that you sew as pelters sew fur, and leave one hole on one side, then take it up from the other side, until the stitching is completely done.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	 The second method of stitching, which Galen calls specifically, is as follows: gather the two parts together naturally, and apply one of the edges to the other edge, in this manner: insert a needle or edge near the mirror, and pierce only that place; leave the two edges of the mirror; then turn the needle and pierce from the part behind until it reaches the inside, through the two edges of the mirror; then pierce one and the other from the part behind until it reaches the inside, in the two other edges of the mirror that are on the opposite side; and this is the most common method of stitching.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	 Galiens said this word, and it is testified by all, that one should sew the belly with two needles, having thread in each; and it must be done as those who sew purses do, by inserting one needle from one part, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew purses; and know that when the wound is inside the belly, the stitching is more difficult than in other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	 The judgement of the wound is similar to that of other wounds: and it is that when you find the fresh wound full of blood, before the arse moves it, you should return the intestines, and the fat; then put powder healing charcoal on it, and if the arse has moved it, put any ointment present on it until the wound heals over; stitch it, and bind it with sifac, and mirach; then care for the wound as you would others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, immediately apply old cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	 You do not need any other medicine in many cases where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound may spread to the main parts of the body, then you should wet soft linen with warm oil or rose oil, and place it around the wounds and under the saddle; and if there is pain or swelling in the bowels, and this often occurs, then clisterize with black wine, and similarly if the putrefaction reaches the intestines; pierce it from within, and know that when it is the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	 The intestine known as "jeun" cannot heal when it is pierced, and this is due to the inflammation of the veins that are present there, and due to the subtlety of the entire body, and the proximity of its nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	 And if the hernia jumps from the wound, put it back in place like an intestine while it is fresh; and if it is old and turned or black, you must tie off the area that is black, so that no blood comes out, for there are veins and arteries; then cut the part between the ligament, and hang the two heads suspended from the underside of the wound to facilitate the extraction when the hernia falls, and the wound bows.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the bladder
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	 When the intestines are torn and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people, as I have seen a man who was pierced or wounded by a lance; the wound was on the right side of the stomach, became ulcerated and turned into a fistula, and there was discharge and bloating; I cured it according to what I knew, and did not stop fumigating until it healed, and the wounds were sutured.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	 And when I saw it sewn up, I feared that the patient had ill in his belly; and there was no ill, but he remained in better condition, eating and drinking; and any experimentor said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, that it should be bound in this manner: take a deep breath with great bellows, then press the lips of the wound together, and when the breath has opened the mouth, place it on the two lips so that it stretches the mouth open; then strike the head, and hold it so that it cannot loosen, then put another deep breath in this manner until the wound is fully captured; and sew the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	 If the head becomes inflamed in the intestine and brings no harm to the patient, it can be tied with a fine thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal, as follows: take the end of this thread of intestine and tie it to the head of a fine linen thread twisted together, then insert the thread into the needle, sew the intestine, and tie it in place; and this method of suturing is not forceful but rather relies on faith and hope. If the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the large intestines, there is no trick or cure, except through subtleness.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or that it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	 Know that every wound or abscess, when it grows, is universally called "fistula", and likewise when it swells and becomes hard.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	 And a fistula is according to the truth, a hard and white swelling that does not cause pain, and likewise becomes as hard as a bird's feather; sometimes it clears up with a clear discharge, and other times it becomes thick; sometimes it is small, and other times large; sometimes it appears suddenly, and other times gradually; I have spoken about this in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, is not otherwise than by one of the nine causes: namely, because of the smallness of the blood or body; or because of its malice; or because there is hard matter within it, and above the lips, which does not allow flesh to grow; or it has too much pus; or the wound is torn, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because corruption is the manner of pestilence; or because the region's property is slow digestion, late health, and prone to nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, their signs, and their remedies of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I shall tell you the cure for fistula made by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	 Know that fistula occurs in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come from the large veins, arteries, nerves, or the intestine, bladder, ribs, spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet; and if such a fistula comes to the property of the main member and similar places.
