Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	 And all such fistulas are difficult to heal, and there is only labor and ignorance, except for any fistula that does not come up to the level I mentioned and you have confidence in its cure, and you know it; if so, take a tent of wax or iron, if the fistula is straight, pierce it; if the fistula is twisted, seek a subtle tent of reed, as reeds bend with twists; and if the fistula has been torn and you cannot seek it well with tents, cleanse it through one of the openings, for moisture goes from one opening to another, and cleanses it; then treat it skillfully according to your ability, knowing whether there is bone or nerve, and whether it is completely blocked; ask the patient about the pain they feel when you press your hand, and where they feel it; and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, nerve, artery, vein, or in any of the places I have mentioned, pierce according to what I said, and cut out the defective tissue and corrupted parts that are inside; and then heal it until it is healthy; and if the fistula is deeply rooted straight ahead, you must pierce completely through it as much as possible, then insert moistened tents filled with medicine, and push them to the end of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the excess tissue that remains inside; and then place clean bandages on it until it is healed; if it does not heal by this means, cauterize it as we have said; and if the bone is rotten from the fistula, pierce it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If a vein or nerve does not bother you or your main limbs as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is decay and blackness, scrape it until all corruption is removed, then treat with charcoal-like substances until it is healthy; and if it is not healthy, it bows as before, know that you are not yet done: uncover it and dig as deep as you can, remove all the decay, then restore the joint; and if it is thus healthy, that's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	 If the corruption is too deep that you cannot reach it, know that there is no other solution but to let nature take its course; and if there is a small corrupted bone that can be pulled out with pliers, extract it with an appropriate tool, and if there are many bones, pull them all out, do not leave any one behind; and if moisture opposes you and there is no error or fear, strike and press the moisture and charcoal, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	 And if you cannot remove them within an hour, put something irritating pus on the wound and leave it until the flesh is separated around the bones, and then the bones will come out more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as in the leg or thigh, press only on the corruption until all the blackness is removed, then restore the wound; and if there is a great part of corruption and it reaches the bone marrow, it must be cut and covered up to the corruption, and then heal it until it heals; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened in a man's leg, so that you may take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	 The young man was about thirty years old who had pain in his leg due to something inside his body that caused materials to come to the leg, and he had a large abscess that did not burst from any cause; but they mistakenly operated on it out of folly, causing the abscesses to open, and a great amount of matter came out, and it became a fistula, and a lot of pus flowed out which made the body wet and cold; and many people tried to cure him for two years, but there was no wise man in the craft of hands until I was called upon, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him, and the pus flowing from the openings to a great extent; and the young man's body turned red, and he had a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	 I inserted a tent (or a probe) into one of the wounds, and then searched all the wounds, and found that some were approaching each other from every part of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	 Then I hurried and probed into one of the wounds as far as I found a part of the bone, and it was corrupt and perforated; the corruption reached to the bone within; what appeared to me as the corrupted bone, I thought there was no other corruption except that which I left; and I began to heal the wound with medicinal salves for a long time but could not seal it; then I renewed my efforts, and found the bone as before, and discovered that the corruption continued in the bone; I removed it, and tried to set the bone; but I could not do so more than a palm's breadth of the bone, and it fractured completely, then I renewed my efforts with medicinal salves; and it healed quickly and was sealed, and no further work was required except for the weakness of the patient, who could not bear it, and for the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	 For the blood evacuation often happens, but it healed completely, and a hard cartilage grew in its place on the bone, and it had good composition and did not have any harm or counteraction of any kind, neither in the air nor in coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	 If a bone in any part of the body is broken, it should be treated like this: take thread and tie it to the open end of the bone; command someone to pull it upwards; place another thicker thread of linen on top of the cartilage that is from the bone, and tighten the knot so you pull the rotten cartilage under it, and uncover the cartilage where you want it to be, so that it does not blister the cartilage; place a splint or a rod under the bone to cover the rotten cartilage; it should be done as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and it should be done again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	 And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in a part or throughout, you must uncover all the flesh; then place the iron under it, and then press from one side to the other on the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is at a joint, strike the dislocated joint, and the bone that contains it on the other side; and if the corruption is between two joints, there is no other way than to cut; and if the corruption is at the tip of the finger or toe, this is a difficult matter, but you must find out where the corruption is opening; and clean it in all ways that you can, but do not let the vein or nerve interfere with your efforts; and know that the instruments for cutting these bones are many, according to the structure of the bone and its appearance, and their thickness and thinness, and their size and smallness, and hardness; and therefore it is necessary to equip yourself with an instrument suitable for each type of work; and know that the work will show you the tool you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the signs of the diseases; so think about the tool you need according to what is appropriate.
dou feu	hot fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	 The shoulders may dislocate from within or from without; and when you have treated the corrosion with medicine, but it does not help, you must cover that member up to the level where the corrosion occurs, so that the patient escapes death by this means, or a greater evil, the fault of the limb; and the signs are that the limbs become black, as if they were burned by fire, and afterward there will be more blackness, for this corrosion goes from member to member and takes all over the body; hasten to cover it, and if it is due to the sting of some venomous creatures such as sea scorpions, weasels and similar, cover it at the head of the hand, and do not give it any space to come up to your hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	 And if it comes up to the hand, strike at the joint so that the corruption does not reach the arm; and if it comes to the arm, strike at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it's death, and there is no remedy except for the quantity of its virtue; and thus do when the corruption comes or falls: if it comes at the first joint, strike after the other joint; and if it comes or falls, strike all the joint; and if it goes to the leg, strike at the knee joint; and if it goes above the knee, there is no other remedy but to let the patient die; and the way to strike or soothe the member is that you bind it above and below, and extend one servant one cord below, and another servant the other cord above, and you draw the flesh which is between the two cords with a spatula wide enough so that the bone is exposed; then strike or soothe, and put linen cloth on each side, so that the soothing does not touch the healthy part, and bring the corruption to another place.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	1. And if bleeding of blood comes when you work, then cauterize the place immediately, or apply some powders that restrain; afterwards return to your medicine until it is complete; then bind the member with a suitable ligature, and cure it until it heals; and I will tell you what happened to a man in my time: there was a blackness which looked like a burn from fire, and this corrosion first appeared on the foot of the man, until it covered the entire foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he plastered the foot with copper and became well; and for a long time afterwards, the corrosion returned to his toe or hand, and it came to me; I applied restorative things after the cleansing of the body, but the corrosion could not cease; and he asked that I amputate his hand, and I did not want, because I had hope of restoring the matter; and I also feared that if I amputated his hand, that he would die, for the strength of man was weakened; and he despaired of everything, and returned to his earth, and plastered his hand with copper and became well; and I have not told this story except for the reason that one does otherwise when it is necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	 Sometimes an abscess appears in a charred place, and it stays for such a long time that it causes a large swelling of flesh; and then it grows and pierces, and the flesh jumps out with it, leaving the place open, just like a soldier; and the skin that is above it is as delicate as unravelled fabric, and does not reach the bone or nerve, and such illness is called "sain", and is not called "fistula"; but if it becomes so long that it reaches the bone fully, it is called "fistula"; and the skin should be cut all around, in the same way as unravelled fabric; and it does not heal due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	1. And if the skin is inflamed and corruption is not complete, and the flesh is thick, cure it with a clyster in this way: check if the breasts are large and the nipples that are in it are odorous; then clysterize with an Egyptian medicine which is made like this: take asafoetida, oil, litharge, equally, cook them together in a pot over fire until the medicine turns red and thickens to the consistency of honey; then take according to your need from this, make it into water and honey, and clysterize the breast, hold the wound open; leave the medicine for two hours, then remove it while straining; do this many times, until the breast is healed and the pus is gone; and at any time clysterize with water of vinegar ashes, when this medicine is not present, and take vine ash water, pour it on, then rinse, and clysterize, until you know that the breast is well healed; if the patient cannot endure it, or the Egyptian medicine and the vine ash water, then clysterize with water and honey or mead where the honey has the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine strengthens the blood; when you have done this and you have confidence that the breast is well cleaned, then clysterize with those substances that cause it to produce char in the breast, and take defaecating remedy and oil roses and wine; or clysterize with certain medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken their properties or how to treat ointments; if the wounds of the breast are small, and the clyster nozzle cannot enter, then widen it slightly with a knife point, and apply an Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is widened; if the wound is too large, then tie it up and leave only enough room for the clyster or the nozzle to enter, and if the wound emits pus, then cover or lower it.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	 When the intestine is completely protruded, do not allow it to be retracted by force; and if you cannot cover the abdomen as desired, arrange it in such a way that the intestine moves downwards to its lowest point, because when the intestine is completely protruded, do not allow it to be retracted by force and if you cannot cover the abdomen as desired; then arrange it so: let the intestine move gently downwards without leaving anything of the intestine; take medicines for setting to apply on the wound, and place a linen cloth over the entire wound; then press strongly towards the hernia orifice that is larger than the first, because the hernia will be plugged up with the other cloth according to the size of the orifice, and place it over the hernia orifice in order to align the intestine, and do not remove the large cloth until after many days once; and the one who is over the hernia orifice, frequently removes it to realign the hernia, and knows if anything comes from the hernia, whether it is venom or pus or too much, or indigestible; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread out in this way and you see the nature that arises on the hernia orifice, then know that the intestines have closed already and approach healing; then remove it in the morning, or the third day, and when you are removing the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the packing.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breasts are swollen improperly after many days, know that breasts do not always swell.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	 And if subtle venom poisons for a long time, do not despair of health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	 There are some people whose wounds do not heal for a long time or who make them worse; and if the breast swells indigestedly after many days, know that it will not shrink; and if the breast does not dry out, and is swollen and protruding, use drying medicines containing moisture in substance and dryness in effect, such as plaster of Paris, for it is the last medicine; use plaster of Paris, mixed with rose oil, and equal parts of old wine; then let it set and use it; and if plaster of Paris is not available, use myrrh and aloe and incense, grind them, powder them on the honey when it is on the fire; and then apply a cloth to it, and sometimes administer an aromatic oil and celestial roots, which are like flour and cinnamon; and use simple medicines or compounds: grind them, make powder, and sprinkle it on the honey that I have said, and use it; if the wound is deep and not cured by this cure, then know that the corruption is complete, and it presses into the bone or hard members or joints; if the wound is cured by a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 Parasitic abscess originates beneath the nail of the finger or toe, or sometimes elsewhere; and when it is neglected, if not attended to, the abscess grows, spreads and discharges pus until it reaches the root of the nail, possibly even destroying it completely. The corrosion advances up to the bone, causing painful odor and enlarging the joint, turning its color.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	 When treating as described in the previous section and it does not help, then you must cut away all the remaining excess of the nail and cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy and the nail is intact; and when the skin around the nail begins to swell and turns white, and it starts to bleed, you should place heat under the nail so as not to burn the skin, push it upwards slightly, cut away the affected tissue gently and lightly, apply burning and corrosive medicines to remove all of it; then cure it with warm ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	 And if the corruption is in the bone, strike and draw it out, for as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal; and if you see the tooth corrupting, strike it with one of the teeth that was mentioned before, then heal it when it is healed; and if it is pierced, wounded, and causes great pain, it is necessary to drain it first; then strike the nail with a pointed spatula in cutting across it from above, and be careful that the cut does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, place something over it to soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain in the hand is deafening
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	 The fingers that grow on some men by accident are all flesh, and sometimes they have bones or nails, and one of them may not grow in the root of the joint, or their growth is in one of the fingers of the hand.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	 The one born in any natural way should not be silent, and the one born at a joint may possibly be silent; the size of the one who is fleshy shall be light, in this manner: measure him by his root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	A newborn from the joint root is difficult to cure; hold it covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For the one who is born or should be in the last birth, you must first cut the round flesh up to the bone, then cut the bone with an appropriate saw, and heal it until it heals.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swellings that come to the joints often come by birth, or by injury from a wound, or by burn from fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	 If you must cut that suture, so that it may be repaired according to its natural forms; then put between them two tents or dampened cloths in oil rose, so that they do not stick together; or you put between them two thin planks until the joint is healed, as required.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If it happens that one of its two [parts] comes with the palm, then strike the joiner [or joint] as necessary.
des vils	 The poor (ones)
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	 Wounds are large swollen ones filled with melancholic superfluities that occur in many members of the body; and it happens more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must sometimes administer purge for the liver, and then cleanse the basilica (small intestine).
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 The iron cure is in two ways: one is to strike it, and draw out black blood; the other way is that you open a vein and let all the blood flow out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	 The incision is made in this way: first the leg of cold water is warmed up very strongly, until the flesh becomes thin, then hold the patient's leg from above the calf to the part below the knee; then make an incision in a vein, either in one place or in two places or in three, with a large cut, then separate and draw out black blood to your hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the disease's strength can bear; and then sew it up, and command him to eat meat that is stimulating black bile; and repeat the evacuation and healing when the veins are full, and help the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The elevation of the hernia is carried out in this manner: raise the patient's leg, if there is much hair, then immerse it in water, or if not available, heat it with fire; and apply it to the groin area along the thigh, or in the part below the knee; then scrape the skin at the edge, and peel off the vein from both sides, as soon as you feel it; it will appear red and black, and when it appears under the skin, it seems like a white cord; then push the intestine down, until it is elevated from the skin, and then pull it up gently, then press again in another place three fingers away; peel off the skin over the vein again as before, then lift it, and press again at the other notch, as done previously; then make another cut, or more if needed; lift it again, and press at the base of the foot, then pull and lift until you reach the second cut; draw it out, one section by section, until it all comes out, then press; and if you cannot draw it out and lift it, insert a strong double-threaded needle through it, pull and draw, insert it under the intestine, turn your hand from side to side until it comes out; be careful that it does not pop out, for if it pops out, it cannot be drawn or lifted, causing harm to the patient; and when you have treated it all, place damp wool soaked in vinegar and oil over the wound; and care for it until it heals.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 And if the face is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it open forcefully, but do not cover it up; draw it out as we have previously stated.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	 The shape of the iron used to pierce the face should be curved and not sharp, so that it does not cut the vein; it should be thick because if it is too thin, it would cut the vein, but be thick as we have said. Here is its shape:
de la voinne civile	 of the common vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 This vein is located in the legs, in warm parts where no grass or trees grow and in dry ground; it may also grow elsewhere, but this happens due to the corruption that comes from below the skin, as when snakes enter the body through the flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that a very large inflammation comes in the leg and then the pulse changes and the vein begins to forcefully emerge, as a root of a plant does.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 When the shoulder is open, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of cloth from 7 to 12 inches wide and sew it, leaving the cloth on the leg and every time it starts to swell, wrap it again around the cloth and sew; if it becomes too long, cut part of it, and wrap the remaining part and do not cover its root, until it is completely out; for if you cover it, it returns into the flesh, causes abscess and purulence or other illness. Therefore, it should be treated little by little up to the neck and no remnant remains on the body; this vein can sometimes be as long as 5 or 10 fingers, and once I had a man come to me whose vein was 10 fingers long, when you cover it with lard or lead, pierce it all the way through, so that everything drains out. Empty the matter inside it and apply herbal medicines for purulence every day, then cure it like an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 And sometimes at this vein, many hands are applied, and especially when it opens at the joint of the foot or hand, causing a great loss and bleeding that jumps; treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 from worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	 This disease is called "cattle sickness" on our land because it often affects cattle, and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, and travels throughout the body expanding and contracting, causing pain in one member after another as it moves through the skin or goes away, and jumps out; it is poisoned by corruption of some humors, like serpents and worms and ascarides in the stomach; and there is doubt about its harm, for when it travels through the body, it moves towards the head and reaches the eye, possibly entering it, and destroying the oil; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 When you see it to be cured and drained, one can force it out only when it moves: therefore, you must bind the limb above and below with a strong narrow rope, then strike above and draw it out; and if the wound is deep into the flesh, and you cannot touch it, cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm that it does, is that it runs oil, as we have said; and if you see oil coming or near to it, hold under it a cup-shaped object, then strike above, and draw it out; and it is necessary to use the patient with purifying medicines of soluble substances for bad humors, and to prevent him from eating spoiled foods.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 The pain which comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that moves from one member to another; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	 I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the armpit of the arm; afterward, it began to rise like a worm towards the shoulder, very quickly, as if living silver when it cuts from one place to another; the pain left that place and pierced into the shoulder, then a little later it ran all over her body, until it came to the other arm; then she told me that it returned around her body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed at how it moves from limb to limb, because I had never seen this disease in such a manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	 Moreover, I wanted to point out that pain often wants to move from one place to another, but in the case of this woman, it did not want to do so; and I thought it was because the woman had a dry body, exposed armpits, and due to this constraint, it appeared as if the wind were confined; however, this does not apply to those who are delicate and have moist bodies or closed armpits.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	 And when you see to cure this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we have said, lay it down quickly and firmly on both sides, then press upon it until the breath constrains itself to the place; cauterize the place; and if you do not see it at your eyes, treat with what drives out wind such as fetid pills, pills of serapin, and similar others.
des saiettes	 arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows come in various shapes and sizes depending on where they strike the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	 They differ in that some have large points, small, smooth or serrated; those with two angles, those with tongues, and those where there are pieces; and the one which strikes any member does so according to two manners: in a principal member, such as brain, heart, liver, spleen, kidneys, intestines, bladder and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	 When a limb falls into any position and the signs of death, which I will tell you later, appear to you: it is necessary that you take care of the removal of this arrow, because death comes in many ways after; and when this ill sign does not appear to you at all, and the arrow is not fully inserted, pull it out, and heal the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	 And the sign of the brain when the arrow pierces and hits the skull, and a bubo-like swelling appears on the head, is when scrotum, spermatic cord, and hernia, and redness and inflammation of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of the mind, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps there is discharge from the nose or ears; and perhaps it loses speech and voice; and pus comes out of the wound white like cheese, and also it swells like a blister of meat; and if this sign appears to you, keep away from the treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is not inserted.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	 The signs of an arrow wound when it hits the chest or the heart are that it is near the left breast, and it feels as if something hard has been thrust into it, not empty; and sometimes the arrows also become silent like hailstones, and there comes cold blood in the court (cavity), and chilliness and cold sweat, and fainting: know this without doubt that death is imminent.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that has never pierced the bone is when there is no pus-like scum jumping out from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and breathes heavily and asks for cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	If the arrow falls on the bed of the wound, it is lodged between the ribs; it causes great pain and heavy breathing and moves all the limbs of the shoulder.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	If the arrow falls on the stomach, it might cause something undigested flesh to jump out from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow strikes or pierces the belly, and does not burst from the intestinal passage, there is no hope in treatment, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	If the arrow strikes into the bladder, and the urine bursts out and flows away, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the hands and arms, throat, shoulder, neck, spine of the back, wrists, hips, legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to various positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When an arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not poisonous, as I will tell you what happened to me, you should do this instead.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	 If an arrow or splinter falls into the root of the nose: I tried to pull it out from another side under the cheek fat, and it came out without harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	 And playing with an arrow that fell into the oil fat beneath the paper under the ear: the arrow was curved, and I could not reach its tip towards the end, and the arrow was large like a Turkish bow, without any special skills for ears; the game was safe, and no ill accident occurred.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	 And pull an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears (meaning it had barbs): I was the one who pulled it out, and I made it as smooth as possible while doing so, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	 And pulled an arrow from the man who had it lodged in his throat or belly, and I thought he would die; but after he had passed thirty days, his condition did not change; I cut above the arrow, devised a plan, drew it out, and there was no bad outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	 And if an arrow falls or strikes the man on his back, and the wound is sewn up over it; and the arrow remains inside him, and does not alter his natural condition, nor does it find any trouble in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	 And for another man, who received an arrow in his face and the wound was stitched up; and he endured suffering great pain for a long time; and many similar things happened to him.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	 And a spear was thrown at the king of the princes, who had fallen in the melee, and he leaned slightly to the right side; and the spear was completely retracted three days later, and I was called to treat him afterwards.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	 I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	 I probed it with a delicate probe and did not feel anything; but he felt a prick and pain below his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	 I thought it was the point of the spear, so I applied a drawing plaster with an attractive and digestive leech to it because the flesh did not swell; and the tip of the spear appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	 I placed the arm in a sling for several days, and healed the wound straightaway, and kept the patient for a long time until he felt the arrow within his neck; and he told me this.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	 I applied an irritating medicine to the wound for several days until it opened, and then tried it, and felt the head of the arrow protruding at its place; then I inserted the medicine into the opening of the wound through that irritant, until the head of the arrow became visible; and after exceeding the term of four months, it burst out so that I could pull the pliers over it, and on both sides, but it could not come out; then I did not cease to refine and devise ways of instruments, until I got the pliers well made according to the form that will come at the end of this chapter, as I pierced it, and returned the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	 And the mirrors judge that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored; I will restore it then, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	 I have told you the quality of arrow extraction, but you put your care into that which I do not say, because books cannot fully grasp it; but wise masters can compare well with a little thing and with what is present and defective, they find nine solutions, and nine tools, to the detriment of things foreign that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	 I say that arrows do not come out of the limbs where they are fixed except in two ways: either through the place where they enter or from another side; and the one that jumps out where it enters is an arrow inserted into flesh, and sometimes jumps out again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	 And if the shoulder does not jump now, leave it until the skin is stretched around, and the joint is aligned; and in the same way, if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, let it be like that for several days and move it every day; and then it will jump, and if it still does not jump, pierce all around with a very sharp instrument until the surrounding area is widened, and then pull it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	 And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head and goes up to one of the ventricles of the brain, and any of the accidents that I have mentioned occur in the patient: do not pull it out immediately, but leave it until it is even after several days, because if the arrow reaches such a state, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	 And if the arrowhead is not fixed entirely but only in the bone and does not reach so far, and the patient remains for some days with bad condition, then try to draw it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply pierced and cannot be drawn out, administer tourniquets around it as I told you; then heal the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	 If the arrowhead is lodged in the body so that it cannot be seen, try to find it with all your might; if you feel it, draw it out with any instrument suitable for the purpose; if you can't due to the narrowness of the wound and the deep penetration of the arrow, widen the wound as much as possible; then draw the arrowhead and if there are ears attached like they hold onto something, remove the tissue that is stuck inside it from both sides as much as you can, then break or bend the ears of the arrowhead so you can pull it out; be careful not to break the arrowhead while trying to pull it out.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, push the lymph down to the joints around it, then pull it, for extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	 And if the flow of blood obstructs you, bring what we have said in the treatment chapter to your attention; and be careful with the incision of the nerve and the vein, and use devices as much as possible to draw out the arrowhead without risk, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and position the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow hit him, for this is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot do it, position him according to what the sign indicates.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	 The arrowhead comes from another place, or it opens something related to it, or the skin is swollen in that area as one can see or feel; cut then around it, as far as the pliers can reach, and then pull it out; if it does not come out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	If it is retained in the bone, turn your hand round and round until it enters the bone and widens the opening, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	 And if it cannot come out, leave it still, and then continue the extraction until it comes out; and if it was from an arrow, push it all the way in; and if it fell, and you see that it should be administered gently, administer an instrument with a pointed end, so that the point of the arrow enters the hair of the instrument; and then push further, and when the arrow is caught by the instrument, push the instrument with the pointed end entering in, to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	 If the arrow is touched, you must cut all around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 If the arrow falls or lies in the abdomen or bladder or side and it is near, and you can cover over it, then cover it; and be careful not to cut a vein or nerve, and pull it out, and then stitch the wound, if necessary; and care for it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the tweezers used to extract arrows is similar to an eagle's beak, and here is its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in many sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	 The form of the swelling head [or mass] is like the feather of a bird, to push it to the point of an arrowhead, as shown here:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the tweezers for pushing and for grasping is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins in the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 There are 31 veins from which one recovers, of which the number after the ears is 16, namely: two bladders that are called "herbech"; and the two arteries that are in the temples; and the two veins that are in the eyes of the two eyes, which are called "aspir"; and the vein that is on the forehead; and the vein that is at the base of the nose; and the two tendons that are at the neck; and the two veins that are above the lips, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and the two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 The veins that are commonly cured in each arm are V: one is the cephalic, located on the left side of the chest and called by the common people "arm vein"; the median is called "fistula", composed of the cephalic and basilic, and called by the common people "heart vein"; the basilic is either on the right side of the chest, and it is called by the common people "ventricular vein", located above the wrist bone, and it is the one that is opened, which clearly appears above the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 And the cephalic vein is the vein between the little finger and the ring, and has two branches; and in the leg there are three veins: one below the wrist on the left side of the chest, and the second is at the right ankle; and the one called "nesse" which is at the other ankle's wrist; and in the other leg there are three veins beneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 The treatment of the veins located behind the ears helps with catarrh and emigraine, as the old physicians have known; and the quality of this treatment, just as I tell you, is that you raise the patient's head, and rub the place or the veins with a rough cloth; then hold the patient's neck with a screw, until the two veins appear behind the ears in the two dependent places on the head: then press on them, and where you feel the pulse beneath your hand, hold firmly; then take the lancet, and thrust it through the vein up to the bone, then move your whole hand along the vein, and pierce and the skin and the vein well two times through; and let the blood flow until you see; then bind and tie, until it is healed; and I have already said about incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	 The first artery of the two that are in the temples, is good for migraines, old sores, and eye diseases; it cures tears from the eyes. The quality of the artery is as I say: the patient lowers his neck until the two veins appear clearly; then feel the pulse under your thumb, then press on it; then lift the vein up to your index finger on top of your thumb, insert the lancet into it, lift the vein further and strike, as you have done in the other veins, and let the blood flow according to your need; then release the patient, and place your thumb on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it; then form it, and leave it until it is healed; we have spoken of its covering and its extraction, where the book begins.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	 The first joint of the vein in the forehead is as valuable as the head cavity in the face diseases of old, and it has emigrated and turned red; and the qualities are such that the patient twists his neck while straining, until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", whose form is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	 Place the point on the vein and lift it with your hand, or something else, and allow blood to flow according to the amount that you see; then release the patient's neck and tie the vein until it is healed and not worked on again with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Moreover, the flames should not be too sharp; and the vein must be crossed, for the bone is close by, and in case of an accident, the flames might break it when they are too fine.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	 The second joints of the veins that are in the eyelids help with swelling, redness, inflammation in the eye, and face diseases; and the qualities of their vein drainage are such that the patient twists his neck in a bind, as before; then drain it, and let the vein drain from the cross, a short length of flame, a little wide, because there is no char.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	If the vein is thin, it may break; then correct the blood flow, as needed, and then tie it up with cloth, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	 The vein of the nose from the nostril is useful for treating ague, scrofula, and diseases of the face such as migraines and redness that come from the face, and especially when it is old. The qualities of the vein are that the patient holds their neck, then compresses their nose with your left hand, and takes subtle flame long, and pierces it through the opening between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open easily and the blood will start to flow soon; do not go too deep, and make the bleeding stop according to necessity, then leave it for a night, because it is quickly restored. This is the form of the flame:
