Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	 The strain of the second joint helps in the setting of the ankle, at the beginning of swelling, and in many diseases, putrefaction, corrosion, herpes, and inflammation; and the qualities of the strain are such that the patient extends his neck under one and the other, as we have said; and the master standing above the patient's head, the patient lying on the bed, then open the vein slightly along its length, then draw out the blood moderately, or as much as necessary; then heal another vein, then untie the ligature, and gently tighten all the veins so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	 of the removal of stones (or kidney stones) from the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The healing of mouth wounds assists in the cooling of the mouth and the corruption of gums, as well as cuts and swellings of the lips, and the nose and around it.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	 And the qualities of the removal: have the patient sit before you and hold his neck as I said; then turn the liver, and look at both veins, one is to the right liver and the other to the left, and they are recognized by the fact that they are dark, and by the smaller veins surrounding them; therefore strike one and the other, and if you do not know which ones they are, and you have doubt, then strike the larger one of each, and similarly do with the upper and lower veins above and below, as it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	 of the removal beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	 The veins under the tongue, which are located below the language, help after the cephalic vein is opened, and this is when the neck is compressed, and when there are diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth; and the qualities of saining are that the patient should spit in your hands before the sun, lift the tongue, and look under each side to find a black vein: thus both are healthy, and do not go too deep, as beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	 The veins from which one commonly sains are sained in two ways: either by pressing firmly all over with the flat blade of a mirror or a thin olive-oil-like substance as you cut through, and it is called "anesil"; and they are large and small according to the size and compression of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame mirteenth is very renowned, and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	 And it is necessary to open the veins swollen with thick blood, containing much and troubled blood; and this is the form of the olive-oil flame.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more finely pointed, and it is for healing subtle veins with thin blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	 The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps to alleviate the diseases that are in the throat, neck, chest, and stomach; it is necessary for the patient to urinate healthily, and for him to release the artery that is beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	 If the artery is struck and bleeding occurs, it should be stopped, as I have said; but the flame should not be pressed, but cut off like a nail.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	 If the basilica does not open clearly, you must open it and change another one; or you may choose any other opening from it, or you may urinate in its place by the arm: it opens clearly; and cut off the flame gently, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	 And if you wish to find the joint of the bone, it is necessary that you dislocate the arm; touch the joint until you recognize the pulse; then mark the joint with a cross; tie the arm and burn the vein with fire; be careful not to injure the artery when you see the joint swell, for it is the artery: avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it rises high like a child's urine and the limb without is red and thin, know that it is not of the artery: haste then, and place your finger on it for a long time, then press your finger firmly against it, as it often happens; tie the arm and leave it still, do not let the patient move it; be afraid and do not let it move until it becomes healthy.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if it is not bleeding and the medicine is not present, and it swells up, then cut open the artery if it is open, because the head will shrink back; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	 And take a slice of fennel, cut it and take one half and place it well until the next day; if it does not bleed, that is good; if it does, cure it as we have said, with powders that stop blood; and stopping the bleeding should not be done in many ways due to the small size of the wound, and the thickness of the thread on the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	 The healing of the vein in the middle helps treat blood from the head above and from the chest below, as it is composed of basilic and cephalic, as we have said; and it is necessary for the lord to be aware that he bleeds due to the nerve that is beneath, and if it bleeds too much and you find the nerve, inflate and heal it as much as possible, and by accident it may not heal; and this nerve opens up frequently, and if it does not open in any men because of its subtlety, then you must use an instrument to close it; and avoid touching the nerve with your strength.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	 The first aid for the skull is to draw blood from it and help the eyes; it is necessary to drain with olive oil or myrtle fire, because it is the safest of all veins, as there are no nerves or arteries beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	 Moreover, it is necessary to seek the lighter vein and not hurt anything the first time, even if you have to start again; and sometimes the veins swell for some men the first time, but don't hurt them.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	 The first thing you should know about draining is that it is not done unless to maintain health and avoid future illnesses; and the draining should be done in one of the three veins: the skull (cephalic), face (facial), or basilic; and it should be done at the beginning of spring, during summer, and in winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear; and it should be done on the first or third day, after 2 or 3 hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	 The sacred art of healing administered to diseases has no fixed hours, but when necessity arises during day or night, in all hours and at every moment; and it is not appropriate to heal children until they are 14 years old, nor a woman bearing fruit before the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should the elderly over 60 years be treated.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	 And when some desire to be healed, in whatever manner that may be, it is necessary that the intestines are cleansed with a light clyster, if much feces have been retained, so that the veins do not expel the superfluidity harmful to the main organs; nor is one healed who is excessively salty from meats, or drunk, as long as they are in such a state, nor those suffering from dropsy; and if one desires to heal after a colic attack, vomiting, distention of the abdomen, excessive urination, labor, watchfulness, and conjugal relations, and those whose strength is weakened, or injured by weapons or the body itself; then refine the humors, if they are gross, through food and drink and medicines, if you have that power; then immerse [the patient] in baths, provided nothing hinders, to refine the blood, and heal the vein from the side of the third finger as we have said; and protect him on that day from labor, pain, lust, and similar things; be cheerful and joyful, and let the healer be taller than the one being healed, and rub his arm two or three times, then gently pull out the suture above, because when it is too tight or small, it cannot heal without; then rub the area with warm water until the veins swell, and feel them; then moisten the healer's fingers with a little old oil, then place his thumb of his left hand under that vein near the joint where you wish to heal, so that the vein does not flee or escape from being cut.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	 For there are veins which flee like ropes in the sinew, and those that are full of windiness, so that when fire is applied to them, they shrink from the flame and cannot open the vein, and such is one of these; and if the vein swells, the wound is too narrow, therefore the sinew-pullers should be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens for the first time, it is good; but if not, then continue a little below or above that place where it did not open, unless the place is swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	 And if the limb swells and the patient panics, allow it to rest for a day or two, and do not tie the arm: perhaps abscesses will form; do not enter water, then repeat the sinew-pulling if desired; and if the opening is small, or the wound is narrow, cauterize the opening gently and you doubt that blood will flow out as much as you see, put heat directly on it in that very opening; and open it a little hastily, so that the limb does not swell again; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	 If you see the joint swollen, do not start the bleeding, put a little bit of oil on it, as it alleviates the body from blood, and the oil is transformed in this place where the oil is applied; and similarly administer oil in each bleeding that you make incisions into veins, to stop the flow of blood; and the same thing works for triacle and bow, when it is placed on the joint; if it becomes too thick, it becomes thin and spreads.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	 And if there comes a large abscess, which happens often, especially when the incision into the vein is small, hurry, and put a moist sponge on it, hot, and keep it for an hour; and you should do this after the flow of blood from the vein, and if it remains in place after several days without any blackness or greenish color, it will not harm; and if you see something, put something made of aloes or myrrh, re-melted under warmth, on it, as a plaster, or something similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there is abscess and appearance at the opening of the basilica: put your hand on it then, and if you find it soft with the pressure of your hand, this is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore do not put anything on top of what has been said, for by chance it may be in court without the artery; but make .i. plug (or pressure) dry to harden the place, then cure it with another remedy until it heals.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood from each according to the quantity of its power, and of the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, allow it to drain until it becomes red; and if you see it swollen, allow it to become subtle; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	 And it is necessary for the one who is full and hollowed out, and has need of bloodletting, to make a larger wound for him, and let the veins be wide; but for the weak one, do the opposite, and it must be drained little by little, and it should be done by cutting across, not by pricking; and this method of draining is safe from the disorder of blood and damage to nerves, and is more effective than draining long or wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	 For the one whose body needs to be bled, it is necessary to give moistened bread under ripe pears; if he is heated, let him bleed three or four times; and for those of cold constitution, eat before bleeding soft bread in syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chicory, and fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	 If the palm hurts after bleeding much, then it is necessary to apply a poultice of charcoal, and an aromatic subtle syrup; and use other things as we have said in the division or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if you wish to shatter some bone [or break a bone], and heal it again later, as necessary, when it has been weakened by long healing, it should heal little by little, according to the quantity of its strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	If you wish to shatter some bone [or break a bone] after the first healing, and it has been strong, it should heal in 9 hours after the first healing, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	If you wish to heal from another side, it should heal on the second day or the third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	 For there is much blood within the body that is already warm and causes fever; in such a case it is necessary to draw out a large quantity, and open the wound as wide as possible; then you reward all the conditions of bleeding, and place your hand on top of the poultice when it stops bleeding, so that death does not come at the site of the poultice, and this happens many times when the bleeder is negligent; and you must not dislocate the arm, and make blood come out a second time, and if the wound is closed, you press firmly; nor should you straighten the arm if it is curved, but leave it until it stops bleeding a second time; or you pierce the point of the flame, so that the congealed blood from the vein issues, and place on top a piece of fresh linen and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the abscess has burst, leave it be and do not squeeze it until the abscess is soothed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	If you need to draw blood a second time, do it in the same place or in another vein or the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is connected to the carotid artery because it is composed of them.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	 And the manner of the wounding is that the patient plunges his hand into hot water until the flesh turns red; then it should be bound moderately, so that the vein appears clearly, then pierce with care, neither wide nor long; and make a large cut, and heal well near the joint of the hand, and if it cannot be drained, put the hand back in hot water, and let the blood flow out into the water, as much as you need; and if it is in the summer, do not push the hand back in hot water, for it causes more harm in the summer than in the winter; and the wound of this vein is safer than all other wounds, as there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	 The hot cautery for the hand should be applied for all liver diseases, and this is the method: hold the hand, immerse it in hot water until the vein flees if you see it; and if the hot cautery passes through, and you cover it entirely with everything, it causes no harm; and do not go too deep because the nerves are completely bare beneath all, and then replace the hand in hot water, so that the wound does not freeze up and cannot heal.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have let the blood as much as is necessary, place oil and wax over the vein to solder it quickly, and do this for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The salve for the left hand applies to the sickness of the mice, and do the same as I told you on the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	 The hot cautery for the spleen should be applied for all diseases under the body such as stomach diseases, retained inflammation, kidney disease, thigh and leg diseases, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	 And the qualities of his wound are such that the patient should put his foot in hot water and rub it over the vein until it perishes, and tie it above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot it goes to the many rain; therefore, make a large incision there or at the ankle, which is more beneficial.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you cut above the foot, be careful of the nerves that are below and make a cut as in skinning; let the flames be anesthetized.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	If the wound cannot be opened, immerse the foot in water and allow the vein to drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	 And if the wound treatment is required for the first time, it should start again above a little, because the area is salty; do not doubt of the nerve, as we have said, and similarly do with the softer part of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The flesh of the sciatic nerve is at the knee, and its draining relieves the pain of the thigh, when it is for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	 And the qualities of his wound are that the patient immerses it in water and twists above the ankle four fingers, for otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, let it be drained in all ways that you can, and by crossing; and it is more beneficial to cover it, because the area is soft, and it is very susceptible to human hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	 And if you don't press it, there is no opening or hole in the back of the foot, and turn towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves; and make as much compression on the blood as you see, then untie the ligament, and put cotton on it and apply pressure; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	 blister healings
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses are made of horns, or hairs, or glass; and ventosation is done in two ways: either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 And this cautery called ventosation, which is for wounding, is of two kinds: either it is at all fire, or with fire; and the cautery made by wounding and the evacuation of blood is performed in fourteen parts of the body, so one is entirely in the head, and the others are in the neck; and the others in the two shoulders; and the ventosations under the chin; and the ventosations of the two elbows; and the ventosations of the two knees; and the ventosations of the two ankles; and the ventosations of the feet; and the cautery does not treat blood, unless it is from small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and for this reason it should not be used at all, if as with opening a vein; and it should not be administered either by fire or without fire, in any disease that comes from congestion, until all the body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	 And if by necessity or habit it is required to apply cupping glasses, we will administer them every hour at the beginning or end of the month, and in between and at every occasion; for there are some who, when they need to apply cupping glasses, have a heavy head; and there are some who find themselves full and red in their face, and in their head, and at the neck, and darken under the eyes; and there are some who have a spot of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongues, and bleed; and there are some who think, see spots of blood and vomit and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we observe these signs, especially during winter months, we instruct to fumigate after 4 hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	 The suction of the nose helps with headaches ... that come under the eyes, and it should not be done after the evacuation of the entire body; and this cupping is in place of cranial suction, and one who is of a cold constitution should not use it, or one who has catarrh, for it does them great harm; and therefore those with cold headaches should not use it.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who frequently heal themselves become forgetful, and therefore it is necessary to place the leech a little lower out of fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	 The ventosation in the neck is located in the sinus of the head and basilica, and for this reason it is beneficial for straining the throat, and for cutting the channel of the windpipe, and completely, and filling; and it must be pushed lightly, because if it holds too firmly, it can cause obstruction in the throat or in the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	 The ventosations in the ribs of the neck cause headaches, otalgia (ear pain), migraines, strangling sensation, and pain at the roots of the teeth; it is located in the sinus of the basilica; you must instruct the patient to press his hand, not to touch the artery, and not to let blood flow.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The ventosations beneath the chin are useful for diseases of the mouth and corruption of the gums, as well as similar illnesses that are within the mouth; and it is in the position of the salivary glands of the two lower lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventosations of the shoulders are useful for diseases that come from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	 The ventosations of the ribs is as valuable as three veins of the arm, for it draws blood from these large veins; instruct the lord not to poke too deep, for the muscles are naked there and know dark veins and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The plaster that is on the buttocks is beneficial for treating piles from below, and for diseases beneath, and it must be large, made of flax, because it needs to draw well; and if it is fine, it would break; and this causes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The plasters on the legs heal openly, because they draw blood from the entire body, and are beneficial for old rain sores, scrofula, bladder diseases, and reduce the flowers; they are in the region of the hips and knees, and weaken the body after long use, and bring pus into various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of putting on the cupping glass is as follows: First, you empty it and fill it promptly, then apply it quickly and evenly, do not stop doing this until you see the spot turn red and swell, and appear the color of blood; then cauterize, and place the cups again, taking care in the positioning of the body, for there are some who have cold skin or clear pores: it is necessary to make a single incision, and it is necessary to make wide cuts, and a little deep one; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is thick, it is necessary to make two incisions: the first time to refine the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, it is necessary to make a third incision; and when we want to draw blood drop by drop, we must pierce it only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 And if we want much blood, we often reward it; and if the flesh is thick, poke deeply, and let the veins be clearly seen, and to those who have thick skin and hard, and who have wide pores, you should anoint the muscles of the ventosities with sharp and dissolving oil: if it is in summer, sharp oil of violet or sweet almond oil or oil of cucumber seeds; and if it is in winter, oil of parsley, lily, camomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take amaranth oil, or balm of Gilead oil, or anise oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 And if one whom you treat has tender flesh and wide pores, no oil should be applied, but it should be washed after the ventilation with rose water, cold water, water of morello cherries, water of cucumber, water of porcelain or other similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture should rise with ashes of sage or of myrtle, and of sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 Those with large superfluities rise from old wine or sour milk or decoction of anise or camomile or others; and it is not necessary to ventilate before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and do not sleep after the ventilation, and it is necessary that he wakes up when he needs to be ventilated and when he has been ventilized.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 And let him who is sick and coleric take cold things, such as green apples and endives and lettuces to drink, and similar things; eat little, eat boiled meat, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 And he who has a cold constitution should take honey syrup and fragrant wine which is neither old nor new, eat little, eat spices and small birds and poultry; on the day when he will vomit, he should drink more than eat; it is also necessary to give some men certain amount of triacetum or musk at times before or after the vomiting, for the support of the main members; but let the hot ones be careful not to drink.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 The hollow bladders (caused by injury) are those placed on the liver, spleen, podagrie (gout), abdomen and belly, flanks and loins, because these members cannot be injured elsewhere, and it is done only to draw blood from one member to another, as we do with the nipples when they bleed; to remove the viscosity in a member, as we do with bladders placed on the abdomen or belly to reduce swelling; and to alleviate pain, when there is obstruction or stone, by attracting the obstruction or causing the stone to depart from its place; and thus it functions when placed on the liver and spleen when there is retained wind, and these bladders are administered empty for sucking only; and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with cold water, as in diseases of the pleurisy, and in this way the bladder is filled with hot liquid or liquid in which cooked herbs like comfrey have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the blister applied with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 And it should be two fingers and a half in width and depth, and it should have a small hole around the middle, as for pushing an awl, and made of bone, soft enough not to hurt the patient when placed on the member; and in the middle there should be a rod of bone or iron, to place a splint, and they should be big and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them; because the swellings of children are different from those of the elderly, and thin from thick.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 And the splint should be placed as follows on the member: take the splint of wax or thread, and place it across the hole in the plaster, so that the light is at the bottom of the plaster not to burn the patient; then place it on the member, and your fingers should be above the hole as we said before, so that when one looks, if steam comes out, you remove the plaster; and take the thread again as before, and repeat often, if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	 In the bladder, which is administered in pleurisy disease, it should not have a plug nor a stopper, and it should only be used when the bladder is full of liquid, and placed on the member alone; and this is its shape:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 Without plugs or stoppers, they should only be used in members that cannot be bladdered (such as lips and gums), and in open wounds of skin (such as the eye or nose), etc.; and the quality of its use is that when you find bladders containing clear sweet liquid without impurity, you take them; put them into a vessel with sweet clear liquid until they become accustomed to it and have no air in their bellies; then bladder and bladder again, clean the member thoroughly and apply the bladders when they are full and warm; if it is a place where a bladder can be applied, apply it, as this is very effective.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 If the shoulder is not in place, lift it upwards gently and then down again, very well, and then press it; and if the shoulders remain too close to the body, moisten a linen cloth with cold water, and place it, until the swelling subsides; and if the swelling multiplies, place vitriol powder or similar things on it until it subsides; or you put half-peeled beans on the shoulder and leave them until they harden to the shoulder, it will then be stopped; and if you have more need for this, take other swellings.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 And if the swellings do not want to take, rub the shoulder with fresh blood, or you insert a needle until the swelling comes out and then place it, and as soon as they feel the blood, they harden; and when you see that they are dripping, sprinkle some powder of aloe and silk or charcoal on them, they will then stop.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 Learn, dear child, that the foolish man should turn away from this chapter, for he will never see any of the ancient books, nor read a letter in them; and for this reason, science is foreign to our land, because I have never found anyone good at it; and I do not know anything about it, except through the knowledge of ancient books which I have studied so much that I have dealt with the subject, and by experience, and by the practice of my life; and I have described in this chapter what is contained therein, and have summarized it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, as I have done in these two chapters mentioned earlier.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, let us say the prologue of this book, the sums of speech and the chapters where the wise put their understanding, and dwell on the truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 I say that when fracture or dislocation or twisting or sprain comes to anyone, it is necessary that you take care of the patient on both sides, unless something stops you, such as weakness of the body, old age, or children; or if the time is not very hot or too cold; and avoid cold meats, namely raw flesh, eyes of fish and meat, do not drink wine, eat no fatty meats, do not fill yourself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt about pus-filled heat, or spreading of matter in the member; if the patient returns to his first primary governance as he has used it.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that make thickenings, or he should have viscosity, such as cooked oats in water, and meat pies, and pork, and veal, and beef, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For this nourishment helps the bones to heal more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 And know that broken bones in the elderly and debilitated cannot be well regained or mended according to their nature due to the weakness of the limbs, nor those that are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but there is no need for care, set it on the broken bone the large tendons which hold and join the limb together, as forcefully as it was before; and do not bind it completely with its covering, and therefore feed it with large foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that breaks (injuries) are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the neck is other than the break of the foot, or leg; and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways of breaking.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	There is a break that heals quickly, and another that lengthens, like the quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with an open wound, or just a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 And have your tool and equipment ready for restoration in the appropriate manner, according to what memory comes into its place; and it is known that a bone break occurs when the joint is twisted, and opened widely through dislocation, and struck with the hand; and when there is no tortuosity nor touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no break; but it may have tortuosity, or fissure, or small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You must not move it with your hand, but put on the following medicines and then hold it gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 And know that the breaks which go to the joints, and are the two parts disjoined, you must now put them in equal alignment, so that abscesses heal quickly; and if abscesses grow hot, let him leave it for a day until the abscesses calm down; then make it equal to the bone which you can easily and wisely move; and know that the restoration of it is easier than the restoration where there are pieces; then bind it as needed afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 If there are fractures in the bone, separating it into two parts, whether it is a hand or foot, or a small member, or tendons, or one tendon and the hand; then arrange the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken limb are disjoined, you align all the pieces to their proper places with every tool at your disposal, and ensure through your work that no injury or pain comes to the patient; then properly join the two bones according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not good; straighten it carefully, and do not strain it too much, nor force it as those who make abscesses or contractions in the member through their work do, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 And when the limbs are set in place, you should punish the patient so that he does not move them, neither while awake nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way; and keep a close watch to ensure that the limb is secure and feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 For if it feels no pain, it is not set in place, and you must put it in the proper position so that it feels no pain; and beware that it should be properly aligned, for twisting may come when it is restored, and the quality of a broken limb depends on this.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members are various in smallness and in largeness and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 For there are small members such as arms and fingers: you should wrap them in thin linen cloth; and for large ones such as thighs and legs: you should wrap with a broad, hard string, because the large strings embrace the entire large member evenly, and keep it equal on all sides, so that there is no swelling; then wind three or four turns around the limb lightly, and hold one part of the string with your hand, then go above the break and tighten slightly, less than the break, then move away a bit from the break; and soften the string little by little, until you take a large portion of healthy tissue, then take another string, and turn it around the broken limb in the opposite direction; then return to the part below the break, and tighten moderately, not too strongly or too loosely, as we have said in the first instruction above; then put between the strings cotton wool or linen until they are all equal, then tie them all together and then place well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 And if there is a boil or abscess, place on it a calming substance for the abscess that is hot, and also remove the boil, leaving it in this state for several days; then hold over your steels (i.e., metal instruments), and they should be about half the size of a thick cane, or of a rod used to make splints, or of palm branches, and they should be shaped as follows:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 But the steel that one places on the fracture should be slightly larger and wider than the others; and it should also be as long as is necessary for the member, whether small or large; then hold over your steels in the same way as you did with the first fracture, then tie a cord above it so that it follows the same pattern; make it tighter at first, but gradually less tight; and the cord should not be too thick or too thin, and should be of flax; for if the cord is too thick, like I have seen in the work of fools who make their ropes from twisted flax, and that is a great error, because the fracture will not heal evenly if it is too subtle, and it should never have less than two fingers' width of space between each steel.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is impaled by the points of the splinters after setting a fracture in healthy bones, put linen or canvas padding under them so that they do not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with breaking and the ligaments are torn, I will tell the cure after this.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to set a splint for all broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 For when the limbs are large, no need to apply hot irons for less than five or seven days, according to your certainty of the abscess healing; and here is the ancient method for restoring fracture, dislocation, and twisting: it is that you take flour kept near the mill walls, and mix it with plenty of egg, and apply this mixture, not too thick nor too thin, and let it dry, and this is the common method for the plaster restoring a fracture in various positions, especially for women and small children, as it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way of making a plaster to heal fractures, dislocations and twists: take alum, radish juice, sulfur, asafetida and Arabic gum, mix .x. parts; add mastic and aloes, .v. parts; eight parts of camphor; then make powder, and mix it with egg yolk; if the patient's constitution is hot, use this plaster, for it has a good composition, and quickly heals broken bones, and benefits many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	 Another plaster method for twisting: take mugwort and wormwood, 10 parts; myrrh and aloes, 9 parts; sagebrush 6 parts; Armenian bole 10 parts, grind well, and mix with vinegar or plenty of egg, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Another way of dislocation treatment for joints and bones displaced from their places, relieving the pain that occurs, and trimming with bone cutters and breaking: take new linen, wet it in warm water and oil, and place it on the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 This plaster does not restore [the limb], but it is good for relieving abscess heat and bone pain properly.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way of plaster to restore broken bones: take dried fig leaves and ground up earth-parsley, mix them together and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	 Another way of plaster for the setting of broken bones and promoting wound healing.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	 Take root of vismalve, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of beans, each a part; grind them and mix with wine, and if the member is scalded, mix with moist coriander water or vinegar, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another method of emplastrum (medication) stronger than the first, when an abscess hard comes to the restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 Take roots of mallow, linseed, balm, medick, and burnet, and flowers of violets and camomile, altogether one part; grind, and cook with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book not to put anything on a broken limb for restoration except wax made from beeswax and oil, and nothing else, and he states that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen says that something dry and slightly warm, such as myrrh, aloes, incense, and similar things, should be put on a broken limb for restoration, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to treat wounds and pain is: take crushed mugwort and hops, or feathers of birds, and mallow, and equal parts, grind them together, and make a poultice with the mixture.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then let it heal a little after that, and make sure the patient feels no pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; do not let it heal for many days. If pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hurry, and let it heal, and remove the emplastrum immediately; and take a light cloth, and sea sponge wet, and dip in water, and cleanse the place, until the itching ceases, and the pain is alleviated; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, moistened with water or rose oil, and tie over a nut, as long as you are sure of abscess heat; and let the inflammation of the member rest, and the pain be removed, then continue the subtle cure, and a little emplastrum, and not to strain it too much as before; and make it subtle until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see that the abscess has healed and turned red, swollen, and painful, and you need plaster and linen, start it again as you did initially equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	 And if no swelling comes to the limb from what we have said, do not dislocate it unless after three or four or five or seven days; and sometimes leave it twenty days, as one sees, until the fracture heals and the joint approaches the flesh again; then hold it more tightly than before, and fatten its meat, as I said before; and if you see the joint drying out too much, know that nourishment cannot enter therein; therefore give hot moist heat to it every time you dislocate it, and this should be done daily and slightly loosen the bandage; by this means cut off the swelling from the limb, and correct immediately what the foolish doctor does, who keeps the limb twisted: it is harmful, and it is a dangerous procedure, and I see no other remedy than to rest and work correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	In various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	 Many types of fractures exist, and they have various shapes; for there are some fractures caused by sword impact, breaking the entire bone from its shaft which is beneath the bone, as happens in a cleave or split; and because of this, this type of fracture is called "cleaving" or "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	or if the sword strikes the bone from above and penetrates through, it is called this type of breakage "absolute"; and the wound caused by these two types of breaks can be either large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a deep bruise or cut, or arrow wound, or falling on a stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if the wound is deep enough to reach the membrane underneath the bone, or it is on top of the bone and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	 And if the wound is re-opened in the bone as thin as a hair, and the fissure is small, it is called this type of fracture "capillary"; and if the wound is made by hitting with a stone or falling, or by something similar, causing the bone piece to enter below; and the joints are pointed like blacksmiths when they make over the kettles; the pieces of metal go inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	 And this happens more to those who have a moist bone in the head, such as a child's head; and it happens in all these ways of fracture when small bones are dislocated, like teeth; and I will speak about it further.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all the ways of breaks by pulling on them, and the examination by probing, and the corruption of the flesh that is upon it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hairy appearance is known by those who, when the bone is exposed and rubbed on top, causes the break to open black.
