En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, be aware of the patient's symptoms; if you see any bad symptoms such as vomiting blood, loss of consciousness, swelling, paralysis, high fever, hairs emerging and reddening, and other signs in various conditions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any doubtful symptoms, and you hope for salvation, start the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the frostbite comes to you for the first time, in winter, it is necessary to remove the bone before the 14th day of the month that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if this is the case, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue beneath the bone is not corrupted, and the events that we have mentioned occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	 If the bone fracture reaches to the membrane that covers the brain, you must cut the affected area as follows: take hold of the child's head and expose the bone in all ways possible, and over the wound's figure as much as possible, and if blood or pus comes out while exposing the bone, or abscesses form, help with what is needed; fill the cavity with damp cloths soaked in rose oil, let the wound rest until the abscesses are calmed, and be sure that there is no more bleeding; then begin to remove the bone, and this is done according to two ways of work: one way is to make a straight cut before, and it forms a shape.
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And put another, larger incision next to the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is to have various incisions, some narrow and others wide, pointed and made with iron tools; work carefully so as not to pierce the bone.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is dislocated and hard, you should perforate it around [the area], so that you can administer splints with wedges, not penetrating more than the bone near the tip, and above the point there should be a margin or circle that prevents the tip from passing beyond the bone; and you should have several of them, so that each one comes to the appropriate place on the bone's thickness, so that you have splints for all [the parts]; and this is the shape of the four types of splints:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for perforating around the broken bone is that you place one splint on the bone, then turn your hand until you feel that the bone has been perforated; then move the splint elsewhere a little afterwards, and do this all around, then cut the space in the bone between the fractures as subtly and lightly as possible, and as delicately as we have said, so that you draw the bone to your hand, or any of the tools you have like pliers or tweezers; and be careful not to touch the brain or spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	 And when you have pierced the bone and treated it, it is necessary that you reset the protrusion which remains of the bone to any other similar instrument resembling an incisor, but it must be thinner and more subtle than the other incisors; and if small bones or scales remain stuck, do not leave them, gently remove them with instruments; then treat the wound with ointments and bandages as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of work is that which the Gauls say, who are very wise; and it is praised much, and these are its words.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you must uncover a part of the bone where the fracture moves open, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place beneath it this lenticular incisure (as shown in its form):
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	 Do not cut through only one side, and make the incision in two parts, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike gently with a small hammer from above to break the bone all around, and be careful of the fabric underneath; if it is adhered to the bone, remove it gently because you can injure the bone senselessly without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not penetrate through to the cloth and the bone is cut only from above, and there are small pieces, then after that roughness, remove the scales with a sharp rasp, using different amounts according to each place, in order to bring about the most suitable smoothing, according to the work and the figure of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If the king shaves with great razors, and afterwards with finer ones, and never ceases to do so until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair cuts and subtle breaks, it is necessary that you apply the remedy according to his guidance; this is not something that can be answered by him who has put his study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	 If the wound is open, you should take a linen cloth of the appropriate size for the wound, wet it in rose oil and place it over the wound; then take another cloth doubled over once or twice, wet it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth; do this as lightly as possible so as not to burden the wound, then administer more linen through the other side but do not strain it any more than it covers the wound only; leave it like this for a day or two until the abscess subsides, then remove it and administer medicines such as marshmallow root, oatmeal, incense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; make a powder from these things and apply it to the wound and immediately administer unquestionable medicines without bitterness; ensure that the wound is always clean, do not leave any dressing or pus on it, as when pus accumulates on the cloth of the brain, it will rot and cause great harm to the patient; for when something bitter is placed on the wound, it will cause pain through the other side.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, take care that no bad accident befalls the patient as we have said, it is doubtful with uncertainty.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if blackness does not come violently except by the medicine that has been placed upon it, its virtue being such, then you should take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil and mix them with beeswax; then anoint it thusly. Then cure it in the manner of cures as is necessary, until it heals.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the neck are broken above, or one alone, because there are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous and does not break, but only bends or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	 If one of the two parts is broken, you should chew your little finger or thumb nail, and put the same break inside your index finger, and in the pocket outwardly, until the nail grows again according to its natural figure; and do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the breakage is in the upper part of the nose, and the finger cannot reach the place, then you must place it equal to the top of a ruler, a little larger.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	 If the break is of one of the two parts, do as before, and hasten to restore it on the first day if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth, when the abscess has calmed down, then put linen strips at the base of the nail where the break is.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you apply a bandage on the other side, if there is only one fracture; and let the cloths be as thick as they fill the wound of the neck.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	 And they said to any restorer that one must soften the tendons with butter, and move each one every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	 It does not seem good to me, but it must be softened with an egg yolk mixture and flour powder; then let the tendon rest until the bone is hard and the cartilages are hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes feathers of geese are placed instead of stitches, and if one piece of cloth surrounds them, and the breakage is held, the patient is blown upon with breath; do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	If abscesses come to the wound while you are working on it, place either alum or cotton soaked in rose oil, or a pinch of turmeric.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if there is no abscess present, apply a plaster from flour and incense powder mixed with egg yolk, then put light packs on it and do not bind too tightly; and if the break in the nail is small, and it breaks into many small pieces, extract them using appropriate tools, then seal the wound, and treat it with char, and solder, as plasters and ointments suitable for this purpose; and if there is no wound within the nail, cure the tendons and put willow sticks on it until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	On the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is dislocated beneath and there is no wound outside, and only the break is outside but not broken in two, if one knows it slightly, it indicates that it is corbeled inside.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the break is on the right side of the jaw, insert your index finger into the patient's mouth; and if the break is on the left jaw, place your index finger of the right hand inside, and gently push the break inward and align it with the other hand from outside.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the jaw is separated into two parts (i.e., diastasis), you must provide two parts of extension until it is equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement of the teeth or rupture, hold them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place a broken cork over the mandible, and put on one double cloth; and place on the cloth a large and well-made splint, or an equal piece of leather, long and wide according to the mandible, and attach it where you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and encourage them to eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	If you see that the figure changes, release it on the third day and then reset to its original state; place a plaster over it with flour from the mill mixed with egg or meal of wheat; after removing the cork; and put a light linen plaster over the plaster when it dries, and if the disposition of the patient does not change, leave it until it is healed; many times it is healed in four weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess arises, bring what we have said before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, observe that no piece of the bone has been removed; if it is necessary to remove the broken part, do so with subtle tools suitable for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, stretch it by fire as needed.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Once all the pieces have been removed and none are left, stitch the wound if it is wide, and place one plaster suitable for this purpose on it to promote healing until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps break often in front of the shoulder, and the fracture is in four ways: it is fractured and dislocated in two, and there are fragments, and it is the easiest to restore; or there is a fracture with an open wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is when there is a fracture with an open wound, that you have two assistants: one holds the shoulder where the forceps are broken; and the other stretches the neck towards the affected area; then align the fracture to your hands so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither deformation nor dislocation.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if more extension is needed, put a round cushion of cloth or linen under the shoulder of the patient, and make it as large as necessary; stretch and tie the bandage, and hold the cushion in place with your hand, so that you align the break as required.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	If you cannot draw out the head of the splint from below because it is lodged in place, then have the patient lie on his side, and put a small pillow under the shoulder. Then push the shoulder downwards, so that the bone of the splint is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then direct the break to your fingers and if you find debris, then it should be cut open. If the pieces cannot join due to any reason, hit it at one of the incisions that you have made; but place this instrument under the splint, to prevent it from flying out.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	 And it seems like a spoon, and is not hollow, and should be as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; and there should be two cuts, as you see, and one should be wide, and the other narrow, as the opening of the wound when you have treated the bones; and when you are sure of the abscess cold, if it is shallow, or you doubt about the abscess cold, use linen and bandages, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	If the abscess becomes cold, moisten one linen cloth in rose oil, asafetida, and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	 The setting of the bone when it has wounds and cuts, is that you put a plaster made from milled powder and egg yolk on the bone, and place light splints on top, and place a spear under the affected area if needed; then take a very wide bandage, a palm wide, then cover the splints with two layers of linen, and apply the plaster; then take a thin stick, 3 feet long and wide, and wrap it around that wide bandage so that the ends of the bandage hang; and place the stick over the broken bone, and turn the bandage around the neck, and under the affected side, and under the healthy side; and tighten each part separately, and when you see that the broken bone aligns correctly, and you clearly see that the stick does not move above the broken bone, then keep it in place every day, and when the linen loosens, tighten it; and make the patient lie on his back, and put a small pillow under the affected area to lift the shoulder up; this will help the collarbone to heal along with the alignment of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it except for bad accidents occur, until 20 days; then start applying the plaster again if needed, and tighten it and leave it in place until it is healed; and it is healed in the most cases within 28 days, and in less time with some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	 It happens that the shoulder breaks or is dislocated and cannot be felt except through touch; if it appears according to the shape of the break, you must reset it according to its natural form in all possible ways; then put powder from the mill on it with a lot of egg and light wads, and place a double cloth over it; then place a wide and subtle awl, slightly larger than the shoulder, and if there are any hollows in the shoulder under the awl, use linen wads to fill them so that the awl fits evenly; and then tighten it all with a great firm bandage, so that the awl does not move from its place, and watch it every day; and whenever it swells, tighten it and adjust the awl if it is out of its place, and have the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder will be restored in 20 or 25 days. And when this number is reached, release it, for it is not bone that easily moves out of place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	If a part of the bone protrudes before and not under the skin, lift it up, extract it, and do what we have said to treat an abscess at the shoulder joint with warm cautery.
de la brisure dou pis	of the break in the thigh
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	 The broken bone is sometimes fractured in the middle, but it happens rarely; however, it often breaks at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	 And when it is fractured at the end, it tilts downward, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of nourishment, and soon, and by chance vomits blood, and the openings in the broken bone are exposed, and he feels no relief.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back, and you place one cushion between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and assemble the ribs of the two sides to your hands, and carefully align it in all ways, until the figure of the bone is as required; then you place splints and padding over the thin part of the broken bone, or a lighter staff, and wrap it in one bandage, and hold it on the broken bone so that it does not move; and turn the bandage around to the back, and tighten it gradually, and check every hour whether the bandage has softened, if it has softened, you tighten it; and if it is necessary to unwrap, due to corrosion or pruritus that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hurry, and undo it, remove the padding, and direct those who have come in matters of care; then rewrap the padding, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the broken ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the fracture of ribs occurs only in large ones after the back, and at the chest within, and they do not bend easily except because they are slippery; and this is well known at the investigation of the joints.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 And the resetting is to align the fracture as needed.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	 Then place the splint and tie it with a stick if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the rib fracture is displaced downwards, the patient feels very great pain and swelling, as in pleurisy, because the bone points to the skin; and it swells at the ends, and immediately vomits a large amount of blood, which is a serious illness, and the ancients have applied many devices.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And to those who say that it is necessary to administer foods which swell the belly, for pushing out the rupture.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	But we do not do so, that hot abscesses come, if they have not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have come, he is cured.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And it was said to someone that vents (tubes) should be placed on the head, for draining pus, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the tubes will attract excess fluid to the head due to its weak position.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And it was said to someone that the head should be covered with damp linen in hot oil, and tents (something like small bags or pouches) should be placed between the ribs to make the wound even around it, then let it be treated with a cure for pleurisy, meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear from the broken rib, and there is doubt in the patient, it is necessary to break through the side of the broken rib, and it is necessary to place an instrument under it for support; then you should cut open the bone, pull it gently, and sew up the two edges of the wound if it is large, and treat it with splints until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if an abscess swells up, place soft, oiled linen cloths on it and on the affected area; and treat the affected area as needed for the abscess, and keep the patient lying down on the side where it is, until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	of the break in the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Never does a fracture occur in the bones of the neck or spine, and it rarely bends.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	 And if this happens to someone and you want to know if it will heal or not, take notice if their hands become softened, swollen and dead, and they cannot move or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel anything.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	 Know that it is fatal in many positions, and if they do not speak or feel when you tighten and prick them, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient should be healed if treatment is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	 And if a similar thing happens in the spine of the back, and you want to know whether it is healthy or not, take care if the feet are paralyzed, and if the accident that has occurred is in hands, and the back shows sudden movement without will; and when it is put on its stomach, it still moves without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	 And when it is placed on its back and it wants to lie down, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	 Know that it is deadly; do not treat it.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to him, it is a lighter matter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is to apply hot poultice if there is an abscess, then put rose oil or egg yolk oil on the spine until it is soothed; then put one of the comforting and drying plasters on top and tie it with a thread, and command the patient to rest; do not let him sleep on the part where he feels pain until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If any bone dislocates, it should be covered with oil; extract the bone, then sew together two lips of the wound if it is large, with a stitch; then treat the wound with soothing balm until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken (which is called "head of the cow"), put your hand on it from the left side, and align it with the other hand to your power, then put the plaster and the linen cloth on top, if you need them; then bind it, and if there is any bone dislocated, make it straight, extract it, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the bone of the pelvis
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	If the pelvic bone is fractured, there will be a slight decrease in the head, and it will elongate and bend towards the opening, causing pain at the site, and swelling of what is fractured.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you stretch out your hand above, as long as you are over the fracture; and feel which part is fractured and the shape of it; and if the fracture is only at the head, then make the fracture equal, as natural.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long or it bends towards the inside, then make the patient lie on his stomach, until the restoration of that fracture is prepared for you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it even, place the splint upon it, then place a rod or stick on top and hold the fracture so that it does not move; and immerse the limb beneath the ribs until the fracture is healed.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	If an abscess has come to the surface, do not touch it until the abscess has subsided, and place what we have said before on top of it; then return to treatment, hold it as necessary, if there is no bad incident; and this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is that which is between the chest and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it should be restored according to one of the two ways; of which one is that you take a splint made of thicker material, in this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two shoulders with two ropes, and bind them from above, and place the patient on one seat; then you cast the broken arm upon the splint, until it reaches the elbow, and have a protrusion of splint in the middle, then bind it above to any heavy object or the assistants extend it downward; then the healer equalizes the fracture with his hands together, until the fracture returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another manner is that you hold the patient on their bed, and hold their hand to their neck, then command two servants that one holds the place above the break with his hands, and the other holds below at every joint, and extend each to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	 If you see that the extraction is too strong, hold the ligament below the break, and above the break, and extend each of the assistants to their respective places.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 If the break is near the head of the shoulder, you must put the ligament in the middle below the joint, and the other towards the costal arch, below the break; and if the break is towards the costal arch, you must slightly put the ligament without effort, so that the break is equal to its place, and to the costal arch; then equalize the break as necessary, and hold it, unless an abscess develops.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	If an abscess swells up, do not tighten it for more than 7 days, but put soft linen and rose oil on it to calm the abscess; then you can tighten it. The method of tightening is that you place the clamp on the break, then assemble the arm on the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or chest; then pull the cloth tight on the shoulder and the arm so that the arm is in its socket, unless something prevents it, or the bone is not moving.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use stitches; place a larger and stronger splint above the break, with one inch of space between each stitch, and make sure each stitch is large enough to pass over the break from both sides; then hold the splint in place as I have said at the beginning of the chapter concerning the break, more tightly and lessen in width.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	 And if you see the swelling and constriction, as we have said, when you restore a broken limb, and you doubt whether it is an abscess heating up, leave it to heal for seven days, as we have said; then examine it every three days to see that no pus or redness appears at the site, or that the blood does not come to the limb because it is too constricted.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	 If you notice that the swelling and constriction disappear within three days after your initial examination, as we have said, then...
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	 And if no such incidents occur, do not remove the bandage for less than three days or more, and let the patient lie on his back with his hands on his stomach; put a clean linen sock over the shoulder and observe every hour of the day or night that the appearance of the broken limb does not change or the bandages become soft; if the injury heals by the power of medicine, give the patient the meat as we have previously mentioned, in such a way that the meat is initially tender; and when it begins to regain its strength, let it grow.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	 And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be reset in 40 days; and then you must release it and administer baths and ointments to guide its healing.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	 And if the dislocation is crooked and swollen, it may take a month or two to release it.
de la brisure du bras	of the break of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm consists of two bones, which are called the "ulna" and the "radius," the former being small and forming the forearm's outer side, while the latter is larger and lies beneath it near the elbow; by chance, only the large ulna breaks, or both break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	 When small fractures are broken, the restoration is easy, and healing quick; but when large ones are broken, healing is difficult, and more painful than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	 If only the small fracture is broken, it should be gently extended and made level.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	 And if it is the large fracture that is broken, it should be pulled more forcefully; and stretch it on the splint, and hold the handle of the hand higher than the others, and the small one lower than the others, and cross the patient over himself, and the splint in front of him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any pain; then extend the attendants arms to the part below his hand or elbow, and one other attendant above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	 And then make the mirrors equal, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the breakage of bones, place each one back in its place, and if none is displaced that points to the center, and you cannot restore it to its place, then saw off and remove the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the breaking open, I spoke of it in the singular chapter, take care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	 If pusples (abscesses) arise at the beginning of healing, apply a plaster made of rose oil and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft; and stick the plaster gently over it until the abscesses are soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	 Then remove the wax, and apply a poultice of milled powder with plenty of egg, then place the sticks; let the stick for breaking be stronger than the others and a little larger; and know that it should have six sticks or more in various positions: whether the break is in one bone or two; and tighten more above the break than elsewhere, and always less when pulling, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the drapes over the break be soft and moist, not hard nor rough; and let the threads, with which it is tightened, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	 And watch the member and the ligament afterwards for some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	 And if any bad accidents happen to the member, such as itching that happens on the member, you must anoint the member with warm water until the itching is soothed; and do not let the member rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	 Then continue with the binding, and if the ligaments are weakened and the bones dislocated, or similar things, address accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the swelling cannot come to the member because it is too narrow, you must soften it a little, and let it be for some days until the swelling subsides, and then set it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	 And if none of these things mentioned above happen to the patient, do not remove the bindings for twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	 Furthermore, you should place his hands at his neck, and ensure his neck is even, and watch for movement or dislocation; he should sleep on his back. Know that this fracture will be restored in thirty to fifty days, or perhaps twenty days, according to the compositions and complexions of the remedies.
de la brisure de la main	Of the break of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	The fracture of the hand occurs frequently in the back of the hand and the fingers, but only a few breaks occur at the wrist.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or fractured, the patient must cross their arms and sit upright in a straight position; then place their hand on an extended cloth, and extend the broken bones, aligning them with mirrors until they are well set; apply the plaster and bandages, unless abscesses appear, then put a splint according to the size of the break; and swaddle it in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	If the fracture is around the palm near the abdomen, make a splint from cloths and instruct the patient to wrap it around their broken hand; then tie it with a long cloth, and let the splint be as wide as the palm of the hand, and tighten it as necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is on the outer side (of the bone), it is necessary that you place a splint above and another below in the sole, so that the hand remains open and straight, then tie it all around the hand, and compress the ligament between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the break occurs in any of the fingers, equal it as necessary; and hold it with the sole and, if you see, place a small straight splint to lift the break and keep it from moving; and if the break is in the other fingers, such as the index or one of the others, equalize it, and tie it with the healthy finger that follows; or bind them all together in one holding, for movement is harmful, or place a splint on it, as with a finger; and take care in the restoration and the placement of the abscess, and treat those who come, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the thigh are often broken, and one can see this when it twists forward and backward; and restoration is such that a ligament is tied above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patients lie on their faces, then each of the ministers extends his ligament equally to its equal part; and this is when the break is between the bones.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	 And if the fracture is near the root of the leg, it may be one of the ligaments towards the heel, and the other ligaments below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	 And if it is near the knee, then the ligament is below the knee and the extension is distal; then place the hands on the bone so that it is equal to its two sides, as naturally, and then set the splint and the bandage, unless an abscess comes in.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess that is hot, let it cool down first, then return to your work and treatment; the ligation is done in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	 You must wrap above the fracture with a bandage doubled in two or three layers, and remove any excess, then turn the leg so that the heels come to the root of the thigh, and thread the string through the thigh and the leg, below the knee, and bring the head of the string above; then turn the leg and the bandage upward, then place splints on the fracture and a splint on the bone of the leg; then use soft fabric for seven inches between the leg and the thigh to set the strapping evenly, then begin to bind three or four turns around the fracture; and as you go higher above the fracture, let it be less constricted. Then take the two strings that you have threaded through the leg and thigh, and tie three splints that are above, then return to below the head of the string, until you reach the foot; and bind so that it does not move from its place, then leave it in this state, unless an abscess or swelling or any such thing comes.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If there is a fracture, loosen it and direct the pieces as we have said many times; and if there are bone fragments that protrude, they must be removed if possible; and if not, the fracture should be opened and drained; and treat it as we have said until it heals.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the leg is broken in such a way that stakes are set, as in the shoulder or arm; however, during the restoration process, the patient does not feel any pain.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the leg is restored in about a day, or slightly less or slightly more, according to the various complexions [of people].
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the street of genoails
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	 Know that in the groin region, there occurs little breakage, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	 If it breaks, it is not a simple crack, but rather a tear or wound that causes pain at every place and great pain.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that one equalizes what is uneven in its ends, as much as it can be assembled; then place the splint, and put a round stick if needed, and tighten it as required, then inspect all the dispositions that we have said about other breaks, such as abscesses and others; apply to each accident what is necessary for it, until it heals.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	 Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is properly called "ham" and the others are called "shin"; and it breaks in the same way as it does in the arm, and for this reason the restoration is similar to that of the arm, and the work is the same. And if the two bones are broken together, the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the slender bone (tibia) is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	 If the large bone is broken, it causes great pain and can be seen; it turns under.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	 Therefore, provide extension, make it even, and align the limbs equally; however, if the fracture is ugly, and there are many pieces, the extension should be smaller and lighter; and adjust accordingly to your judgment.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your task, take two splints of wood that will support the leg from both sides and be as long as the leg from the knee down; then wrap them with two bands, one above and one below, and bind it in the middle so that the leg cannot tilt to the right or left, and this is good; nor should anyone apply a splint of wood longer than the length of the leg, and place it under the leg as a restraint for movement, and properly make it at the fracture where there is pain; and move the leg every day to see if there is an abscess or any other accident; treat it until it heals.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the bone fractures in the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there comes no fracture, but sometimes the bones of the foot do have a fracture and nothing else except for a slight crack in various positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	If there is a fracture in the bones of the foot and you see the bones overlapping each other, place the patient's foot on the ground as if he were walking, then place your own foot over his, where the raised bones are, press hard until they return to their place; put splints and bandages on, and put a small flat table under the patient's foot with two hollow holes, then tighten it around the foot evenly; when you have wrapped cloths around, and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when four or five days have passed, undo the linen, for you will find the bones equal, whether fractured or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the two [shoulders] are broken, restore them as we have said about the arms of the hand; then place a splint on the broken shoulder according to its length and let it be slightly larger, then place beneath the arm that tabula I mentioned, and hold it in position; and if there are 2 or more [broken], break each one separately, place a splint on each according to its size, wrapped in one linen cloth, and hold the tabula beneath the arm; and let it be so that the tabula is placed above the belly of the arm, facing towards the back, so it covers well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things I have said about other fractures, after what we have said; and treat each accident as necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone in the thumb
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the bone of a woman's nature (pelvis) is broken, make her lie with her back enlarged, then incline her to the part of the small of her back and hold her from behind; then fill the cavity of the patient with cotton and stuff it as full as possible; then move the woman and lift her lower back little by little, and when the cotton comes to the entrance of the pelvis, let the bone come out with the stuffing; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, replace it, and do this for seven days or longer: the fracture will be healed, and if you see, take a bladder of barley, tie one end of a cord to it, and push the whole bladder into the pelvis; then blow forcefully into the cord until the bladder swells inside: the pelvis will return the fracture; then fill it with cotton and leave it for some days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 And when the bone of the thumb of man is broken, either of woman, restore it as we have said in the hing joint; and such breaks are not hidden from him who puts his study and his craft to it and intends my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	 For the fractures indicate various positions for the right way of restoration; understand it then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In a spear (shaft), when it is broken, take an owl's throat and insert the shaft; then wrap cloth around it, and leave it for 3 or more days, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of breakage with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	For the one who has a breakage with a wound (especially if it is large such as the bones of the leg or shoulder), he must be bandaged now, just as the bandages that we have said testify.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healed, then treat it with vinegar (if you have nothing else), then immediately proceed to set the breakage in that same hour or the following day, unless an abscess has come forth.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess has come forth, then wait until the ninth day, allowing it to heal before touching or working on it again, for doing so would cause a bad outcome.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone breaks and appears above the knee joint, you must put it back gently into its place with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	If the fractured bone does not align to put it back into place, you must use this tool which is made of iron, about 7 or 8 inches long, and the width according to the size of the wound; and for this reason, it is necessary for the mirror that he grips 3 or 4, depending on what is needed in each bone-setting; and it should be round and a bit large, so that it does not bend during your work on the limb, and pointed at the tip, and large from the middle forward, as follows:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	 And it is called "palm joint," for which the crooked head of the bone should be placed on top of the obvious bone, and push it once, until it comes back and becomes even one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 And if the fracture is subtle and the instrument cannot well take the bone, then you must cut the head of the bone, so that the instrument has power over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone, as we have said, strike it with an appropriate instrument, either chisel or saw, to your ability; then remove what remains in the bone with sharpness and small shavings.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 Afterwards, immerse the linen in black, sticky vinegar and apply it cleanly if it is warm; do not put any scorched cloth or oil on the wound which may bring rot and corruption; then administer oil when you have restored the bone, leave the wound open, cover it with a layer according to the size of the wound, taking care that the wound is not constricted with the breakage; and many times have the foolish surgeon done this, and brought death or corruption upon the patient, and beware that the bindings are more gentle and softer than other injuries.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a bad incident may come, as we have said, and you feel pain at the place, do not put stitches on it; but instead wrap around it, in place of stitches, hard cloths and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	 And if the next day or two after the application of the poultice you see it swell at the wound, remove what you put on it and apply healing ointments for wounds such as healing balm and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you dislocate the limb twice a day, in the morning and at evening, as long as it is healed and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limbs should be set in such a way that the bone slips slightly downwards easily.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	If it passes many days and the bone cannot heal but slides back, as there are small pieces of bone, so it is necessary that you try to keep pressure on the wound and remove all the loose fragments that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 And if a fistula appears at the place or any other kind of corruption, you must treat it according to what is said in the chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 And if the bone is broken and open above the limb, such as the thigh or shoulder bones, and similar in other large members, do not draw it out because many times death comes, but leave it until it can be drawn out; perhaps it will come out by itself after 20 or 30 days, then cure the wound if you can; otherwise, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The arriving bruises on the sore
