Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	There are often many times after the healing of the fracture, especially when it is near the joint, and it is unpleasant to see the appearance of the limb member; and by chance, the limbs cannot perform their natural duties.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore, be careful: administer medicines such as aloes, incense, myrrh, and sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others, such that you take any of these things or all together, and crush them with a sharp wine or with plenty of egg white or with oil; then put it on the wound in poultices, and bind it well, and do not unbind it for many days; and then break it open, and start another one, as long as the nodules are removed; or you bind above a piece of plank well made; because the properties of plank are that they remove all swellings from the limbs. And if the nodulation has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cut off the top, and make the excess apparent; or you shave it at any razor, as long as it is removed, and cure it until it heals.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The member which is weak after treatment.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored and remains after treatment, the members are weak and delicate in many cases: one reason being that it was tied too tightly, and was not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many sutures, and the nourishment could not reach the member; or because of excessive drainage; or because of excessive movement, not at the right time; or because there is little blood in the body, which makes them weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body thin, until the blood multiplies in him; and administer baths, and give him joy and comfort; then put wax on the member, so that the wax attracts great nourishment to it, and drain it often with cold water, until the nourishment goes to the member; and return it to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	twisted limb after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When a limb is twisted after restoration, and the bone is broken open, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nevertheless do not lose hope; do not believe the foolish who say that one must break the limb anew, and many foolish people have done this in our land; and this treatment is blamed, and great harm comes from it, and perhaps death; nevertheless, if the swelling and torment are fresh, it is necessary that they be treated with hot, soft water or softening herbs such as vismalve leaves, radishes, mellilot root, and similar things; and you make a soothing poultice, such as dyaquilon; or you take figs with fat, grind them with wheat bran, and similar medicines that reduce swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 And sometimes the dislocation is removed by rubbing continuously and for a long time with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 Bring movement to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is swollen and hardened, just like stone, and it requires iron to be removed, then it must be covered up to the bone, incised carefully with a subtle instrument; and cloth and bandage should be applied in treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs to someone, it must now be returned without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 For if one delays, the joint swells, and by chance if it is set in place again; therefore, it should not be moved when it is swollen: many times it causes pus and other pain; however, when this happens, let the patient purge himself, then leave him, until the abscesses have all subsided; then immerse the limb in hot water and oil, then gently straighten it, and cure each member as the cure comes to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters concerning shoulder dislocations down to feet.
des mandibules	of jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It rarely happens that jawbones should be dislocated in two ways: either they are slightly displaced from their place and softened somewhat; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards the chin, and saliva flows from the mouth which it cannot hold, nor can it close its mouth, wrapping its tongue around with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When small dislocations occur, they return through various positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 If it is whole and complete, then you must quickly reset it, and do not linger; and in such a way that the attendant holds the patient's head, and pushes one of his hands into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is from two parts; and the other hand should be open, to put them equal; and command the patient to soften, his jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And he shall bring it back into its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it [the dislocation] is reduced with force, most certainly it will recur, especially if they are the two jawbones together, anoint them with hot water and oil, until they are gently reset; never force to reduce it, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 And when they are reset equally, the patient's mouth should be closed with soft linen cloth soaked in a ointment made of rose oil and wax, then it should be tied gently with several ligatures; and the patient should sleep on his back, and his head should be kept between two cushions so that it does not move neither to the right nor to the left, nor it forces itself to move, but takes light food, until the pains are removed, and the jaws are healed; then eat lightly whatever he wishes, and do not force himself to open the mouth for eating or drinking, until the jaw is well healed and healthy.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	If the two mandibles cannot be set right within an hour and are not converted to their places, fever and accustomed sores come, and possibly rupture of the belly, and possibly the vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a disaster; and many times he who experiences it dies within eight days.
de la forcelle	Of the noose
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The noose cannot dislocate from within its continuity and the ribs, and it is occasionally dislocated outwardly, and one can feel it.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 Then the patient lies down on his back and extends his arms; then presses the shoulder with your hand in a certain way, and it will return; then apply the splint and bind it, and hold it in place; the head that is turned towards the side cannot dislocate again; if it does, reset it to its place as we have said; then apply the splint and bind it, and keep it in place, and command the patient to rest until he is healed; and similarly, the shoulder of the back can be reset when it is displaced from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	The dislocation of the shoulder.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 Know that the shoulder is not dislocated except in three ways: one way is when it dislocates at the socket below; the second is at the hip part; and by chance, it dislocates above the hip part, but this rarely happens; it does not dislocate behind the shoulder or inside the nerves; and it often dislocates below towards the socket, especially in those with little flesh, for it returns quickly to its place; in those with enough flesh, it jumps back quickly, but returns slowly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes happens to some men, percussion or breaking, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they believe that it is dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you should verify [the dislocation], as long as you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 And it is known that the dislocations, when they are below towards the socket, distinguish between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a clear difference between them; and at the head of the shoulder, there will be a hollow, and beneath the shoulder at the toucher the head of the shoulder, just like an eye; and the patient cannot bring his hand back to its place, nor can he move in any way; and similarly, if it is dislocated above, it is not hidden, for you can clearly see it at the toucher; and this type of dislocation is not easily corrected when it is new, unless the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	The method is that the minister raises the patient's hand up, then puts his thumbs under the dislocated joint and pushes it upward to its place; the minister then lowers the hand and places it down, it will come back quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 And if the shoulder does not come back as we have said in our hands after several days, it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water; and bring a soothing and calming poultice, such as a decotion of elderflower, fennel and lentil in water, and apply this; then lay the patient on his back, and place a piece of equal linen under the affected shoulder, neither too soft nor too hard, then place the hand on the linen, and lift the head of the shoulder gently, and pull the arm of the patient; another attendant holds the head of the patient still so that it does not move downward; this shoulder will return immediately, and if you see it dislocate again in this manner: it is necessary to have a person present who is larger than the patient; and be straight toward his side, and push his shoulder under the patient's affected shoulder, and lift the affected shoulder upwards, so that the patient hangs from it; another attendant pulls the patient's arm downward towards his stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too lightweight, he can carry no heavy thing with him, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 Also, one may reset it in another way: one thrusts the long needle into the ground so that the head is as round as a pea and not too thick nor thin; then it shall be placed under the patient but with soft fabric over it, and the patient should be standing upright; then extend the hand away from the other side forming a "V"; the jointure will return to its place quickly. If it does not want to return due to all these things that we have said, perform this cure: take a thick needle of about two fingers in length and four inches wide, which has a round tip for inserting fully into the socket, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lay the rod over the patient's shoulder, so that it does not prick the patient; then place it under the shoulder of the patient; extend your arm along the rod; hold the limb on the rod and the arm at the wrist, then place the arm on one side of a small bench with enough space for the hands to be placed underneath; extend the other hand downward, and let the body hang from the other side; the joint will re-align itself in the process.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	When the joint is in place, regardless of how it may be, you must place a spherical pad of wool under the shoulder; then apply the plaster made with powder from the mill, incense, and egg white over the entire shoulder and around it; then press down on the shoulder underneath while turning the string around the plaster, and tie the hand to its neck, keeping the hands in place.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it must be applied ointment, until the limb is comforted, for it will heal sooner; and afterwards apply more after 5 or 7 days, and move it; and if it is firm and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 And if the joint is out of place due to moisture or for some other reason, then you must administer cauteries at three places, as it is stated in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	If you do all this, and it dislocates again after 7 days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot raise its arm above, then know that the nerve at the base of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be set in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the thighs and hips, or backside, is made by a push and extension of hands, and other force is applied to it; and care should be taken until it heals.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And after healing comes stiffness in the member and delayed movement; the patient should use baths many times, until the stiffness subsides and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation cost
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated at points, and it returns to its points; and if it has dislocated from all sides, both in front and behind, and dislocation cannot be restored because it can clearly be seen and felt; and it dislocates according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 And when you join the broken bone with the healthy one, you should see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 For the joint is swollen and the arm cannot bend nor touch the shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary to reset the dislocation as soon as an abscess comes, for if an abscess comes, it would be painful to reset; and perhaps it cannot be completely set again, especially when it is at the back; it is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and perhaps death may come.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is such, when it can be returned in this manner, that you extend your hand to its two hands; and its arms should be spread out, and the hands of the patient according to the cut thereabout, both above and below, and push the joint to its sockets together, or to the root of its palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, then it returns when the patient doubles their hand over their hand, and pushes the root of the displaced palm back into place.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 If it does not return to its place, apply strong extension; and it is that two people extend the arm and burn it with two torches so that it does not move at the extension; then turn the arm from each side, and when you have wound a double large cloth around it; and when the mirror has joined the joint to his hand, anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint firmly until it returns; and when it is in place, put dry plaster over it with egg, hold it strongly and let the arm hang on the patient's neck for several days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	If the joint is closed in its place, untie the bandage and leave it; if you see that the joint does not bind well, renew the plaster and the bandage, and leave it like that for some days until it is firmly set; then untie it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	 And if there is pain after the repositioning of the joint and it becomes motionless, bathe and rub it well, and press until it is soothed; or you may put a sheep's wool soaked in warm, moistened dung on the jointure, then leave it for a day and a night, then remove it, and let it enter the water again; and when it seeps, rub the jointure gently, then replace the wool, and then enter it into the water again; and do this two or three times until it is healed; and if you see, put warm, moistened hay on top of it, and press it; it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand is displaced and the repositioning is easy, more so than other joints; it should be returned to its place as quickly as possible, in the hour itself when it is dislocated, unless the ligaments are inflamed or there is an abscess hot.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	 Then the repositioning of the hand is done by placing the sick hand on a table, and extending the fingers of the attendant's hand, and aligning them with it, so that his palm is above the appearance of the jointure, and he pushes until it returns to its original position; it is necessary for you to observe if it is well in place; then have the patient place the back of his hand on a table for stretching and repositioning.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	 And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, place the patient's hand on a table, and the attendant places his hand above the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 If it returns now, it is good; if not, hold down the pressure on poultices for abscess easing and let the pain resume.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	 If the patient cannot endure it and you are unable to put it in place after some days, the dislocated joint remains; this does not harm the patient as long as the hand is injured and cannot be straightened completely: thus know that the nerves have been severed or the arteries; there is no other means of help except by applying a cautery to ease the case, and in case it may be of any use.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is healed, place it in a splint as we have said, then strap and leave for 5 days, then release and leave it in this state.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it cannot be moved well and there is no swelling, moist with warm water and rub until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	 Whenever the fingers of the hand are dislocated on either side, or on the back of the palm or stomach, then stretch the dislocation back into place as much as possible, then hold the finger's head and turn it towards the part where it is disjointed; and leave it for two days, and then straighten it on that day; and bind it as we have said, and loosen it from day to day, and make it move, and relocate it; and do this often, until it becomes narrow, and similarly do, if it is dislocated on the stomach side of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it heals; and similarly do, when it is dislocated from another place.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	The dislocation of the vertebrae in the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the vertebra of the back or neck is dislocated, or if there are multiple dislocations, there is no remedy, for death quickly approaches the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	 And the signs are such that the hernias jump spontaneously, cannot be held, and many times the member becomes softened, or the two knees or the two arms or the back; when it becomes silent at four parts, it is called "gilbositez"; treatment is that you look to see if the gilbositez has come from childhood: if not, there is no cure nor healing from then on.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	 And those that fall or are caused by blows or similar things, the old methods of cures used to speak in great words, but there is not much benefit; I have abridged it according to my understanding, and I have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	 I say that in the hernia that comes before, there is neither tool nor healthiness; and similarly, the one that comes directly between the two sides, which cannot be cured except by him who comes from behind, as I have said; and it is that the patient should lie on his back in an even position, and have a restraint under him, so he does not bleed; then insert the iron [cautery] into the first opening in the ground, and the other at the feet, and tie a rope above the patient's hips, and another at the thighs, and knees, and ankles; and two ministers know the ropes, one at the head and the others at the feet, among the two cauteries; and they should be well closed, the cauteries as we have said, and the ministers place their hands on the spine until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	 And if the dislocation does not return through this cure, take a board that is three spans long and curved beneath, and position the patient on their side, and push the head of the board under the opening, then put the middle of the board on the spine; place your hands on the other end of the board, and press firmly until it returns to its place; and if you see it does not, turn the screw that twists by hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	 And take two needles of one arm's length and place them on either side of the patient's head, leaving a palm's width between each needle; have a screw in each needle, or the lever turning, and the needles should be firmly fixed in the ground so they do not move; place a turning needle between the two needles, like linked chains, and have in the turning needles two short needles of one palm's length to turn the screw; then lie the cord that is tied on the needles to the screw near the head, and the other cord to the foot at the other screw, and each of the attendants turns their screw according to the cord, and the master adjusts the spine as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	 And when it [the shoulder] is aligned, put on it a plaster of drying agent with plenty of egg, then press and afterwards stick a probe of three feet in length, which penetrates the site of the dislocation and the healthy part of the spine, then tie a cord, as we have said, and use the patient gently with subtle heating, until it is healed; and if anything comes at the end of the healing process, administer softening and calming medicines, along with the probe mentioned earlier; and sometimes a piece of wood is administered, and sometimes it appears in the rear spondyle of the back, and it is thought to be dislocation; and this is the bone that opens, for which one should have no presumption: perhaps death will come.
des dislocations de la hainche	of the dislocations of the shoulder
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	It is known that the shoulder and shoulder blade joints come from dislocations only, and they are not dislocated in the same way as other joints; the shoulder joint is dislocated in four parts: inside and outside, front and back, more inside than out, less so in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 And the knowledge of its dislocation within is that when the diseased leg is joined with the healthy one, it is longer, and the diseased knee is more open than the healthy one; and the diseased person cannot bend his knee in fire; and it is the joint which is dislocated due to abscess swelling that is hot, because the hips of the thigh come there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one who is about to die, is that this event is contrary to those mentioned earlier.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of one whose leg is straight according to the accomplishment, are that it does not double the knee due to pain, and if you want to make him walk, he cannot do so beforehand, and retains his urine, and swells the ankle, and when he walks, he steps on the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of one whose backside event occurs are that he cannot stretch his knee nor bend it, and the leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the hip of the thigh is in its place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedies for this kind of dislocation are as follows: first, you should examine whether the dislocation is old and if it stays in place according to its position, there should be no treatment; and there should be no presumption that it can heal on its own.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	For the fresh dislocation, which is of the four kinds of dislocation, you should hurry and turn the joint, pushing it inward and outward, moving it to the right and left; by chance if it returns, there will be no need for further treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	 And if it does not return in this manner, then you must apply forceful pressure, and hold the leg firmly between two hands, or tie it with a rope above the knee; and another person extends his hand in such a way that he pushes his hands under the knees, then tightens a strong rope on the thigh; and another grasps the top of the rope; and all extend upward and downward at once, until the patient is lifted from the ground once, and hangs suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to four similar cases, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	 If the shoulder is not in place, it is necessary to treat its appearance. When the dislocation is at the front, you should remind the patient to lie on his healthy side, then tie a cord around the root of the thigh and the joint that is beneath the angle, then pull the cord upward towards the angle and towards the forceps; then take another helper with their arms, grasp the large joint of the sick thigh, and extend it forward in a wide manner; it will return to its place now; and this method of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	 And if you cannot lock it in the manner that we have said, then you should bind the two feet of the patient tightly with a strong rope above both ankles and both knees, and the sick leg should be extended two finger-widths more than the other; then it should be hung up by the head on a pole, and suspended from the ground by two long arms; then command one helper to grasp the head of the thigh, and another helper hanging with the patient, who will grab the thigh in a manner, because the joints return now quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	 And when the dislocation is out (of place), the patient lies down, as we have said in the one who has dislocated his shoulder; then straighten the ligament on the affected leg properly, and also on the thigh; next insert rods, one at the head and one at the feet; then push the rod between the knees towards the patient; and place moist cloths around it to prevent the patient from bleeding; then extend each assistant away from him, and the mirror put his hand equal to the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	 If it comes back (to its proper position), that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	 If it does not (return to its proper position), put on a bed and press as we have said in the dislocated shoulder, and make the patient lie on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it should be extended immediately as I have said, and place the mirror on the bad angle, then press with the other hand, and stretch it downward towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 If the dislocation is outward, it should not be extended downward nor raised above ground; instead, the patient should be as if the hip were dislocated to the outward position, as we have said in the lying-on-the-two-hips method; and he should be on his side, and the limb extended as we have said before, and it should be pressed against the joint on the table; and he will be ready when the patient extends his legs and they are equal; then align the thighs, and place the pillow, and bind with a bandage so that the hip does not move; and rest for three or four days, then unbind, and place the pillow again; and if you see that they are equal, bind as before, and leave it for three days; then unbind, and let him walk well, until the limbs are comforted.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: inside and outward, behind; and do not dislocate it forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend their leg at the knee, and if it does not bend at the knee, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all such cases is that you make the patient sit straight, extend their leg if they can, place your back on its face, and place their foot on your feet; then take their thigh with your hands, pull apart between your hands, then bend the two sides of the thigh outwardly forming an "M"; another attendant extends their foot until it returns to its place, and the signs are that it bends the leg lightly at the knee; apply the plaster, straighten the leg to the knee, and bind them tightly for three or four days, then release it; do not let the patient walk beforehand, until the limbs are comforted.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	 And if the limb is not straight, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of clubfoot, until it heals.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the ankle dislocation
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes crushed, and sometimes completely dislocated from within and outwards.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	 And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and one tries to push it back to the dislocated part: the reduction should be gentle, and it should be gently extended with hands when only pushed out.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	 And when it is fully dislocated, you must have the patient sit upright, and hold him by the leg, above the ankle; then pull the foot towards yourself with your right hand, then to the left twice, then lift it up, and push the foot forcefully upwards; do this twice, as we have said, while pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, repeat the process, because it will return; and if it cannot return, lay the patient on his back on the ground, and firmly fix the passeil between his knees, and wrap cloths around, so as not to hurt the patient; then hold the leg by the calf, and another person holds the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will quickly return.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	 And when it is at the point [of dislocation], put a plaster and poultice on it, press it to form, and tie the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves that are above the ankle, so that the bindings are not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the bindings soften, tighten them; then untie it on the third or fourth day, and advise the patient to walk for four days; and if he goes before that time limit, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess swells there, you must soothe it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, they must be stretched out gently without strain, and it is an easy thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the dislocation is in any notch of the back of the foot, you must make the patient sit on a flat surface or table upright, put your foot above the joints opening, then press your foot firmly until it returns to its place; and when it is even and there is no gap, put a two-fingered board under the foot's heel, then tighten it, and leave it for three days, then untie it; and let him rest until he recovers.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	 When a wound comes with dislocation and it is to be restored, often the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in treatment unless you are wise in the art and have used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate, merciful, and slow, nor hasty; first apply calming medicaments to the abscess, and leave the patient in the hand of God if you see no hope of health; but when there is hope, reset the limb to its place as soon as the abscess subsides; and when the limb is in place, administer calming medicaments to the abscess again, and treat the wound, as necessary, with warm ointments; and if there is a fracture along with dislocation and small bones are displaced, break them and do what has been said for simple diseases; and beware of entering into fear, as I have said, for it harms you according to your Creator, and for the safety of your skill and body.
Amen	 Amen (Pronounced as in English)
